# 道德真经指归老子指归

**The *Zhǐguī* of the *Dàodé Zhēn Jīng*
Title: *The Zhǐguī of the Dàodé Zhēn Jīng*
Also titled *The Zhǐguī of the Lǎozǐ*.
Composed by Yán Zhūn (style name Jūn Píng) of the Han dynasty.
Original text comprised thirteen volumes; the first six are now lost.
Base text source: *Zhèngtǒng Dàozàng*, *Dòngshén* section, *Yùjué* category.
Collation references:
1. *Chéngdū Yílán Táng Cóngshū* edition (hereafter *Yílán* text);
2. *Mìcè Huìhán* edition (hereafter *Mìcè* text).
Supplemented from Wáng Déyǒu’s *pointed and annotated* edition of *The Zhǐguī of the Lǎozǐ* (published by Zhōnghuá Shūjù, 1994).

**The *Zhǐguī of the Dàodé Zhēn Jīng*
Composed by Yán Zhūn of Shǔ Commandery (style name Jūn Píng), with annotations by Gǔshénzǐ.**

In ancient times, when Lǎozǐ composed the *Dàodé Jīng*,
His original intent was to trace the form and refine the *qi*,
Ascending to the divine and luminous.
Where life and nature first emerge,
Where emotions and intentions take root,
Where advance and retreat, response and influence unfold,
Where breath and movement bend and stretch—
He aligned these with Heaven and Earth,
Examined them through Yin and Yang,
Unfolding transformations from beginning to end,
Where all things find their place.
He penetrated the subtle and reached the profound,
To perceive the natural order.

Condensing the essentials and extending the categories,
He recorded two *jīng* scrolls,
Articulating Heaven’s intent,
Revealing Earth’s heart,
To govern the realm,
To nurture all things and the people.

Each chapter has its inner and outer layers,
Unchangeable in their order.
When a chapter is complete, its structure is whole—
Like a root and its stem.
The words follow one another in sequence,
Neither above nor below can be altered.
Widely spreading the Dao and virtue,
Like the dragon and the *lín* [unicorn].

Add a single character, and it becomes a wart or excrescence;
Subtract a single word, and it becomes a scar or ulcer.
Thus, "great" precedes "small"—this is the highest principle.
To record the Dao and expound virtue is called a *jīng*.

At its beginning, "upper virtue does not virtue,"
For transformation arises from the Dao,
Yet the Dao does not claim dominion over it.
Hence, he entrusted it to the "one of old times."

「In ancient times, the *One* [得一] was attained—
Its movement stems from *contrary action* [反行],
And only those of high innate nature can truly perceive it,
Thus it was entrusted to the *superior sage* [上士].

The *superior sage* has lofty and keen insight,
Deep and distant understanding alone,
Disdaining the world and holding all things lightly,
He bears only the *Dao* [道] on his shoulders,
Thus it was entrusted to *Dao generating the One* [道生一].

*Dao generating the One* is supreme emptiness without name,
Receiving the primal *hun* [混冥],
Refining the clear and the turbid,
Molding the *Great Harmony* [太和],
Thus it was entrusted to *the utmost softness under heaven* [天下至柔].

*The utmost softness under heaven* is subtle and formless,
Piercing the firm and penetrating the distant,
Conquering all without defeat,
Thus it was entrusted to *possessing named wealth and goods* [身有名货].

To possess named wealth and goods brings strength and power,
Yet strength and power invite calamity,
Thus it was entrusted to *Great Completion* [大成].

*Great Completion* is like emptiness,
Void of named wealth and goods,
All things harmonize and communicate,
Thus it was entrusted to *the world with the Dao* [天下有道].

*The world with the Dao* rests with the sovereign,
The sovereign without desire sees all things preserved,
Thus it was entrusted to *not stepping outside the door* [不出户].

By not stepping outside the door, one knows the life and fate of all the people,
Receiving them in harmony and resting in ease,
Thus it was entrusted to *daily learning brings increase* [为学日益].

To daily learn brings increase,
Yet words arise and affairs multiply, exhausting the spirit and harming the people,
Thus it was entrusted to *the Sage has no mind* [圣人无心].

*The Sage has no mind*,
Uniting with the people’s *shen* [神],
Cautiously preserving their life and fate,
Returning to the primal *zhen* [素真],
Thus it was entrusted to *born and enter death* [出生入死].

To be born and enter death,
Every movement depletes the spirit,
Discarding the non-returning for the returning,
Cannot long endure,
Thus it was entrusted to *Dao generating life* [道生之].

*Dao generating life* is through emptiness and nothingness,
Where all things are preserved,
Silent and still, unmoving,
Nothing it refuses,
Thus it was entrusted to *the world has a beginning* [天下有始].

*The world has a beginning*,
Non-action as its core,
To penetrate all affairs without confusion,
To know all without limitation,
Thus it was entrusted to *let me have knowledge* [使我有知].

*Let me have knowledge*,
The *Dao* refined and practiced,
Fear of losing the natural order,
Bringing ruin to descendants,
Thus it was entrusted to *good foundation* [善建].

To *good foundation* with virtue,
Connecting with all things,
Blessing future generations,
Flowing to the ends and flourishing,
Thus it was entrusted to *the virtuous sage* [含德之士].

*The virtuous sage*,
Embodied in the *Dao* and walking in the *shen* [神],
Like an infant—innocent and unknowing,
Thus it was entrusted to *the knowing do not speak* [知者不言].

*The knowing do not speak*,
The *yīnyáng* [阴阳] subtly transform,
Internally rectifying the self,
The self extending to the family,
The family extending to the people,
Thus it was entrusted to *govern the realm* [政治国].

To govern with rectitude,
Without decrees yet all things move,
Foreign lands and customs come without command,
Thus it was entrusted to *square yet not cutting* [方而不割].

*Square yet not cutting*,
All things preserved whole,
Conquering all without defeat,
The *Dao* of heaven shines great,
Thus it was entrusted to *rule the great realm* [治大国].

The ruler of the great realm must not act greatly nor do greatly,
Great actions and deeds bring great disorder and turmoil—then ruin,
Thus it was entrusted to *the great realm* [大国].

*The great realm* is naturally advantageous,
All under heaven desire it,
Calmness below brings return,
Frenzy above breeds war,
Thus it was entrusted to *harmonizing with things* [道物].

*Harmonizing with things* is firm and steady,
Those who attain it are enlightened,
Those who treasure it are preserved,
Those who guard it are profound,
Thus it was entrusted to *non-action* [为无为].

*Non-action* makes the transformations effortless,
Things flourish unseen—yet all things grow,
Thus it was entrusted to *its ease in holding* [其安易持].

Before signs appear, plans are easy,
Holding to it like the simple,
No visible affairs yet all calamities vanish,
All blessings come naturally,
Thus it was entrusted to *the ancient Way* [古之为道].

*The ancient Way* is to keep the people simple,
Cutting off extremes and eradicating roots,
Sealing the gates of knowledge,
Thus it was entrusted to *the rivers and seas* [江海].

*The rivers and seas* know no limits,
Empty and tranquil, dwelling in the lowly,
To receive all the valleys,
Thus it was entrusted to *the world calls me greatly unlike* [天下谓我大似不肖].

*The unlike* Way uniquely aligns with heaven’s heart,
Raising armies and moving the people,
Invincible and undefeated,
Thus it was entrusted to *the use of arms* [用兵].

*The use of arms* follows heaven’s patterns and responds to human needs,
Arising from its root,
Not from my own will,
Thus it was entrusted to *my words are easily known* [吾言易知].

*My words are easily known*,
Without wisdom or understanding,
Without speech or affairs,
Letting things act naturally,
Thus it was entrusted to *knowing the unknown* [知不知].

*Knowing the unknown*,
Discarding the mind and discarding intent,
Born yet like death,
Preserved yet like loss,
Abandoning my clever artifices,
To pursue calamity and misfortune,
Thus it was entrusted to *the people do not fear authority* [民不畏威].

*The people do not fear authority*,
Lightly shunning prohibitions and easily entering,
Trapped in officialdom,
Their great fate severed from heaven,
Thus it was entrusted to *daring to be bold* [勇於敢].

*Daring to be bold* stirs the heart of the thief,
Taking life and losing principle,
The law decays and the state perishes,
Thus it was entrusted to *the people do not fear death* [民不畏死].

*The people do not fear death*,
Desires unchecked and prohibitions ignored,
Following their emotions and inclinations,
To reach poverty and destitution,
Thus it was entrusted to *the people’s hunger* [人之饥也].

*The people’s hunger*,
Heavy taxes and excessive levies,
Greed for plunder, ceaseless scheming,
Harshness and rigidity, seizing life,
Thus it was entrusted to *the people’s life* [人之生也].

*The people’s life*,
Soft and weak yet fearing reverence,
Harmonious and pure, subtle and refined,
Keen and bright with daily learning,
In death, they become harsh and rigid,
Thus it was entrusted to *the Way of heaven* [天之道].

*The Way of heaven* diminishes fullness and supplements emptiness,
Nurtures the soft and compliant,
Overthrows the firm and shatters the rigid,
Thus it was entrusted to *nothing under heaven is softer and weaker than water* [天下莫柔弱於水].

*Water*, though soft and weak,
Can overcome the firm and strong,
Resting in the subtle and delighting in the small,
In peril it finds its ease,
Thus it was entrusted to *the small realm* [小国].

*The small realm*’s sovereign,
Form is empty, power is weak,
Life depends on neighbors,
Thus it was entrusted to *the trustworthy* [信者].

*The trustworthy* are aided by all the people,
And preserved by ministers and generals,
Heavened by earth and sky,
And assisted by the *Dao* and virtue.

Zhuangzi said: In the past, when Laozi composed the *Jīng* [经],
He recorded the principles of transformation,
*Dao* and *virtue* as its mother,
The *Jīng* listed first,
Heaven and earth as its model.

The *upper jīng* corresponds to heaven,
The *lower jīng* corresponds to earth.
Eight chapters for the *yin* Way,
Nine chapters for the *yang* Way,
Using *yin* to follow *yang*,
Thus seventy-two chapters.
Beginning with *yang* to follow *yin*,
Thus divided into upper and lower.
With eight chapters for the five *xíng* [行],
Thus the upper *jīng* has forty chapters before it begins anew.»

「With four *xíng* [行] and eight chapters,
Thus the lower *jīng* [经] has thirty-two chapters before it concludes.

The *yang* Way is odd, the *yin* Way even,
Hence the upper *jīng* precedes and the lower *jīng* follows;
The *yang* Way is vast, the *yin* Way confined,
Thus the upper *jīng* contains many, the lower few;
The *yang* Way moves leftward, the *yin* Way rightward,
So the upper *jīng* follows in succession, the lower reverses its course.

In reverse and succession, they intermingle as one form,
In profound obscurity, they merge into chaos—
The *Dao* [道] as their central sovereign,
With repeated seals and verifications to reveal their threads.

The lower *jīng* is the door,
The upper *jīng* is the frame.

The wise discern its efficacy in the *jīng*,
And thus grasp the numbers of heaven and earth,
The cycles of *yin* and *yang*,
The pairing of husband and wife,
The bond of parent and child,
The rites of lord and subject—
And all things unfold in harmony.

**Yán Jūn Píng** [严君平] of the **Zhuāng** [庄] clan spoke of the *jīng* titles—
He was a native of **Chéngdū** [成都], in the commandery of **Shǔ** [蜀],
And since his surname was **Zhuāng** [庄], he was thus called **Zhuāngzi** [庄子].

During the **Chānghé** [章和] era of the **Eastern Hàn** [东汉],
**Bān Gōng** [班固] composed the *Hànshū* [汉书],
But to avoid the taboo of Emperor **Míng** [明], he altered it to **Yán** [严];
Both **Zhuāng** [庄] and **Yán** [严] were common terms in ancient and modern times.

**Jūn Píng** [君平] was born in the middle of the **Western Hàn** [西汉],
When **Wáng Mǎng** [王莽] usurped the throne,
He withdrew into seclusion during the **Yǒnghé** [炀和] era,
Truly a **zhēnrén** [真人] of the ancient age.

The *Moral Dao/Way True Classic* [道德真经] *Zhǐguī* [指归] consists of volumes one to six (missing),
The *Moral Dao/Way True Classic* [道德真经] *Zhǐguī* [指归] volume seven.

The **Commandery of Shǔ** [蜀郡] **Yán Zūn** [严遵], styled **Jūn Píng** [君平], compiled the *Gǔshénzǐ Zhù* [谷神子注].

The **uppermost virtue/power** [上德] does not **virtue/power** [德] (Chapter#1).
The **uppermost virtue/power** [上德] does not **virtue/power** [德], its virtue/power is **mysterious** [玄]—
Thus, it is said that he who has virtue/power, **virtues/powers** [德] without return.
The **lowest virtue/power** [下德] does not lose virtue/power—
Its virtue/power is **heard** [可闻], thus it is said that he who lacks virtue/power, **virtues/powers** [德] **recur upon the self** [反身].

The **uppermost virtue/power** [上德] acts without **doing** [为], and all things follow **naturally** [自然]—
Yet nothing is left undone; its merit is **ascribed to Heaven** [归天].
The **lowest virtue/power** [下德] **does** [为]—
Yet it exhausts the **spirit** [精神], and its merit is **ascribed to man** [归人].

The **uppermost benevolence** [上仁] **does** [为]—
Yet it adds **favor and love** [恩爱], and does not **do** [为] as the **ascetic** [禅] of the **sages and worthies** [圣贤].
The **uppermost righteousness** [上义] **does** [为]—
Yet it establishes **order and limits** [有民] for the people, and its merit is **transmitted to descendants** [传子孙].
The **uppermost propriety** [上礼] **does** [为]—
Yet it **regulates rites and origins** [节事原], and none respond—
It loses the **people’s hearts** [人心], then **rolls up one’s sleeves** [攘臂] and **enforces harmony and kinship** [强和亲].
Thus, when the **Dao/Way** is lost, the **virtue/power** [德] **name** [名] first **sprouts** [萌].
When **virtue/power** [德] is lost, **benevolence and love** [仁爱] **take form** [形].
When **benevolence and love** [仁] is lost, **righteous distinctions** [义分] and **roles** [职] become **clear** [明].
When **righteousness** [义] is lost, **rites and jade offerings** [礼玉帛] are **performed** [行].
**Rites** [礼], then, are the **thin outer layer of loyalty and trust** [忠信之薄], the **waning of virtue/power** [衰亡].
They are the **beginning of disorder** [乱之首], the **gateway to craft and deceit** [巧伪门].
**Preassigned roles** [前职] are **thus established** [预设然], yet **the Dao/Way’s refinement** [道之华化] has not yet **been heard** [闻].
They mark the **beginning of foolishness** [愚之始] and the **source of confusion** [惑乱根].
Thus, the **true man** [大丈夫] **embodies the Dao/Way** [体道] and **rules** [君].
He **dwells in its substance** [处其厚], **embracing loyalty and trust** [含忠信].
He does not **dwell in its thinness** [不处其薄], **abandoning rites** [去礼].
He **dwells in its reality** [处其实], **moving with cause** [动有因].
He does not **dwell in its refinement** [不处其华], **avoiding premature knowledge** [不前识].
He **seeks this and discards that** [去彼取此], **pursuing it within himself** [求诸身].

**Zhǐguī** [指归]:
The **origin** [所由] of **Heaven and Earth** [天地],
The **source** [所以] of **all things** [物类],
The **Dao/Way** [道] is its **root** [元],
**Virtue/power** [德] is its **beginning** [始],
**Divine clarity** [神明] is its **core** [宗],
**Great Harmony** [太和] is its **ancestor** [祖].
The **Dao/Way** [道] has **depth and subtlety** [深微],
**Virtue/power** [德] has **thickness and thinness** [厚薄],
**Divine essence** [神] has **purity and turbidity** [清浊],
**Harmony** [和] has **height and depth** [高下].
The **pure** [清] is **Heaven** [天], the **turbid** [浊] is **Earth** [地],
The **yang** [阳] is **male** [男], the **yin** [阴] is **female** [女].
**Humans and things** [人物] **borrow and receive** [禀假],
Their **endowment** [受] has **much and little** [多少],
Their **nature** [性] has **refinement and coarseness** [精粗],
Their **fate** [命] has **length and brevity** [长短],
Their **emotions** [情] have **beauty and ugliness** [美恶],
Their **intentions** [意] have **greatness and smallness** [大小].
Some become **petty men** [小人], some become **gentlemen** [君子].
Their **transformations** [变化] and **separations** [分离]
Are **divided and judged** [剖判] by **categories** [数等].
Thus there are **Dao/Way men** [道人], **virtue/power men** [德人],
**benevolent men** [仁人], **righteous men** [义人], **proper men** [礼人].

Dare I ask: What **actions** [行] does that **man** [彼人] take
To earn such **contradictory titles** [殊谬名号] as these?
**Zhuāngzi** [庄子] said:
**Emptiness and non-action** [虚无无为], **opening and guiding** [开导] all things—
This is called the **Dao/Way man** [道人].
**Purity and stillness** [清静], **responding naturally** [因应], yet **doing nothing** [无所不为]—
This is called the **virtue/power man** [德人].
**Compassionate love for all things** [兼爱], **boundless universal application** [博施无穷]—
This is called the **benevolent man** [仁人].
**Rightly ordering names and realities** [理名正实], **acting with righteousness** [处事之义]—
This is called the **righteous man** [义人].
**Modesty and withdrawal** [谦退], **words and yielding** [辞让], **respectfully guarding harmony** [敬以守和]—
This is called the **proper man** [礼人].

All these five types **seek longevity** [乐长生], **revere virtue/power’s thickness** [尊厚德], **value high renown** [贵高名].
Each **cautiously refines his emotions and nature** [慎其情性],
**Trusts in his innate wisdom** [任其聪明],
**Follows his strengths** [道其所长],
**Returns to his ease** [归其所安].
Their **endeavors and pursuits** [趋务] **diverge and scatter** [舛驰],
Some **negate** [否], some **affirm** [然],
Their **transformations** [变化] **differ in direction** [殊方],
Their **titles** [建号] **vary endlessly** [万差].

**Virtue/power** [德] has **superiority and inferiority** [优劣],
The **world** [世] has **prosperity and decline** [盛衰],
**Winds and customs** [风离] **drift apart** [俗异],
**People’s fates** [民命] **differ** [不同].
Thus some **drift boundless and profound** [溟涬玄寥] yet **lack a name** [无名],
Some **are enveloped in dim radiance** [蒙澒芒芒] yet are called **Emperor** [皇],
Some **are vast and overflowing** [汪然漭泛] yet are called **Sovereign** [帝],
Some **are bright and expansive** [廓然昭昭] yet are called **King** [王],
Some **are distant yet harmoniously varied** [远通参差] yet are called **Lord** [伯].
These are the **names that can be spoken** [可言者].

Yet **Lord** [伯] is not **Lord** [伯],
**King** [王] is not **King** [王],
**Sovereign** [帝] is not **Sovereign** [帝],
**Emperor** [皇] is not **Emperor** [皇],
**Being** [有] is not **Being** [有],
**Non-being** [无] is not **Non-being** [无].
**Ten thousand transformations** [千变], **ten thousand variations** [万化]—
They cannot be **reckoned** [为计].
**Layer upon layer, countless eons** [重累亿万]—
They cannot be **named** [为名].

How then can one **clarify** [明] this?
When **one changes a dynasty and becomes King** [易姓而王], **sealing at Tàishān** [封於太山], **ascending at Liángfù** [禅於梁父]—
There are **seventy-two instances** [七十有二] of this.
Yet some **have signs and portents** [形兆] **so indistinct** [圻堮仿髴] as to be **unrecognizable** [不可识]—
They cannot be **spoken of** [称言].
Are these not cases where **nature and fate differ** [性命不同], **merits and titles do not align** [功名不齐]?
No, this is not so.

Thus, the **ruler of uppermost virtue/power** [上德之君]
**embodies the Dao/Way** [体道] and **preserves** [存],
His **divine essence** [神] **harmonizes with transformation** [与化伦],
His **virtue/power** [德] **moves the mysterious depths** [动玄冥].
He **rules the world** [天下王], yet **none witness or hear** [莫有见闻].
His **virtue/power** [德] **returns to all things** [归万物],
And all say it is **natural** [自然].
The **uppermost virtue/power** [上德] does not **virtue/power** [德]—
It **aligns with the Dao/Way** [与道同].

The **ruler of lowest virtue/power** [下德之君]
**embodies virtue/power** [体德] and **acts** [行],
His **divine essence** [神] **wanders with transformation** [与化游],
His **virtue/power** [德] **matches Heaven’s grandeur** [配皇天].
He **rules the world** [天下王], yet some **see or hear** [或见或闻],
His **virtue/power** [德] **flows to all things** [流万物],
Then **recurs upon his ruler** [复反其君].
The **lowest virtue/power** [下德] does not lose virtue/power—
It **virtues/powers** [德德] itself.

Why is this so?
The **ruler of uppermost virtue/power** [上德之君]
**receives in nature** [性受] the **Dao/Way’s subtle intricacies** [道之纤妙],
His **fate** [命] **obtains the One’s refined essence** [一之精微].
His **nature and fate** [性命] **harmonize with nature** [同於自然],
His **emotions and intentions** [情意] **embody divine clarity** [体於神明],
His **actions** [动作] **align with Great Harmony** [伦於太和],
His **taking and discarding** [取舍] **conforms to Heaven’s will** [合乎天心].
His **divine essence** [神] **thinks of nothing** [无所思],
His **will** [志] **worries about nothing** [无所虑],
His **wisdom and clarity** [聪明] are **mysteriously distant** [玄远],
His **stillness** [寂] is **emptily void** [泊空虚].
His **movements** [动] are **formless** [若无形],
His **stillness** [静] is **as yet unborn** [若未生],
His **merits** [功] are **like Heaven and Earth** [若天地],
His **deeds** [事] are **as a babe’s brother** [如婴兄].
He **abandons form** [遗形] and **hides his will** [藏志],
**Aligns with the Dao/Way** [与道相得],
**Boundless and profound** [溟涬], **enveloped in dim radiance** [蒙澒].
**None in the world know him** [天下莫知],
**He drifts beyond the four directions** [潼溶方外],
**Soaring to the utmost distance** [翱翔至远].
**Yin and yang** [阴阳] **serve as his ministers** [为使],
**Ghosts and spirits** [鬼神] **plot his counsel** [为谋].
His **body** [身] **transforms with the Dao/Way** [与道变],
**Above and below are endless** [上下无穷].
He **advances and retreats** [进退], **shifts and adjusts** [推移],
**Ever accompanying transformation** [常与化俱].

Thus, **serene and effortless** [恬淡无为],
His **virtue/power** [德] **overflows the mysterious realm** [德盈于玄域].
**Silent and profound** [玄默], **still and boundless** [寥],
His **transformation** [化] **flows to the limitless** [流於无极].
His **favor** [恩] is **incalculable** [不可量],
His **virtue/power’s thickness** [厚] is **unfathomable** [不可测].
He **encompasses all** [兼包大营],
His **benevolence reaches ten thousand lands** [泽及万国].
His **wisdom is insufficient** [知不足] to **match his transformation** [伦其化],
His **words are insufficient** [言不足] to **guide the customs** [导其俗].
**All under Heaven** [天下] **chatter and murmur** [咮咮喁喁],
Yet all **receive his transformation** [蒙其化] and **are enveloped in his harmony** [被其和].

If such a one **originates from nothing** [元无],
**He vanishes and none know who made him so** [绝而不知为之者何谁].

This is called the **uppermost virtue/power** [上德] **does nothing yet nothing is left undone** [无为而无以为].

The **ruler of lowest virtue/power** [下德之君]
**Receives in nature** [性受] the **Dao/Way’s righteous breath** [道之正气],
His **fate** [命] **obtains the One’s middle-lower essence** [一之下中].
His **nature and fate** [性命] **compare with nature** [比於自然],
His **emotions and intentions** [情意] **approach divine clarity** [几於神明],
His **actions** [动作] **nearly align with Great Harmony** [近於太和],
His **taking and discarding** [取舍] **embody utmost virtue/power** [体於至德].
He **entrusts his divine essence** [托神] to the **Great Void** [太虚],
**Hides his roots** [隐根] in the **mysterious depths** [玄冥].
His **movements** [动] **return to softness and weakness** [反柔弱],
His **stillness** [静] **returns to peace and harmony** [归和平].
He **loads the compass and measures with the square** [载规履矩],
**Gazes into the utmost purity** [镜视太清].
His **transformations** [变化] are **dim and indistinct** [惚恍],
His **responses** [因应] are **formless** [无形],
His **refinement** [希夷] is **vague and obscure** [茫昧].
He **barely has posthumous titles** [几无号谥],
**Measures the earth** [方地] **to follow Heaven** [随天],
**And transformation is his constant** [与化为常].
His **virtue/power

The **unformed virtue** shines unseen,
The world in childlike innocence,
The four seas as one,
Vast and silent, profound and still.
With the people in harmony, gazing together,
With all things in mutual regard.

At such times, the **Great Dao** remains undivided,
The **pure virtue** unsplit.
Within the six extremes, one alone exists.

His **endeavors** are in **subtraction, not addition**,
His **actions** refined, yet **unforced**.
What he does is few,
What he upholds is strict.
The people are sincere and loyal,
The age harmonious and tranquil, serene and unadorned.

Water and grass suffice as stores,
Fur garments as fine attire,
Great trees as halls,
Caves as dwellings.

The ruler stands like Heaven and Earth,
The people like grass and wood,
**Enveloped by Dao, united in virtue**,
**Serene and undemanding**,
Yin and yang in perfect accord,
All things flourishing and multiplying,
No decrees issued,
The world in peaceful submission.
Fine millet and red grasses grow spontaneously,
Sacred dragons and phoenixes dwell among them,
Sweet dew descends without ceasing,
Auspicious winds stir without pause.

Without **righteousness or benevolence**,
Within the six extremes, **harmony with Heaven’s kinship**;
Without **rites or sacrifices**,
Within the four seas, **all are kin as brothers**.

**Kin yet not harmonious**,
**Respectful yet not reverent**,
Heaven, Earth, and all things—
**Mingled in primordial unity**.

The **lower virtue** acts yet **has means**.

The **Supreme Benevolent Ruler**,
His nature pure and luminous,
Bright and far-reaching.
Mind and intent **empty and still**,
Spirit and qi **harmonious and yielding**,
Commanding Heaven and Earth without exclusion.
**Perceiving the subtle, grasping the essential**,
**Knowing the known while embracing the unknown**,
Nurturing life through virtue,
Loving the people as his children.

**Manifesting all things, responding to change**,
Echoing and shadowing in accord,
Marking Heaven’s divisions,
Clarifying Earth’s principles,
Distinguishing the proper roles of all things,
Opening the gate of **understanding past and present**.
**Creating blessings for all**, to benefit the myriad people,
**Recording the inner while overlooking the outer**,
Guiding them with **affection**,
**Accumulating thought and depth**,
To attract the distant lands.

**Laws and prohibitions** are **balanced and gentle**,
**Edicts and commands** **broad and yielding**,
**Actions and measures** **timed with the seasons**,
The world rejoices.
Thunder and lightning do not rage violently,
Winds and rains do not rise abruptly,
Grasses and trees do not wither and decay,
The people do not die young.
**Even the crawling and creeping** all find their place.
The aged and weak wander freely,
The strong till and weave,
Each has descendants to the fourth generation,
Gray-haired elders and children abound,
The ruler as parent, the people as children,
Virtue flows to the four seas,
Yet he **holds nothing**.

The **Supreme Benevolent** acts yet **has no means**.

The **Supreme Righteous Ruler**,
His nature **balanced and just**,
Emotionally **open and discerning**,
Investigating harm and benefit,
**Discerning and wise**, his heart like a **compass and square**,
His will like a **measuring rod**,
**Serene as water**, **straight as a plumb line**.
Delighting in great deeds to **establish his fame**,
Taking pleasure in **beginning blessings**,
Avoiding **precursors to calamity**.
**Wielding authority and transformation** to **govern the age**,
**Exalting benevolence and righteousness** to **oversee the people**.
Following **Heaven and Earth’s principles**,
Regulating **all things’ proper order**,
Serving parents as **revering the divine**,
Treading upon the people as **walking on deep waters**.
**Listening broadly to all nations**,
**Judging with moderation**,
**Awe-inspiring yet not tyrannical**,
**Harmonious yet not indulgent**,
**Stern yet not cruel**,
**Discerning yet not harsh**,
**Rooting in origins, determining ends**,
**Establishing posture to govern the people**.
**Advancing and retreating with the times**,
**Flexing and yielding with transformation**,
**Actions and duties shift with change**,
**Rites and customs evolve**.
**Edicts are trustworthy and clear**,
**Laws distinct yet not excessive**,
**All matters decided by ministers below**,
**Authority and power solely with the ruler**.
**The court upholds the Dao with caution**,
**Exalting virtue to expose deceit**,
**Enacting the five punishments**, marking the flesh.
**Honoring origins, valuing beginnings**,
**Adjusting according to norms**,
**Conforming to principle in severance**.
**Authority arises, power expands**,
**Awe shakes the land**,
**Setting aside self for others**,
**Benefiting the people without harshness**,
**Dismissing even the slightest offenses**,
**Exalting the finest virtues**.
**Internally benefiting the royal house**,
**Externally encompassing all things**,
**Addressing decay through transformation**,
**Preserving life and reviving the lost**,
**Supporting the weak and raising the young**,
**Benevolence renewed**,
**Land passed to heirs**,
**Descendants unbroken**.

The **Supreme Righteous** acts yet **has means**.

The **Supreme Riteful Ruler**,
His nature **harmonious yet yielding**,
His heart **detached yet desiring**,
His actions **governed by yin and yang**,
His edicts **aligned with the seasons**,
His **institutions vast and varied**,
His **nets encompassing hearts**,
**Honoring and elevating rulers and parents**,
**Humbling and diminishing ministers and children**.
**Rectifying superior and inferior**,
**Clarifying distinctions**,
**Ordering elder and younger**,
**Differentiating husband and wife**,
**Uniting human relationships**,
**Regulating friendships**.
**Returning to proper offerings and rituals**,
**Matters ranked by category**,
**Those bound by rules are praised**,
**The unrestrained are diminished**.
**Encouraging the strong and suppressing the violent**,
**Encompassing customs with moderation**,
**Guiding through the middle path**,
**Yielding to desires while restraining them**.
**Pressing emotions to curb nature**,
**Damming floods before they rise**,
**Guiding the age and customs**,
**Preventing excess**.
**Severing what others cannot**,
**Forcing what others cannot do**,
**Exhausting spirit and harming nature**,
**Burdening the people with labor and complexity**,
**Order arising from chaos**,
**Safety from danger**.
**Knowledge of past and present is thorough**,
**Pure essence fades away**,
**The Great Dao extinguished**,
**Benevolence does not flourish**,
**Heaven’s harmony disrupted**,
**The four cardinal virtues lost**,
**Thunder and lightning shattered**,
**All things wither and perish**.
When a father or son dies,
The world **remains unchanged**.
When bells and chimes resound,
Customs **do not shift**.
When **elegant melodies** play,
The winds **do not alter**.
**Modesty and withdrawal** meet **disbelief**,
**Yielding and submission** meet **indifference**.
**Offering high rank and rewards**,
The worthy **do not descend**.
**Extending arms to hold the jade scepter**,
The virtuous **do not come**.

The **Supreme Riteful** acts yet **none respond**.

Why is this so?
Though **words are abundant and appearance splendid**,
**Sincerity does not reach the heart**.

Thus, the **foundation of emperors and kings**,
**Dao is the primordial origin**.
When **Dao is lost, virtue takes its place**,
When **virtue is lost, benevolence takes its place**,
When **benevolence is lost, righteousness takes its place**,
When **righteousness is lost, rites take its place**,
When **rites are lost, chaos takes its place**.

These five stages—
**Dao governs as one body**,
Yet **each age’s ruler** has its strengths and weaknesses.

Thus, what is done is not what one truly desires,
What is sought is not what one truly obtains—
They neglect the natural way and instead pursue petty trifles.

Now, the practice of rites,
Though outwardly refined and inwardly discordant,
Though splendid in appearance yet hollow in substance,
Though elaborate in form yet decaying at its root—
When rites grow thin, loyalty is neglected;
When authority is light, threats lose their weight;
When trust fails to reach righteousness,
When virtue does not encompass benevolence,
Then governance becomes superficial,
And chaos becomes the origin.
Deceit and falsehood arise,
And disputes spring from resentment.

Therefore, rites and music are established,
Calendars and garments are reformed,
Proper conduct in advance and retreat is prescribed,
Every action follows fixed norms,
Anticipating events to discern gain and loss.
Yet these are but the outward flourishing of Dao,
The superficial aspects of virtue—
Temporary laws, partial techniques—
Not suited to govern an endless age
Or harmonize diverse customs.

Thus, the roots of calamity and confusion lie here,
The beginning of folly and delusion lies here.
What is called foresight—
The outward adornment of Dao,
The first step toward ignorance.

How may this be made clear?
Zhuangzi said:
*"The response of Heaven and Earth follows events,
And events respond to change.
Change has no fixed time,
Thus actions cannot be predetermined,
Nor can change be preordained—
Just as pain cannot be pre-moistened,
Nor itching pre-broken,
Five flavors cannot be measured by bushels,
Nor zithers tuned by inches.*

Rites are suited to their time;
When time shifts, rites must diverge.
To impose the rites of one era
Upon an endless custom—
It is like gluing a pillar to a boat,
Or tuning a zither while holding a ruler—
Thus, it cannot endure the long term.

Therefore, the most subtle subtlety cannot be spoken,
The most wondrous wonder cannot be transmitted.
Perfect loyalty and trust
Cannot be adorned by rites;
Timely harmony and precedence
Cannot be preserved by calculation.

Thus, the keenly insightful and broadly learned,
With wisdom arising from all directions,
Perceive the threads of yin,
Grasp the patterns of yang,
Understand the Dao of spirits and gods,
Comprehend the principles of all things.
Gazing upward, they see Heaven’s embrace;
Gazing downward, they see Earth’s embrace.
Teaching the people without ceasing,
Acting without end—
Yet achieving balance through this—
Is not what is heard.

To speak of deliberate knowledge is not the method for attaining Great Peace.

Compare the trust of all things in their ruler
To the dwelling of the divine in the body,
Or court well-water in the courtyard.
Water cannot be *made* clear by force,
The divine cannot be *thought* into tranquility.
Between Heaven and Earth, all things flourish together—
Not by artificial means can peace be achieved.
Thus, the noble transformation of the great person
Embodies Dao and embraces virtue,
Pierces the boundless void with clarity,
Completes yet seems incomplete,
Possesses yet seems lacking—
In stillness, formless;
In motion, soundless.
Loyal and trustworthy, yet unassuming,
Ignoring the trappings of authority,
Doing nothing yet achieving all,
Like dragon or serpent.

Rejecting rites and abandoning righteousness,
Returning to the state of non-action;
Adapting to the times and responding to change,
Without pre-set rules.
Holding the subtle and grasping the essential,
Moving with the times;
Flexing and yielding in harmony,
Surviving with change.
Calamity and blame arise from within;
A hundred blessings and myriad fortunes
Are unattached to others.

Abandon that, embrace this.
Obtain the Chapter.

The ancient ones who attained the One
Used it as a foundation for life.
The heavens, attaining the One,
Manifest purity, vigor, and rectitude.
The earth, attaining the One,
Finds tranquility, compliance, and right alignment.
The spirit, attaining the One,
Becomes luminous, responsive, and all-pervasive.
The valleys, attaining the One,
Overflow with boundless abundance.
Lords and kings, attaining the One,
Bring harmony and righteous governance to all under heaven.

The means by which this is achieved
Is the cessation of contrivance.
The heavens, without purity, lack yin and yang—
Then fear they may fracture and fail to purify.
The earth, without tranquility, lacks firmness and softness—
Then fear it may erupt and fail to settle.
The spirit, without responsiveness, lacks relaxation and tension—
Then fear it may exhaust and fail to persist.
The valleys, without overflow, lack fullness and emptiness—
Then fear they may dry up and fail to brim.
Lords and kings, without righteousness,
Excessive pride, miserliness, or arrogance—
And those who claim nobility yet neglect the people—
Then fear their lineage may crumble and their temples topple.

Thus, the noble is rooted in the humble,
And disgrace precedes honor.
The exalted is founded upon the lowly,
And greatness arises from modesty.
Lords and kings, in their self-proclaimed restraint,
Are solitary and impoverished, lacking abundance,
Their names are obscure and their forms diminished—
Is this not the way to take the humble as root
And preserve the body within?

Not so! Their affairs are not the One.
Hence, they fashion the cart from non-cart,
And the thing from non-thing,
Not wishing to be busy like the solitary and obscure,
Nor to stand out like the stark and prominent.

The *Dao*’s movement and transformation
Are the principle of change—
The weak, its harmonious application.

The things of heaven and earth,
Having form, arise from causes and conditions;
Having life, arise from the void’s beginning.
The One is the child of *Dao*,
The mother of luminous intelligence,
The source of great harmony,
The ancestor of heaven and earth.

To the spirit, it is non-existence;
To the *Dao*, it is existence.
To the spirit, it is vast;
To the *Dao*, it is minute.
Thus, in its manifestation,
It is both empty and real,
Both nonexistent and existent,
Round yet not circular,
Square yet not measured.
It stretches without end,
Moves without trace,
Neither floats nor sinks,
Neither proceeds nor halts—
It acts yet does not act,
It bestows yet does not give,
Its changes are boundless,
Its principles are contained in the whole.

The void of non-void,
The beginning of beginnings,
Neither outer nor inner,
Mingled in primordial chaos—
Blurred and indistinct,
It may turn left or right.
In emptiness, it abides as constant,
In stillness, it reigns supreme.
It flows through the ten thousand heavens,
It permeates the myriad lands.
All things arise from it,
Yet it bears no form or sign.

The One alone remains,
In mysterious solitude,
All-encompassing without gaps,
Unchanging in simplicity.
Mingled in dark clarity,
It lacks nothing.
It molds the luminous spirit,
Yet does not share its nature.
It shapes the heavens and earth,
Yet does not dwell among them.

It receives without depletion,
It gathers without hoarding—
Neither crooked nor straight,
Neither first nor last.
Its grandeur is boundless,
Its depths unfathomable.
Above and below cannot conceal it,
Its currents cannot be measured.
It spreads and nourishes,
Radiant and unceasing—
Nourishing without mingling,
Transforming without joining.
It does not create, yet all things arise;
It does not act, yet all things are accomplished.
Beyond heaven and earth,
Within the smallest measure,
The breath of *qi* differs,
The forms and kinds are diverse—
Yet all attain the One’s essence to live,
And all fulfill its transformation to thrive.

Thus, the One is the guiding thread for all things,
And the supreme principle of change.
It is the standard for all directions,
And the balance for all variations.
The One is its name,
Virtue its title,
Non-existence its dwelling,
Non-action its work,
Formlessness its measure,
Return its great cycle,
Harmony its end,
The weak its use.
Thus, to know the One,
All changes are inexhaustible,
All transformations are unerring;
To fail to know the One,
Fortunes wax and wane,
Those who rule nations perish,
Those who guard their lives are lost.

Therefore, the ancients who attained the One:
The heavens, in their nature, attained the One’s purity,
Yet what the heavens do is not purity.
Without heart or intent,
Without action or deed,
They follow their nature.
Mysterious and silent,
Without container or shape,
They preserve their life.
Thus, yin and yang arise spontaneously,
Change unfolds naturally—
So they move with firm yet yielding vigor,
Achieving their height,
Luminous and clear,
Greatly harmonious,
Pure and true, unmingled—
The *Daoyi* stands grand,
Radiant and resplendent,
All things draw from its beginning,
Clouds and mists ascend,
Forms and kinds flow forth,
The primal breath of life—
Mysterious and boundless,
Without fail, it covers all.

The heavens attain the One with purity.

The earth, in its nature, attains the One’s tranquility,
Yet what the earth does is not tranquility.
Without knowledge or perception,
Without action or deed,
They follow their nature.
Without measure or number,
Without worry or gain,
They preserve their life.
Thus, mountains and rivers arise spontaneously,
Firmness and softness align naturally—
So they remain steadfast yet yielding,
Direct yet harmonious,
Vast and limitless,
Deep and serene,
All things draw from them to live,
None fail to be sustained.

The earth attains the One with tranquility.

The spirit, in its nature, attains the One’s responsiveness,
Yet what the spirit does is not responsiveness.
Without thought or deliberation,
Without action or deed,
They follow their nature.
Without schemes or plans,
Without echoes or beginnings,
They preserve their life.
Thus, ebb and flow arise spontaneously,
Preservation and extinction align naturally—
So the aged can return to vigor,
The dead can revive,
The trapped can find release,
The ruined can flourish anew—
Change knows no limit,
Return is endless,
All kinds entrust themselves to it,
None stray from its core.

The spirit attains the One with responsiveness.

The valleys, in their nature, attain the One with fullness,
Yet what the valleys do is not fullness.
Without desire or seeking,
Without action or deed,
They follow their nature.
Without kindness or righteousness,
Without giving or bestowing,
They preserve their life.
Thus, solid and void arise spontaneously,
Flourishing and decline align naturally—
So they steam the mountains and flow the marshes,
Becoming pathways of virtue,
Trickling yet ceaseless,
Endless yet uninterrupted,
Radiant and boundless,
Extending far without end,
Filling the rivers and seas,
Deep and vast beyond measure.

「The valleys attain the One with fullness.
The lords and kings’ nature attains the One’s *正* (orthogonality/rectitude), yet what lords and kings do is not rectitude.
Discarding the heart and the will,
Without action or deed,
They follow their nature;
Discarding sharpness and brilliance,
In emptiness and stillness, they respond naturally,
To preserve their life.

Thus, harmony arises spontaneously,
All things align naturally—
So they embody the Dao and harmonize with virtue,
Uniting with Heaven’s principles,
Clasping the spirit and treading upon harmony,
Enveloping all things,
Their influence transforms the myriad,
Filling the six directions with abundance,
Their virtue guides Heaven and Earth,
Their clarity shines like sun and moon,
Their rule governs the world and directs the customs,
Making all under Heaven one.

Lords and kings attain the One to establish rectitude for all under Heaven.
In all these five cases—
Attaining the One and acting upon it—
They flourish without decline,
Achieve without deficiency,
Flow without interruption,
Glow without extinction.

Why is this so?
Nature and life are spontaneous,
Their movement follows the One.

Thus, if Heaven acts,
Its movement does not follow the One,
It will gain elevation yet lose stability,
Gain purity yet risk fracture,
And the yin and yang will stray from their proper courses,
The fundamental principles will slacken,
The harmonious *qi* will be blocked—
The Three Lights will vanish,
Thunder and lightning will act in disorder,
And all things will lose their way.
Heaven, without stillness, will fear fracture.

If Earth acts,
Its movement does not follow the One,
It will gain straightness yet lose flexibility,
Gain tranquility yet risk eruption—
Mountains and rivers will crumble,
The firm and yielding will be twisted,
The *qi*’s transformation will not flow,
The Five Phases will be impaired,
All grains will wither,
And living beings will suffer pestilence.
Earth, without tranquility, will fear eruption.

If the spirit acts,
Its movement does not follow the One,
It will gain openness yet fall into constraint,
Gain responsiveness yet risk exhaustion—
Change will lose its order,
Movement will stagnate and deplete,
Those who flourish will perish,
Those who relax will die.
The spirit, without responsiveness, will fear exhaustion.

If the valleys act,
Their movement does not follow the One,
They will gain existence yet risk annihilation,
Gain fullness yet risk depletion—
Void and solid will invert,
Flows will not enter.
The valleys, without fullness, will fear depletion.

Lords and kings who act,
Their movement does not follow the One,
They will gain nobility yet lose humility,
Gain rectitude yet risk downfall—
In chaos and confusion,
Actions spring from their own will,
Officials stray from the center,
They lose their true name and substance,
The people do not return,
And Heaven and Earth will sever.
Kings without nobility will fear downfall.

In all these five cases—
Nature and life, purity and beauty—
Change reaches its utmost extremes,
Advance and retreat, bending and extending,
Never straying from the proper measure—
Attaining the One, they endure;
Losing the One, they perish.
Much less so for those who rule the myriad without being sages,
Who abandon the proper measure and follow their own hearts.

To uphold the proper measure in action
Is still not free from blame and calamity,
Much less so for those who abandon the measure and follow their hearts—
Thus, they perish in no time.

Therefore, the Dao of Heaven and humanity,
The myriad transformations of things—
The few become the many,
The humble become noble,
The high become low,
The completed become ruined,
What benefits becomes harm,
What profits becomes injury.
Those who dwell in opposition find their reversal,
Those who seek gain lose what they cherish.
This is called: *"Nobility rests upon humility as its foundation,
Elevation rests upon lowliness as its base."*

Thus, the virtuous ruler and sage sovereign
Hold sway over the people,
Their rank is esteemed throughout the world,
Their blessings extend to all things,
Their virtue encompasses the four seas.
The Dao protects them,
Heaven and Earth assist them,
All things return to them,
Ghosts and spirits align with them,
Their austerity inspires virtue,
Yet they call themselves solitary and few.
This is called: *"Lords and kings, calling themselves solitary and few, do not attain the valleys."*

Dwelling in lowliness and guarding modesty,
Engaging in labor and hardship,
Humbling their hearts and curbing their wills,
Striving to place themselves below the people—
Not claiming nobility, so they command the people’s lives;
Not claiming elevation, so they remain above the people;
Not desiring, so they possess all;
Not acting, so they govern all.
Amidst the myriad’s confusion,
Their own being is uninvolved—
Thus they become the foundation of all.
This is not unique to the ruler’s Dao;
All affairs are the same.

The craftsman shaping a carriage,
Makes it round or square,
Short or long,
Curved or straight,
Vertical or horizontal—
Yet all his life he labors,
And in the end, it is not a carriage—
Thus he can complete the carriage and make it usable.
This is called: *"Counting the carriage without making it a carriage, yet achieving its form."*

Jade, as a thing,
Is subtle and few;
Yet stone, as a thing,
Is vast and many.
Many, hence humble;
Few, hence noble.
Jade and stone,
Though born of the same kind,
Few and many,
Are either sought or discarded.
Thus, nobility and humility lie in abundance or scarcity,
Success and failure lie in whether one acts or not.
Thus, neither does one desire to be polished like jade,
Nor to be coarse like stone.

Therefore, the sage acts through reversal,
Guards through harmony,
Adapts with the times in ascent and descent,
Follows transformations in things.
Neither stone nor jade,
Ever dwelling between them—
Neither excessive nor deficient,
Neither noble nor humble—
The One as their guiding principle,
The Dao as their supporting structure.
Thus they can dominate all under Heaven with power that cannot be overcome,
Preserve all living things with virtue that cannot be measured—
Noble yet without worry,
Humble yet without harm,
Elevated yet without peril,
Lowly yet ever more secure,
Discerning in reversal,
Returning to primal silence,
Clear in presence and absence,
Reverting to the first beginning.

Without acting for themselves,
Their spirit and clarity do not falter;
Without acting for all under Heaven,
All under Heaven aligns with them.
This is called: *"Reversal is the Dao’s movement,
Weakness is the Dao’s use."*

Why is this so?
Following the Dao in movement,
Conforming to the One in action—
The Dao’s utmost subtlety,
The One’s greatest simplicity—
Change arises through reversal,
Harmony through refinement,
Existence through non-action.
Heaven and Earth are born from the Great Harmony,
The Great Harmony is born from the Void and Dark.
The Void and Dark are the utmost non-being,
Yet the Great Harmony begins with them and generates.
The Great Harmony has the seed of being,
And Heaven and Earth draw upon it to begin—
This is called: *"Heaven and Earth, the myriad, are born from being,
Being is born from non-being."*

The upper sage hears the Dao and finds it profound and good,
Diligent in following it, for their nature is near;
The middle sage hears the Dao and doubts it shallowly,
As if it exists or does not, for their nature is distant;
The lower sage hears the Dao and finds it unnatural,
Laughing at it, for their nature is opposed—
Not to laugh is insufficient for the Dao;
The Dao’s symbols must be displayed.»

「Thus, the sage sets forth the words of *having*—
To present the Dao as though in darkness, yet its movement is ceaseless and subtle;
To advance the Dao as though in retreat, returning to its origin;
To smooth the Dao as though with a file, refining its roots;
To uphold the highest virtue like a valley, bestowing it in profound mystery;
To display great purity as though in disgrace, appearing unwise;
To manifest abundant virtue as though insufficient, leaving no trace to describe;
To establish virtue as though by stealth, diminishing the people’s blessings;
To reveal true essence as though in error, seeming shallow and lacking;
To embody the Dao’s vastness without corners, without crookedness or straightness;
To achieve greatness through slow maturation, not by immediate clarity;
To produce the grandest sound where voice is scarce, where speech is faint;
To manifest the most sublime forms where shape is none, where no setting is made;
To conceal the Dao without name, without posthumous titles, without distinction—

Only the Dao, indeed, is good at lending itself to completion,
And responds to all things.

**Returning to the source:**
The Way and virtue of Heaven and Earth each have their own patterns,
Things have their high and low, *qi* has its short and long.
Each takes delight in what it delights in,
Suffers from what it suffers,
Sees what it sees,
Hears what it hears,
Accepts and rejects with divergent paths#3,
Fears and rejoices in different directions.

Thus, the quail and partridge soar high,
Yet their whole day is spent in ceaseless flight,
While their hearts dwell in the humble weeds;
The wild goose and swan rise aloft,
Crossing east and west, spanning thousands and reaching ten thousand,
Yet their hearts dwell in the marshes and ponds;
The phoenix and *luan*#4 soar above the ninefold peaks,
Leisurely in the boundless purity,
Yet they always consider themselves lowly.

Stretching their necks, spreading their wings,
They skim the azure clouds,
Eclipse the sun and moon,
Soar high and drift far,
Go long days without eating,
Travel the nine regions,
Rest in the eight extremes,
And thus find their true fit.

The three creatures differ in their ways,
Yet all find joy in their own kind.

Therefore, the boundless source,
The ten-thousand-fathom springs,
Where the divine dragon takes its rest,
And tiny fish retreat—
High mountains and great mounds,
Deep forests and vast ravines,
Lush trees with sprawling branches—
Are where the great birds and tigers and leopards take delight,
Yet where the chickens and dogs recoil in disgust.

Alas, the inherited customs of the Three Dynasties,
The rustic scholars and inked literati’s refined styles,
Reciting the *Shijing* and *Shujing*,
Practicing rituals and etiquette,
Singing elegies and odes,
Plucking the *qin* and *se*,
Exalting benevolence and righteousness,
Honoring purity and clarity,
Studying past antiquity,
Mastering divination and numerology,
Fixing what is and condemning what is not,
Achieving personal security and fame,
With neighbors preserving their legacy—
These are the ways of the middle sage,
Yet abandoned by the upper sage.

In quiet seclusion and profound contemplation,
They strain their minds to comprehend all things,
Fabricate falsehoods and disguise reality,
Speak empty words of names and things,
Dash about in pursuit of advancement or retreat,
Ascend or descend, kneel or bow,
Regulate the rituals of the inner chambers,
Conform to the customs of their age,
Lean or recline, tilt or bow,
Strive to align with the world’s expectations,
Flatter the wealthy and honor the noble,
Cater to the masses’ ears and eyes,
Gain esteem and favor from the powerful,
Follow the trends of the common folk—
These are the practices of the lower sage,
Yet rejected by the middle sage.

Thus, rules and measures do not harm one another,
Diverse natures find their own harmony;
The wise and saintly are not paired with the unworthy,
The foolish and clever do not form a single group.

The noble take joy in simplicity and tranquility,
The petty revel in grand and imposing achievements,
Yet fail to understand the humble dwelling of the common folk,
Nor delight in the deeds of a true gentleman.

Birds and beasts all flourish together,
Each pursuing its own inclinations;
Scholars of all kinds traverse the world,
Each finding their own path.

Therefore, they abandon sharp intelligence,
Discard clever scheming,
Return to true simplicity,
Roam in the Great Purity,
Hold the world in disdain,
Stand aloof without blemish,
Let anger and joy not disturb their hearts,
Let profit and harm not enter their minds,
Treat noble and base as equal,
Hold life and death in balanced measure,
Act without striving,
Gaze upon the profound mysteries,
Their spirits serene and undefiled,
Embrace virtue and contain harmony,
Naturally reversing the transformations of the world.

This is what the greatest sages uphold,
And what the upper sages strive for,
While the middle sages are dazzled by it,
And the lower sages laugh at it in derision.

Thus, what the middle sages hear is not the utmost beauty,
And what the lower sages see is not the utmost goodness.
What dazzles the middle sages and amuses the lower sages
Is truly the most beautiful and good of all.

To lay out grand theories and expound lofty doctrines,
To display the natural and exhaust the subtle—
Then the middle sages are dazzled,
And the lower sages laugh in scorn.

To float empty words and wander in persuasions,
To generate endless variations and schemes,
To create blessings and seek advantages,
To achieve success and fulfill tasks—
Then the middle sages debate,
And the lower sages wake to awareness.

This is not because they delight in calamity and abhor fortune,
Nor because they value misfortune and despise blessings—
Their nature is far removed,
Their feelings opposed.

It is as though they were in the Yellow Springs,
Listening to the nine heavens,
Yet so distant and utterly cut off
That they cannot see or hear at all.

The lower sages do not laugh at the great Dao,
But the Dao is too lofty to be seen—
Like playing a drum before an ox,
That is why they laugh.

Thus, the sage sets forth the words of *having*—
Those who speak of *having* say the Dao is hard to know,
Trace the natural origin of all things,
And use these to guide the myriad directions of life.

To truly speak of *having* is beyond the grasp of the mediocre.
Once the extraordinary Dao is understood,
It is beyond the reach of ordinary men.

Why is this so?
The sage’s Dao is profound, subtle, vast, and distant,
Majestic yet elusive, dim yet luminous,
Empty yet tranquil, where all things pass.
From the finest to the grandest,
It has no form or image.

To push it to its limits is to know it cannot endure,
To constrain it tightly is to find words cannot express it,
To shift and disperse it is to see books cannot convey it—
The bright Dao appears as though in darkness.

Why does advancing the Dao seem like retreat,
And the lost Dao appear as though in existence?
To govern the world, one must first rectify oneself.

Empty stillness is the Dao’s gateway,
Tranquility is the root of the spirit,
Serenity is the origin of harmony,
Silence is the foundation of virtue,
Frugality is the vessel of *qi*,
Subtlety is the craft of action.

Dwelling beyond the realm of *having*,
Standing before the realm of *having*,
Abandoning the world,
First cultivating oneself,
Nurturing the spirit and accumulating harmony,
To govern one’s own heart—

The heart is the sovereign of the body,
The body is the heart of the state,
The world responds in kind,
As though by nature.

Thus, advancing the Dao seems like retreat.

Therefore, to smooth the Dao as though with a file,
Is to let the true and profound arise,
To discard its trappings and distinctions,
To abandon its divisions and logic,
To follow the people’s hearts,
To listen to their natural inclinations,
To extinguish its ornate expressions,
To level its highs and lows.

To break down barriers and shatter keys,
So that deceit naturally ceases;
To dismantle walls and scatter prisons,
So that the people naturally defend themselves—」

The breath of life ceases, the armies rest—
The world becomes a great marketplace.
Ten thousand regions flock to it,
Like rivers flowing to the sea.

The Dao is smoothed as though with a file.
Virtue like the Han Valley—
Not giving, yet all is given;
Not loving, yet all is benefited;
Not dwelling, yet not absent;
Without action, yet grace overflows;
Without kindness, yet blessings abound.
Nurturing all life,
As the mother of the world.

Abundant virtue is like a valley.
Great brightness, pure and green,
Ever as though in fear,
Without constraint yet power ascends,
Without reliance yet authority is heavy.
Virtue mingles with transformation,
Friending the world,
Emerging white, returning black,
Not for beauty’s sake,
Fleeing merit, shunning fame,
Yet ever luminous.

Great brightness seems like shame.
The person of abundant virtue—
Sincere and earnest,
As though insufficient,
Formless, without appearance,
Simple in emotion, easy in nature,
Transformed into childlike innocence,
Doing nothing yet all is done,
As though deaf, as though mute,
The body dwelling in one,
The spirit encompassing all.
Changes unseen, joys unheard,
As though closed, as though sealed,
Alone with the Dao.

Abundant virtue seems insufficient.

Establishing virtue like theft—
Nothing cannot be accomplished.
Plugging the people’s ears and eyes,
Adorning their spirits,
Cutting their desires to benefit their nature;
Extinguishing their pleasures to prolong their lives;
Reducing their adornments so they have no schemes;
Sealing their hearts and minds so they find peace.
Establishing virtue like theft.

Authentic substance like decay—
The people’s mysterious standard.
Nurturing them with the Dao,
Feeding them with virtue,
Guiding them with spirit,
Harmonizing them with laws,
Dwelling in heaven and earth,
Illuminated by sun and moon,
Transformed by yin and yang,
Sustained by water and grain,
Governed by the formless,
Bound by the boundless.

The world murmurs in submission;
The realm is at peace, all things flourish.
Yet it is not their doing,
Nor their virtue—
Great yet seeming small,
Pure yet seeming thin.
Authentic substance like decay—
Decay, meaning shallow and thin.

The great square has no corners,
Encompassing all without measure,
Square yet not square,
Straight yet not straight,
Without boundaries or walls,
Without laws or forms.
Not straight, not square—
All things find their place;
Not square, not straight—
Heaven and earth move naturally.
In action, it is the yin of negation;
In stillness, the yang of affirmation.
Harmony is the central sovereign;
Distinctions clarify themselves.
Unified with heaven, constant with earth.
The great square has no corners.

Thus, great vessels mature late,
Containing all without limit.
Transforming in the formless,
Changing without trace,
Moving yet soundless,
Acting yet bodiless.
Awe and virtue unseen,
Achievements unviewed,
Calamities stilled in darkness,
Blessings born in obscurity,
Silent yet accomplished—
This is called supreme skill.
All things arise from it,
Yet none know how.
Striving yet complete,
Thus enduring forever.
Great vessels mature late.

Therefore, the greatest sound is rare in voice,
Announced without words.
Speaking in silence,
Divine transmission unfolds—
Motionless, yet the world harmonizes.
Soundless, yet all things respond,
Heaven, earth, and all beings
In perfect accord, like echoes answering sound.
The greatest sound is rare in voice.

The greatest form is formless,
The greatest appearance has no shape.
Advancing, all things live;
Retreating, all things perish.
Heaven and earth bow and rise with it,
Yin and yang bend and stretch in response,
Following its form, mirroring its image,
Like shadow to shape.
The greatest form is formless.

Thus, the Dao’s fullness has no name,
Virtue’s abundance no posthumous title.
Merit surpasses measure,
Yet the world does not call it great;
Virtue spans the four seas,
Yet the world does not deem it noble.
Its radiance illuminates the six directions,
Yet returns to obscurity.
The Dao is hidden, nameless.

Why so?
The Dao’s transformation—
Beginning in the nonexistent,
Ending in the trivial,
Existing in nonexistence,
Lending in non-lending,
Moving, all things are made;
Still, the world is fulfilled.
Generous in lending, yet complete.

「**Chapter on the Generation of the Dao/Way**

The Dao/Way generates *One*—a state of confused and indistinct darkness. *One* generates *Two*, which is the realm of the divine and luminous. *Two* generates *Three*, the harmonious mingling of purity and turbidity. *Three* generates the myriad things, manifesting as the forms of Heaven and Earth and humanity.

All things bear yin within and embrace yang without, turning toward the yielding to give rise. The subtle *qi* unites them in harmony, and the weak become complete. What humanity abhors—nameless, solitary, and lowly—are the very things that earn the titles of *Ruler* and *Noble* through ritual and birth. To diminish it is to benefit it; to benefit it is to diminish it. To teach it as lowly and weak is also to teach it as the sacred and knowing. The arrogant and forceful have power, yet they cannot command even their own death, making them cheap in life. I shall use them as examples of calamity and extreme misfortune.

**Annotations on *Zhi Gui* (指归):**
The *void within the void*—opening and guiding the reception—is the void itself, the Dao/Way.
There is no *void* without the void, yet the void cannot void itself.
The Dao/Way can void and thus generates all things, but all things cannot void and generate the Dao/Way.
Therefore, the Dao/Way is the origin from which all things void—the reason it is said: *"There is no void without the void, yet the void cannot void itself."*

The *void* that generates is the transformation and change of the subtle.
The origin of existence is the subtle, yet existence cannot generate itself.
The subtle is *One*.
*One* can be the origin of existence, but it is not a tangible form of existence that cannot generate itself—hence: *"The origin of existence is the subtle, yet existence cannot generate itself."*

The *void of the nonexistent*—the divine and luminous—cannot be altered.
The *void* that creates existence is the nonexistent, yet the nonexistent cannot exist.
The nonexistent is *Two*.
*Two* arises from *One*, though it has a form, and thus can create existence—but it is not existence itself that can create. Hence: *"The nonexistent is the void that creates existence, yet the nonexistent cannot exist."*

The *void* that generates is the subtle and mysterious.
The *void* that moves and completes is the completed, yet the completed cannot complete itself.
The *void* is *Three*.
*Three* arises from *Two*, yet also has its form, rooted in *One*, receiving its mandate from the divine. It portends the generation of all things, yet all things cannot complete it—hence: *"The void that moves and completes is the completed, yet the completed cannot complete itself."*

Thus, the *void within the void* generates the *voids*—the nonexistent, the nonexistent, and the void that generates form.
Therefore, all things with form belong to the category of *things*, and each thing has its origin, each category its ancestor.
Heaven and Earth are the greatest of things; humanity follows next.

Now, the generation of Heaven and humanity—
Form arises from *qi*,
*Qi* arises from harmony,
Harmony arises from the divine and luminous,
The divine and luminous arise from virtue and the Dao/Way,
Virtue and the Dao/Way arise from naturalness,
And all things exist.

Naturalness is the name given to that which no thing compels—it is the Dao/Way.
The Dao/Way’s natural transformation generates the divine,
The divine communicates and forms harmony,
Harmony disperses and becomes *qi*,
*Qi* condenses and takes form.
Hence it is said: *"The Dao/Way generates One, One generates Two, Two generates Three, Three generates all things."*

Therefore, Heaven is called Heaven not because it is Heaven,
And humanity is called humanity not because it is humanity.
Existence arises from the origin, yet the origin cannot generate existence—hence: *"What is called humanity is not humanity."*

How can this be made clear?
Zhuangzi said:
When a person’s form decays, where does it derive from?
When the wise and responsive shine forth, where do they obtain this?
When transformation reaches its end, who is its author?
The origin lies in the nonexistent.
From this perspective, existence arises from the nonexistent,
And reality arises from the void—this is made clear.

Thus, the nonexistent is the origin of the nonexistent,
And cannot be grasped in existence.
It has no form, no sound, and cannot be heard or seen.
Receiving the nonexistent and granting existence—
This cannot be spoken or explained as the Dao/Way.

The nonexistent is the origin of the nonexistent,
The beginning of the unbegun.
All things derive from it,
And it is the source of life and nature.
That which has no name is called the Dao/Way.
The Dao/Way is the origin of *One*.

The Dao/Way is the void within the void,
And thus can generate *One*.
The origin is tranquil and boundless—
It is the void within the void that first generates *One*.

There is a primal *thing* of confusion and indistinction,
Vague and indistinct in its emergence.
Light yet not dispersing, heavy yet not settling,
Yang yet without exterior, yin yet without interior.
It has neither above nor below, nor left nor right,
Reaching through without boundary—
It is the guiding principle of the Dao/Way.
Embracing the void, it is spacious and empty,
Enfolding what has not yet come into being.
Formless, nameless,
Blazing yet indistinct,
Confused yet indistinct,
Dark yet beyond measure—
It vanishes in sound and color,
And nothing can compare to it.
Point to it, and there is no direction,
Seize it, and there is nothing to grasp.
Vast and boundless, it cannot be reasoned or explained,
Grand and harmonious, without end or beginning,
The dwelling of all things,
The first of the primordial—
Thus it is called *One*.

The primordial *One* has the nonexistent,
The nonexistent is nameless.
That from which *One* arises—
The *One* yet without form—
Is the virtue/power within the confused darkness that can generate.

Thus, without end or beginning,
Without left or right,
Seeming yin yet not yin,
Seeming yang yet not yang—
Hence: *"Yang without exterior, yin without interior."*

*One* is void, and thus can generate *Two*.
*One* is the void within existence, transforming into *Two*.
With *Two* things arising, subtle and refined,
They exist and sustain existence,
Following things in their transformations,
Slippery yet formless,
Their vitality never decaying,
Illuminating the dark mysteries,
Without direction or existence,
Enfolding Heaven and Earth,
Their origin unseen,
They cannot be traced by sound,
Nor evaded by form—
This is called the divine and luminous.

Existence sustains things, absence destroys them.
Wisdom and power cannot reach them,
Nor virtue and might be employed—
This is called *Two*.
*Two* is the divine and luminous.

*Two* arises from the origin’s nonexistent,
And thus can generate *Three*.
The divine and luminous are the nonexistent within the nonexistent,
And thus can generate *Three*.

With *Three* things arising together,
Mingled and indistinct,
Visible yet no form discerned,
Heard yet no sound perceived,
Seized yet no thread grasped,
Gazed upon yet no entrance seen—
It cannot be measured or fathomed,
Dark yet indistinct,
Grand yet harmonious,
Pure and turbid in unity,
Moving with harmony,
The origin of Heaven and humanity,
Yet without distinct form or boundary,
Rooted in *One*, receiving its mandate from the divine—
This is called *Three*.」

「Three is the *Great Harmony* (Tàihé).
*Three* arises from the nonexistent,
And thus can generate all things.
The *Great Harmony* is the nonexistent within the existent,
A single transformation yielding the existent,
Hence the saying: *Three* generates all things.
With purity and turbidity divided,
High and low arrayed,
Yin and Yang first distinguished,
And the *Harmonious Qi* (Hégǔ) flowing,
The *Three Lights* (Sānguāng) revolving,
All classes of beings born,
Things with form that may be traced,
Things with sound and color that may be seen and heard—
This is called all things.

When all things are born,
They all originate from the *Void* (Xū),
And begin with the nonexistent.
The *Void* is the root of the nonexistent,
The origin is the root of beginnings.

Backing Yin, facing Yang—
All things back Yin and face Yang.
Returning to softness, abandoning hardness,
In stillness and purity, unmoved,
Mind and intent not stirred,
Yet their form and substance refined,
Their vitality and spirit unbounded—
This is by containing *Harmonious Qi* (Hégǔ) and *Softness* (Ruò),
So that the *Way* is formless.

Thus, the *Void*, the nonexistent, the formless, the subtle, the few, and the soft—
These are the source from which Heaven and Earth arise,
And the root by which all things are generated,
What the common people detest yet rulers name themselves with,
The primal origin of all things,
The fundamental root of success.

For the *Void*, the nonexistent, the solitary, and the few—
These are the fundamental roots of all things,
Hence rulers name themselves with them,
Yet the common people detest them.

Therefore, the wise sovereign and saintly ruler,
With their utmost honor and greatest power,
Dwell in solitude and fewness,
Reside in humility and simplicity,
Pursue what they seek yet flee what they desire,
Discard greatness for smallness,
Find joy in lowliness and loss,
Leave no trace when they act,
Nor any mark when they withdraw,
Advance in fortune and retreat in calamity,
Act without doing, yet all things settle,
Observe not, listen not,
Embrace *Harmony* (Hé) in stillness,
Give birth to divine luminosity,
Their form and substance naturally upright,
Their advance and retreat in accordance with the *Way*,
Never altering their course,
Their virtue soaring like the wind,
Their principles reaching all things,
Heaven and Earth aiding them,
All things returning to them.

Loss is gain.
The common people are not so—
They see and hear only what is already manifest.
Seeing and hearing only manifest things,
They align with what has already come to pass,
And fail to perceive the changes yet unseen,
Hence they value hardness and strength.
Wielding great authority and creating power,
They govern all affairs yet fail to restrain them,
Dispising softness and fewness,
Distancing themselves from subtlety and the solitary,
Their actions clash with the *Way*,
Their stillness contradicts Heaven,
Divine luminosity dissipates into turbidity,
All affairs arise in chaos,
Their thoughts confused and errant,
Their joys and angers unfounded,
Fortunes flee the door,
Calamities enter the home,
The Heavenly Net descends—
They cannot escape it.

Gain is loss.
Then suddenly calamity arises,
And they awaken in sorrow,
Bow their heads in speech yet lower their words,
On the verge of death, they praise virtue.
Though they wish to reform and renew,
Returning to fewness and softness,
It comes too late, and they cannot be released,
Their path to life is distant,
Their nations shattered, their families ruined,
Their misfortunes extending to their descendants.
Hence, the teachings of the common people,
Transform stupidity into wisdom,
Change weakness into strength,
Abandon subtlety for the manifest,
Discard concealment for display,
Flout humility and compete for glory,
And die in pursuit of honor and fame.
This is what people are taught.

Yet the teachings of the *Sage* (Shèngrén) are contrary to this:
Stupidity becomes wisdom,
Humiliation becomes honor,
Subtlety becomes manifest,
Concealment becomes display,
Fewness becomes multitude,
Weakness becomes strength.
Abandon mind and intent,
Pursue the nameless,
Be without knowing or recognizing,
Return to the *Mysterious Darkness* (Xuānmíng).
Paths diverge, directions vary—
Some persist, some perish.

The teachings of the *Sage* teach with fewness and softness;
The teachings of the common people teach with multitude and strength.
What people are taught, I also teach—
Yet the teachings differ.

Hence, mighty Qin and great Chu,
With their strength and domination, were extinguished;
Divine Han and the rise of the *Dragon* (Lóng),
With their harmony and compliance, flourished.

Thus, the strong stray from the *Way*,
The hard reject divine luminosity,
And the ruler who seeks to live long
Must retreat in order to endure.
The strong and hard
Cannot escape their fate.

Not seeking within themselves,
They blame Heaven and fate,
The *Sage* pities them,
And sets forth these teachings first,
Recording them on bamboo and silk,
Clearly demonstrating them to later generations,
So that throughout their lives they may reflect upon them,
And thus incur their own misfortunes.
I shall make this my foundational teaching.

**Chapter on the *Ultimate Softness* (Zhìróu):**
The *Ultimate Softness* is the most formless thing under Heaven,
Yet it overcomes the most rigid and solid things in the world.
The formless enters the *Gapless Chamber of Non-Action* (Wújiān Wúwéi shì),
Thus I know to see gain and loss.
Non-action’s benefit is to preserve the original and cut off chaos;
Action’s harm is to disrupt the original and sever life.
The teaching of the unsaid closes the door to calamity,
Non-action’s benefit preserves all things,
Yet few under Heaven can attain it.

**Pointing to the Return:**
*Virtue* (Dé) and divine luminosity are the most subtle,
Yet they are the *guests* (Bīn) of divine luminosity.
Divine luminosity is the external manifestation of *Virtue*,
Hence it is called *guest*.

Divine luminosity is the most nonexistent,
Yet the *Great Harmony* is its *subject* (Chén).
The *Great Harmony* is the manifestation of divine luminosity’s work,
Hence it is called *subject*.

Purity and turbidity, the *Great Harmony*,
The *Ultimate Softness*—formless,
Enveloping Heaven and Earth,
Containing Yin and Yang,
Guiding all things,
Without fail maintaining their order.

Some exist beyond the cosmos,
Some dwell within Heaven,
Humans and things borrow from it to be born,
Yet none can see or hear it.

Following the *Way* through three transformations,
All things begin to form,
Humans borrow from it to be born,
Yet none can truly know it.

The hair-fine is insufficient to name it,
The weak are insufficient to describe it—
The *Sage* names it with intent alone.

How the *Sage* is called *Sage*:
All *Sages* obtain their title
By studying the *Way* and preserving divine luminosity,
Cultivating life and safeguarding truth,
Achieving truth and thus the *Way*,
Enveloping Heaven and Earth.

This is the profound and essential thing,
Hence it cannot be named with intent alone.
Therefore, it is called *Ultimate Softness*,
And named *Formless*.

Thus, the formless thing
Is not overcome by rigidity,
Nor by strength—
Hence it can wear down Heaven and Earth,
Consume copper and iron,
Race like the wind and lightning,
Span the poles and traverse sun and moon,
Circulate above and below,
Pass through and linger without pause,
Soar in stability,
And descend into the formless.

Things with form have solidity,
The *Void* without subtlety has no power.
The *Way*, neither existent nor nonexistent,
Can thus uphold existence without obstruction.

How does one demonstrate its truth?
The echo is without sound yet cannot be exhausted,
The shadow is without form yet cannot be measured,
Water, though soft and weak, pierces metal and stone,
And sinks all things.
Earth, though gentle and compliant, achieves great works,
And surpasses grass and trees.»

The tongue and ears suffer no harm,
Yet horns and teeth are injured and broken—
Thus it is seen: the soft overcomes the hard,
The empty overcomes the full—
Not by contrivance, but by nature’s own way.

Such is the inevitable order of things,
Unalterable and unavoidable.

This is the natural order of affairs,
Not the natural essence of the *Way*.

Thus, when the land is narrow and the people few,
With scant soldiers and meager provisions,
When desires are subtle and intentions refined,
When the spirit is bright and vigilant,
And harmony aligns with Heaven—

To regard the people as one’s own children,
With virtue flourishing and transformation vast,
With deep benevolence and abundant grace,
When officials are loyal and soldiers trustworthy,
When the ruler worries and generals tremble,
When softness accumulates and weakness endures,
Ever placing oneself last among the people,
Bearing shame and humiliation,
The state becomes a submissive female,
Yet the lords of the realm trust it,
Comparing it to an infant,
And all under Heaven flock to it,
As though returning to parents.

When the people share a single desire,
Authority and might arise naturally,
The strong cannot oppress,
The great cannot seize,
From beginning to end, strength and weakness invert,
Heaven and Earth lend their aid,
The spirit’s brilliance provides support,
Opportunity arrives without constraint,
And one becomes the master of all under Heaven.

Why is this so?
Because the *Way* is soft and weak,
Yet its essence is subtle and sparse.

Thus, when the land is vast and the people many,
When the state is rich and its armies strong,
When historians are bold and soldiers fierce,
When the ruler commands with severity,
When rewards are heavy and punishments sharp,
When laws are rigid and punishments deep,
When officials tremble before the sovereign,
When advantage favors terrain and strategy,
The realm becomes the hero of the world,
Lightly provoking enemies and delighting in battle,
Easily mobilizing troops,
Where cunning begets the extraordinary,
Where Heaven is defied and Earth is scorned,
Where lords submit in fear,
None dare resist,
Where terror shakes the borders,
Where one is always the model of excellence,
Where people fear and things tremble,
Where might shakes Heaven and Earth,
Where virtue and the *Way* are abandoned,
Where the spirit departs,
Where the weak unite in disunity,
Where the people do not rally,
Where the ruler dies and the state collapses,
Where the lineage scatters and disperses.

Why is this so?
Because their essence is hard and rigid,
And their greed and stinginess accumulate.

The *Way* manifests as the having of the non-existent,
