Passing through without obstruction,
Moving without constraint,
Illuminating the halls of contrivance,
Purifying the chambers of non-action,
Entering and exiting without boundary or fracture,
Traveling through pearls and jade without trace.

It is said: the utmost softness
Overcomes the utmost hardness.
How does one demonstrate this?

Sharp blades with form
Cannot pierce the formless.
The spirit, dwelling in the body,
Exits without obstruction,
Enters without aperture—
In the blink of an eye,
It traverses thousands of miles.
There is no entering the formless.

From this, it is said:
Action brings ruin and no fruit,
Non-action brings fulfillment without end.
Heaven and Earth are thus formed,
Humans and things are thus flourished.
The sound of sound is heard a hundred *li* away,
The sound of no-sound moves beyond Heaven,
Shaking the four seas.

What is spoken of is spoken of—
Different kinds cannot communicate.
What is not spoken of—
Transforms yin and yang,
Makes Heaven and Earth respond.

For when virtue and the *Way* are in non-action,
Heaven and Earth are completed.
When Heaven and Earth do not speak,
The four seasons proceed.
These two things—
The signs of the spirit’s brilliance,
The verification of nature’s course.

Thus it is known that non-action is beneficial.
Therefore, the sage empties the heart
To return to virtue and the *Way*,
Calms the *qi* to preserve the spirit’s brilliance,
Diminishes sharpness to hear the soundless,
Abandons clarity to see the formless,
Observes the transformations of Heaven and Earth,
Encourages the natural course of all things,
To perceive how contrivance is the origin of chaos.
Having reached the function of non-action,
One naturally sees the disorder of contrivance.

Non-action is the root of governance.
Speech is the doorway to calamity.
Non-speech is the gate to blessing.
Thus, abandon wisdom and discard cleverness,
Eliminate benevolence and discard righteousness,
Awaken the heart of the *Way*,
Exalt the intention of virtue,
Follow the spirit and nurture harmony,
Entrust oneself to Heaven and serve Earth,
Let yin and yang fulfill their duties,
Let the four seasons move freely,
Cut off the roots of chaos,
Let things rest in their places,
Let the ruler remain serene and unadorned,
Let the people have no concerns.

Teach with the speech of no-speech,
Transform with the transformation of the untransformed,
Demonstrate with the symbol of no-symbol,
And return to the mysterious and profound,
Cover the people’s desires,
Follow their nature and vital essence,
Make the people ignorant,
And they will live long and see far.

This is the teaching of no-speech.

Thus, when I speak not, Heaven and Earth act without contrivance,
When Heaven and Earth act without contrivance, virtue and the *Way* act without contrivance.
These three harmonize and advance together,
Their *qi* blending and overflowing,
Generating great peace,
Gathering humans and things,
Unifying the world within,
Closing the door to calamity,
Making all under Heaven like infants,
With no shame or disgrace,
No sight of fortune or misfortune,
No knowledge of origins or endings,
Naturally vast and unrestricted,
Each household receiving the blessings of the spirit’s brilliance,
Each person achieving the deeds of the sage’s wisdom.

The benefits of non-action.

At such times,
The ruler is like Heaven and Earth,
The people like infants,
Drinking the ruler’s virtue,
Feeding on the ruler’s harmony,
Yin emerging, yang retiring,
Rolling and unfolding with the *Way*.
The sovereign and father above
Are present yet absent,
The world is dazed and content,
Soft and murmuring,
Unknowing like a newborn,
Non-action like a fledgling,
Born without joy,
Dying without sorrow,
Grieving yet enduring,
With vitality in excess,
Seeking nothing,
Yet blessings arrive of their own accord.
Few under Heaven attain this.

Why is this so?

The sovereign who does not speak yet embodies the Dao of non-action.
The key of non-action, the mechanism of speechlessness,
Lies in subtlety and refinement,
Resides in the divine and the profound.

The onset of the divine and profound,
The origin of subtlety and refinement,
Gives birth without root or stem,
Emerges and retreats without gate or door.
Ever abiding between action and non-action,
The primal source of harmony,
The Dao, though formless and unseen,
Can be known through its timely resonance.

Thus it may be heard yet never fully revealed,
Seen yet never fully expounded,
Grasped yet never fully transmitted,
Utilized yet never fully spoken.
To seize and then shove away,
To hold fast and then relinquish—
Easy for the wise sage to explain,
Difficult for the shallow to comprehend.

Why so?
Because it is vast and profound yet common folk cannot reach it,
Because its lofty heights are inverted yet common folk cannot enter,
Because it is faint and diffuse yet the world cannot discern it,
Because it is obscure and hidden yet vulgar rulers cannot practice it.

The body’s name—who is closer, fame or self?
Self or wealth—what is more abundant?
Gain or loss—what is more harmful?
Thus extreme affection brings great depletion to the spirit,
Excessive hoarding brings heavy ruin and retreat to the body.

Therefore, knowing sufficiency prevents disgrace,
Knowing cessation prevents peril,
And the body may endure long,
With great vitality preserved.
**Point of Return:**

That which I inherit by nature and am,
Is virtue and power.
That which I borrow to live,
Is the spirit’s brilliance.
That which I rely upon to flourish,
Is the Great Harmony.
That which I entrust to take form,
Are Heaven and Earth.

All these four—
They nourish me, yet I cannot nourish them.
Thus no law is higher than virtue and power,
No model is greater than the spirit’s brilliance,
No standard is broader than the Great Harmony,
No illumination is grander than Heaven and Earth.

Virtue and power—
Ever living, never dying;
Harmony of purity and turbidity—
Endless transformation.
The Dao of Heaven and Earth—
Preserved yet hard to lose;
The workings of yin and yang—
Ever moving, hard to conclude.

Heaven and Earth, yin and yang,
But seen in their difficulty to conclude,
Not because they lack beginning or end.
From this perspective,
Misfortune reaches its extreme at death,
Fortune reaches its extreme at birth.
Thus the sage,
Above, traces the intent of virtue and power,
Below, measures the heart of Heaven and Earth,
Exalts and displays honor,
Invokes auspiciousness and flourishing virtue,
Embraces depth and vastness,
Cultivates reverence and exhaustion,
Yet nothing surpasses the value of life.

All things arrayed,
Wonders and treasures,
Gold and jade, pearls and jade discs,
Their use profound yet their gain immense—
Nothing surpasses the body.

The artisan of worldly calamity,
The craftsman of national chaos,
Who defies Heaven and Earth,
Who harms the body—
Nothing surpasses the name.

**Extreme pride and excess,**
**Oppressing the people, impoverishing the state,**
**Disturbing the spirit’s clarity,**
**Multiplying desires of the heart,**
**Rebelling against Heaven, violating the Dao,**
**Competing to become thieves and robbers,**
**The world shuns them, wars abound,**
**One person’s actions bring ruin to ten thousand states,**
**The ruler dies, the people perish,**
**All creatures suffer their poison—**
Nothing surpasses wealth.

Though wealth and name are feared and shocking,
Their benefits to the body are distant indeed.
Thus gain and loss,
Sometimes harmful, sometimes useful.
Gaining name or wealth,
Virtue and power do not abide,
The spirit’s brilliance does not linger,
Great vitality is severed,
Heaven cannot save.

Losing name and wealth#1,
Virtue and power naturally support,
The spirit’s brilliance naturally aids,
Fame appears effortlessly,
Riches align with Heaven and Earth.
Gaining name or wealth,
Losing the Dao and the body.
Losing name and wealth,
Benefits align with Heaven and Earth.
Thus preserving the body while pursuing great fame,
Cannot yet be discussed in terms of the ultimate Dao;
Lightening the body while valuing the state,
Cannot yet be plotted for profit.

The name without name,
Is the dwelling of my life;
The name with name,
Is the sack that buries me.
The wealth without wealth,
Is the nourishment of my fortune;
The wealth with wealth,
Is the thief that robs me.
Thus extreme affection for the body,
To build and maintain fame,
Acting and laboring for it,
Forcing nature and temperament,
Only depletes the spirit.

Excessive accumulation of wealth,
Daily swelling with arrogance,
The path to ruin—
Wealth and name both end.
Extreme affection brings great depletion.

Thus the spirit’s brilliance cannot sustain life,
Heaven and Earth cannot preserve the body.
Why is this so?

The transformation of **Dao** and **virtue/power** follows the patterns of Heaven and Earth—
one yin, one yang,
dividing into the four seasons,
separating into the five phases,
spinning like a net,
setting traps without gaps.

All things’ natures,
each have their measure,
unable to interfere.
The heart of creation,
harmonious and upright with fairness,
naturally unified—
straightforward, balanced, and equal,
neither favoring nor rejecting,
communing with all things.
Extending the long,
continuing the short,
reducing the excess,
supplementing the deficient—
the insufficient are nourished,
the surplus perish.

Greed and accumulation bring self-inflicted calamity;
insufficiency without restraint stirs the heart of gain.
The wise deceive the foolish,
the strong seize what they desire—
Nature balances it:
name and profit return to their origin.
Losing them brings sorrow,
gaining them brings joy.
One joy, one sorrow—
the soul and spirit wander;
one sorrow, one joy—
the spirit departs.

When the body dies, the name vanishes,
and disaster extends to descendants.
Thus, name and profit with the body,
are like charcoal and ice—
forms and natures opposed,
their forces cannot coexist.
When name reaches its end and the body its limit,
there is none in the world who survives with both thriving.

The empty is where **Dao** returns,
the real is where things perish.
Now, if one accumulates the real and seeks to align with the empty,
it is like water and fire repelling each other—
impossible to achieve.

Thus, disturbing the heart, scheming the mind,
using emotions to exhaust the spirit,
night and day pursuing affairs,
adornment and rhetoric,
worrying over the masses,
creating deeds and establishing merit,
striving for self-discipline to display virtue—
this depletes what sustains life
and increases what destroys it.

Exhausting sinew and strength,
enduring hunger and thirst,
bearing cold and heat,
treading dangers and narrow paths,
coarse clothing and poor food,
unsuited to appetite,
serving court and night,
bearing shame and disgrace,
spirit and essence fleeing—
unrelenting, opposing **Dao** for glory,
entering excess to possess,
risking the body for security—
wealth accumulates while the spirit perishes,
disaster naturally follows.
Arrogance and ruin arrive together—
this is using fortune to destroy fortune,
seeking profit while losing it.

The more one hoards, the greater the ruin.
Thus, success and failure depend on action or inaction,
life and death on departure or arrival.

Therefore, those who know sufficiency,
align with **Dao** and virtue/power,
abandon name and profit,
establish the self in non-being,
nourish things without self-generation,
share with things without self-preservation—
in sincerity and compliance,
sufficient to preserve the spirit.
Household affairs suffice for a lifetime.

Ever natural, thus unassailable;
dwelling in emptiness, thus unpenetrable;
light on name, light on things, thus unstained;
desiring without desire, thus enduring glory—
this is called *not being humiliated*.

Those who know restraint,
whether noble as a sovereign or poor in caves,
do not distort their will,
nor dim their spirit.
Advancing does not bring pride,
retreating does not bring despair.
No gain, no loss,
no guilt, no merit,
no seeking, no refusal—
like the sea, like a great river,
wandering in the boundless domain,
spirit and clarity unified.
Moving in harmony with Heaven and Earth,
thus unshaken;
distinct from harm and gain,
thus ever constant.

Thus, profound and unshaken,
spirit firm and unbroken,
like Heaven and Earth in grandeur,
like the sun and moon in radiance—
both refined and spiritual,
to preserve the body.
Knowing sufficiency and stopping,
thus enduring forever.
Knowing restraint brings no peril.

This is called *chasing name while name pursues me*,
*fleeing profit while profit pursues me*.
To conceal desire while revealing it—
this can endure forever.

**Great attainment resembles a missing chapter**—
great attainment resembles a missing law—
formless, its use unexhausted, transformation flowing.
**Great fullness resembles emptiness**—
masterless, its use unfathomable, principles vast.
**Great straightness resembles bending**—
nameless,
great skill resembles clumsiness—
unaccomplished,
great eloquence resembles stammering—
full yet empty.
**Agitation overcomes cold**—
movement in form and appearance,
**stillness overcomes heat**—
calm in form and spirit.
To be able to still and clear—
this is Heaven and Earth,
the rectifier for all things, the standard of the world.

**Pointing to the return:**
**Dao** and virtue/power act without action, yet spirit is manifest;
spirit acts without action, yet **Great Harmony** arises.
Without action, things regulate themselves.
Some are born without roots, some walk without feet,
some hear without ears, some sing without mouths—
diverse kinds, distinct orders,
all trading with them.
Mothers grieve for their children,
children grieve for their mothers,
male and female pair,
things honor their masters,
nest-born peck, womb-born nurse,
birds scatter when startled,
beasts flee when alarmed,
yin-things dwell in burrows,
yang-things nest above,
fire moves upward in flame,
water moves downward in moisture—
all things verdant,
spring born, summer growing,
autumn ripening, winter maturing—
all return to soil.
No governance or teaching—
things act naturally.

This is the natural **effort**, **pattern**, and **measure** of yin and yang,
inevitable as such.

From this perspective,
*non-action* does not generate *non-action*,
*negation* does not generate *negation*,
*clarity* does not generate *clarity*,
*obscurity* does not generate *obscurity*.
*Non-action* is not *negation*,
*clarity* is not *obscurity*—
only then does one grasp the rhythm.

*Non-action* is not *negation*,
*clarity* is not *obscurity*—
this is ease, aligning with **Dao**.

Thus, the **Great Dao** is vast and open,
not confined to doors—
the farther it extends, the fewer who know it.
**Dao** resides in the self, not in the wild,
transformation originates within, not from without—
all things perpetually ordered,
wisdom does not arise.

Therefore, the sage holds **Harmony** and treads **Rectitude**,
governs without form,
wanders in emptiness,
mirroring **Great Clarity**,
abandoning soul and spirit,
resting essence and spirit,
acting without action,
silent yet trustworthy,
vast and boundless,
illuminated and solitary—
approaching yet unattainable,
its essence true,
its use unexhausted,
unseen, unheard.

This is called **great attainment resembling a missing chapter**—
its use unexhausted.

Why is this so?

Subtle and thorough,
clear and still in truth,
before form and sound,
transforming its origin—
opening like yang,
closing like yin,
blocked like earth,
moving like Heaven.
**Patterned and martial**, **mysterious and virtuous**—
profound virtue naturally divides.

Thus, when full yet appearing empty,
when solid yet appearing void,
when benevolence and righteousness are not flaunted,
when propriety and decorum are unseen,
when laws and institutions are not erected,
when action is not contrived—

The ruler desires not to desire,
yet the world transforms itself.
Gentle and unadorned, the people are like infants,
dimly unaware, their longings vague,
their paths unknown—
its use inexhaustible,
flowing yet never decaying.

Great fullness resembles emptiness,
its use inexhaustible.

Without tilling, food is plentiful;
without weaving, clothing is ample.
In summer, they rest in nakedness;
in winter, they wrap in furs.
No taboos exist—
they dwell with beasts, unbound,
hair loose, suckling at will,
wandering freely together.
The ruler abounds in virtue,
the people abound in wealth.

Its transformation pervades all things,
doing without doing.
Its radiance unseen, its mystery profound—
Heaven, Earth, and all beings
transform with it in harmony.

Riding the void, bearing the empty,
wandering with the Dao,
measuring the four seas,
circulating through the six voids,
vast and boundless,
dwelling in the utmost nothingness.

Why is this so?
Straight yet appearing crooked,
true yet appearing wrong.
Great straightness seems like crookedness.

When the ruler speaks, the world echoes;
when the ruler acts, all beings follow.
Thus, without sacrifices, Heaven’s harmony aligns,
without decrees, the four seas rectify.
Hence it is said: *Great skill resembles clumsiness.*

Heaven’s Way is naturally humble—
without calendars, yin and yang harmonize;
without fixed seasons, the four times proceed;
without laws, the world is at ease;
without rewards or punishments, names and realities align.

Concealing martial might, it conquers all;
abandoning warfare, it overcomes all.
Without commands, the people govern themselves;
without rituals, the realm enlightens itself;
without seals, the world trusts itself;
without measures, all things balance themselves.

Great eloquence seems like stammering.
Thus, though weak, it appears deficient;
though gaining, it seems like loss.
Without bells and drums, the people rejoice;
without five flavors, their food is sweet;
without adornments, their beauty is natural;
without hoarding, their abundance overflows.

Why is this so?
Following the Dao, trusting Heaven, not relying on knowledge—
thus the people act naturally.

Though the Five Emperors seemed unworthy,
each achieved greatness.
The enlightened ruler, through the Dao, transforms people,
making them align with the Way.

Heaven and Earth’s Way—
advancing and retreating in turn—
all things thereby flourish.
Transformation is unobstructed,
flexing and extending cannot be barred.

When yin reaches its peak,
the earth splits and ice congeals,
cold winds howl, frost descends thick,
fish and turtles burrow deep,
all things curl in fear.
Yet in this time,
dwelling in warm chambers,
beside blazing fires,
wearing thick furs and layered silks—
still, one cannot withstand it.
But when the mind steadies and the spirit calms,
when the body moves and toils,
then sweat pours, garments are cast aside,
and warmth suffuses the body.
*Agitation overcomes cold.*

When yang reaches its peak,
sand is seared, stones crumble,
birds take flight, water creatures flee,
all things wither, rivers dry up.
Yet in this time,
plunging into cool springs,
wearing coarse linen,
dwelling in high halls,
wearing cold stones—
still, one cannot endure it.
But when the heart releases, the mind clears,
when the spirit drifts beyond the four seas,
when the will wanders in the void,
when breath and heart align—
coolness pervades the body.
*Stillness overcomes heat.*

Thus, knowing how to act is a craft—
governing people, nurturing life,
virtue extending to Heaven and Earth,
achievement matching yin and yang.
Yet when chaos arises,
it emerges without form,
stirs without sound,
expanding with governance,
shifting with transformation.
It seizes people like dampness,
reaches them like shadow—
responding like echoes to speech,
never leaving their forms.
The more one acts, the greater the disorder;
the more one governs, the more tangled the affairs.
Even the wise cannot lead,
even harsh punishments cannot restrain.

Yet the *non-acting* ruler
is the sovereign of action,
the origin of governance and transformation,
whose removal of calamity
is like agitation overcoming cold
or stillness overcoming heat.

Thus the sage abandons knowledge, abandons scheming,
empties the heart, focuses the breath,
clears and stills, responding naturally—
then Heaven’s will aligns,
Earth’s intent follows,
governance rises, transformation flows like sunlight,
calamity vanishes like dispersing clouds.
The world follows its example without limit,
all things learn from it without restraint.

This is called *able to clear, able to still—
the world naturally rectifies itself.*

---
**When the Way prevails in the world, the ruler desires nothing—**
even warhorses are turned to manure for fields.
**When the Way does not prevail, the ruler takes action—**
warhorses breed in the suburbs, laws favor martial might.

No sin is greater than ceaselessly pursuing desire,
no calamity greater than insatiable greed,
no blame greater than coveting gain.
Contentment’s fullness knows no lack—
it possesses all without taking.

**The Way’s return:**
A person’s life is entrusted to the ruler;
the ruler’s standing depends on the people.
When the ruler follows the Dao, the people flourish;
when the ruler loses the Dao, the people perish.
The people’s flourishing makes temples glorious;
their ruin makes temples crumble.
Thus the ruler is the people’s source;
the people are the ruler’s root.
When the root is injured, flowers and fruit wither;
when the source decays, the flow runs dry.
Above and below sustaining each other—
thus they endure.

Therefore, when the ruler follows the Dao,
the world is undisturbed,
lords and vassals submit in reverence,
barbarians rejoice in submission,
the four seas share the same winds,
weapons never rise,
border guards have no use for their words,
mighty warriors have no place for their strength.

The wise and clever till where rain falls,
fine steeds pull plows.
This is called: *When the Way prevails, even warhorses are turned to manure.*

The world at ease, each pursues their work,
customs are sincere, the people unified—
clothing woven from hemp, food from tilling,
Heaven’s heart in harmony, all things bountiful,
auspicious omens frequent, blessings abundant.
Not Heaven’s bestowal, but the ruler’s virtue and Dao.

「When the Son of Heaven loses the Dao,
lords do not pay tribute,
valleys split and streams diverge,
laws and institutions clash and differ,
the four quarters rebel and vie in strength,
raising armies to contest authority—
the weak become captives#2,
the strong become rulers.

Thus, the land selects generals and sharpens warriors,
kindling beacon fires on all sides,
deeply plotting and crafting great deceits,
strategizing in the halls of state,
concocting schemes that spawn rebellion,
forming shifting alliances—*crossing and combining*—
light chariots and swift cavalry surge forth,
enemies rise to match them in might,
warriors and steeds perish in the wilderness,
year after year without return,
their ambition and force twisted into ruin,
their governance marked by treachery and violence.

In such times, they groom warhorses
without pause for kin,
race to battlefields first,
dwell on coarse fare of beans and millet,
greedy men sit as butchers,
lowly servants rise as brigands,
the people exhausted and spent,
treasures drained, strength weary,
endless conscription and military labor.

This is why warhorses are born in the wilds.

They long to return home,
but sorrow and lament fill their hearts—
remembering parents aged and weary,
weeping in exile.

Kind fathers and benevolent mothers,
grief and anguish pierce their souls,
their resolve and spirit shattered within.

Soldiers lie slain, heads and heels bound,
bones exposed to the elements,
scattered in the desolate fields—
numberless beyond reckoning.

The roads stretch desolate,
all are fatherless sons,
yearning for command,
rising with sobs and tears—
what crime against Heaven,
to suffer such calamity?

Females lack husbands,
children lack fathers,
their cries of woe and sorrow
gather without cause.

The mighty become leaders,
the middling become butchers,
those above and below protect one another,
inner and outer realms guard as one—
not bound by blood,
yet closer than brothers.

Tall grasses serve as banners,
hollowed earth as drums,
seizing weapons and wielding tools,
marching in disciplined ranks,
constantly drilled in warfare,
their thoughts and loyalty fixed on their lord,
so ardent that their spirits intertwine,
their *qi* and transformations move as one.

Thus, Heaven and Earth grow rigid and disjointed,
yin and yang are severed and blocked,
stars scatter and wander,
sun and moon clash in eclipse,
deceit and rebellion sprout,
calamities arise in tandem—
not Heaven’s infliction of woe,
but the ruler’s loss of the Dao.

The ruler without the Dao
was not born without the Dao,
but first gained Heaven’s mandate through it,
yet failed to uphold it,
and in arrogance and excess,
knowing no bounds,
reverts to his original desires,
sharing the same fate as slaves and captives.

To receive Heaven’s grand mandate,
to follow the sacred ones before,
noble as the Son of Heaven,
rich with all the four seas,
honored with supreme rank and favor—
none can compare.

Yet coarse robes and simple furs are deemed delight,
plain vegetables and humble broths are called exquisite.

To transform the world and shift its customs
is as effortless as wind bending grass;
the people’s conformity
is as natural as fish to water.

If one does not strive to elevate the Dao,
broaden virtue,
refine oneself and rectify one’s conduct,
grieve for the common folk,
to fulfill ancestral sacrifices,
to honor forefathers and pass on their legacy—
to vie with Heaven and Earth in renown,
to share their eternal preservation—
but instead pursues pride and extravagance for fame,
seeks power without restraint,
defies Heaven and opposes Earth,
spurning all with insolence—

then the unworthy rise in defiance,
lightly pressing deep into battle,
the first to arrive are deemed rightful,
distant foes go unchallenged,
alliances fracture, bonds dissolve,
the inner and outer realms offer no reliance,
and with their deaths comes the fall of the state,
the ancestral temples crumble—
yet these are the consequences of their own greed,
not the fault of the world.

This is called: *No guilt is greater than unchecked desire.*

Thus, those who wield authority and honor,
exhausting the people’s limits,
whose fame and titles cover the land,
yet know no contentment—
they become instruments of disaster,
the grand measure of their own ruin.

No misfortune is greater than knowing no contentment.

For the ruler’s virtue and sacred power,
to mold and transform—
already attained, they preserve the people,
unify spirit and form,
and take great shape.

Their movements are effortless,
ears and eyes keen,
wandering in bright and open realms,
listening across Heaven and Earth,
observing Nature’s eternal laws,
studying the gains and losses of ancient generals—
digging wells to drink,
plowing fields to eat,
long wives and children born,
living in harmony with fate—
this is true contentment,
the fullness of sufficiency.

Different beings share the same attainment,
thus it is sufficiency.

How much more so for the lord of ten thousand chariots,
the ruler of a thousand chariots?

Their sufficiency is clear indeed.»

The Way is not in this—
when greed arises in the heart,
coveting others’ lands,
desiring their wealth and treasures,
merging and seizing without end,
ever increasing without cease—
this is the great cause of calamity,
the ultimate source of blame.

No fault is greater than the desire to take.

From ancient times to now,
flying birds and running beasts,
all living things with breath and kind—
none preserve their nature and life
without the desire to take.

Thus, the one who dwells as a ruler becomes a captive,
the one who dwells as a tiger becomes a mouse.
Though their name soars above the green clouds,
their body lies beneath the Yellow Springs.

Those who occupy the station of ox or horse
suffer no ox or horse’s fate;
those who take refuge among dogs and sheep
bear no dogs and sheep’s blame.

Therefore, the lord who attains the Way
establishes his heart in sufficiency,
wanders his mind in stillness,
rejects might and yields to power,
stands alone and dwells in solitude,
abandons all things,
and holds only the numinous in his grasp.
His life preserved, his name honored,
he endures without peril,
and all under Heaven turns to him.
None can resist him.

This is the sufficiency that is always sufficient.

Not stepping beyond the doorstep—
not leaving the door to wander the courtyard—
one knows the households of the world,
knows the people.

Not peering through the window—
there is nothing to gaze upon.
Seeing the Dao of Heaven,
one knows Heaven itself.

The farther one goes from home,
the less one knows—
no sight, no hearing.

Thus, the Sage—meaning the enlightened ruler—
acts without moving yet knows all under Heaven,
sees without looking yet names the Heaven and Earth,
does without doing yet accomplishes through spontaneity.

**The Return to Origins:**
Virtue and power transform,
molding the primal head,
receiving life and nature
from the boundless void,
the mysterious dark—
and from this, all things arise in undifferentiated chaos.

The numinous and the clear interact,
pure and turbid separate,
and the Great Harmony flows
through the vast and open wilds,
the subtle and refined—
and from this, all things are born.

Heaven is round, Earth is square,
humans stand upright, beasts move horizontally,
grasses and trees take root,
fish sink, birds soar,
each thing by its kind,
each kind by its group—
rank and status are fixed,
and from this, fortune and misfortune arise.

From this perspective,
Heaven, Earth, and all beings share the same origin,
the same ancestral source.
Within the four quarters and beyond the cosmos,
all are connected as one body.

Qi transforms and separates,
spreading horizontally and vertically,
divided into two,
judged into five.
Two—Heaven and Earth.
Five—the five colors, the five phases, the five flavors, the five notes.

Some become white or black,
some water or fire,
some sour or salty,
some the metal or wood phases.
Humans and things of the same kind,
male and female—
all these are kin, like brothers.

Though their forms differ and their lands are distant,
their benefits and harms oppose one another,
and the myriad things vary beyond measure.
They return to joy and anger,
to death and life,
their emotions and nature born together,
their minds and intentions in harmony.

How so?
Zhuangzi said:
Within a single body,
all born of the same parents,
the four limbs and nine orifices,
each with its distinct function,
the five viscera and six entrails,
each receiving its own charge—
above and below do not know each other,
inner and outer do not see each other.
The head and feet are Heaven and Earth,
the elbows and knees are the four seas,
the liver and gallbladder are the Hu and Yue,
the eyebrows and eyes are Qi and Chu.

If they did not share the same origin,
if their bodies were separate and distinct,
their movements would not support one another,
their stillness would not await one another—
even the Nine Heavens above and the Yellow Springs below
are insufficient to describe it.

Yet, if the head is afflicted, the feet cannot walk;
if the chest is sick, the mouth cannot speak;
if the heart finds peace, the ears and eyes are keen.
When bending and stretching are harmonious,
when all joints move lightly—
this is because of their shared form.

When the ruler moves nearby,
all things respond from afar;
when things move here,
Heaven and Earth respond there.
They and I respond in kind,
entering and exiting without gates,
coming and going without doors.

Between Heaven and Earth,
within the vast emptiness,
endless and boundless,
all things resonate in kind,
never missing by a hair—
for they are of one body.

Humans know only the unity of their own body,
but do not know that a single realm is always one body.
Humans know that a single realm is one body,
but do not know that all things share one mind.

If all things share one mind,
how can there be separation within it?

Thus, one knows the world without leaving the doorstep.

Therefore, the Sage
does not step beyond the threshold,
ascends to his parents above,
descends to his descendants below,
weighs peril and security, benefit and harm,
returns to the teachings of life and death,
discerns the principles of right and wrong,
penetrates the origins of benefit and harm,
reaches the roots of order and chaos.

Knowing oneself, one knows the family;
knowing the family, one knows others.
Holding fast to the essentials,
grasping the principles,
in action, knowing where to go,
in stillness, knowing what to guard.

Virtue and power are father and mother,
clarity and stillness are teacher,
Great Harmony is friend,
all under Heaven is home,
all things are body.
View others as oneself,
view oneself as others.
The heart dares not stir,
the will dares not rise.
Abandoning old knowledge,
abolishing the three and five.

Acting without contrivance,
dwelling in caves and holes,
not killing living things,
not eating raw plants,
not wearing what is unformed,
not taking what is incomplete—
Heaven, Earth, and all beings
each preserve what is theirs.

Though Heaven, Earth, and all things seem to differ in form,
their beginning and end, their roots and branches,
are all of one body.
Within this unity, there is no resentment or malice.
Received from virtue and power,
how dare they harm or injure?
Thus, Heaven, Earth, and all beings each preserve what is theirs.

Before my form took shape,
the source of my nature and life,
the origin of spirit and breath,
the foundation of my body—
this reveals that the real arises from the void,
that being comes from non-being.
The small void contains nothing,
the great void encompasses all.

My origin lies in virtue and power,
conceived yet unborn,
the means by which form is perfected
until emerging from the dark—
this reveals the profound, the subtle, the refined,
the harmonious, the weak, the moist—
the great through which all things pass,
the unknown, the unknowing,
the doing without doing, the acting without action—
yet its function is great.

Viewing myself as the infant brother,
until I grew strong and knowing,
I saw the soft giving rise to the hard,
the weak to the strong,
the small to the great,
the short to the long,
the foolish to the wise,
the obscure to the clear.

---

Examine my breath’s inhalation and exhalation,
to know that loss is the first of gain,
gain is the root of loss,
advance is the foundation of retreat,
retreat is the root of advance,
fortune is the beginning of calamity,
calamity is the precursor of fortune.

Ascending steep slopes, traversing obstacles and dangers,
my form grows weary, breathless, and trembling—
yet when I rest in stillness,
my spirit becomes even, my *qi* harmonious,
inner and outer preserved in balance—
this is the equilibrium of those who align with the Dao.

Thus I know the great function of
clearing stillness, emptiness, and non-action,
where transformation unfolds.

The four limbs and nine orifices,
pursuing diverse tasks and errands,
with varied abilities and forms—
all arise from the singular origin of mind.
Thus I know that all things, in their myriad directions and forms,
their benefits and harms, all spring from the master.

The master is the origin of all people,
as the heart is to the body.
Examining the heavens and earth,
verifying past and present,
movement never contradicts—
thus I know the Dao of heaven and earth is complete within me.
I differ not from heaven and earth.

Therefore, the family is the root of knowing people;
the body is the source of knowing heaven.
Observe the body to know the body,
observe the family to know the family,
observe the world to know the world.
To observe heaven without the body,
to observe people without the family—
nearness leads to great distance,
small knowledge leads to great confusion.
Abandon the family and step outside—
you see not the world;
abandon the body and peer through a window—
you know not the Dao of heaven.
The farther you go, the less you know;
roaming the four seas, the more you stray.
The more you seek, the smaller your achievements;
the more you pursue fame, the less you attain.

Do not look, do not listen—
seek within yourself.
At the juncture of heaven and humanity,
the great Dao is complete.
Obtain yourself and obtain heaven,
obtain heaven and obtain the Dao,
obtain the Dao and obtain humanity.
Thus, without stepping outside, one knows the world;
without peering through a window, one knows the Dao of heaven.
The farther one goes, the less one knows.

Therefore, the sage does not observe the likes and dislikes of one family
to command the affairs of ten thousand families;
without traveling a thousand *li*,
he commands the changes of the nine regions.
His feet do not ascend to heaven,
yet he knows the intent of the nine heavens;
his body does not enter the earth,
yet he knows the meaning of the nine depths.
The advance and retreat of yin and yang,
the transformations of the four seasons,
the profound and hidden, the obscure and mysterious—
nothing escapes him.

How so?
By examining the inner to know the outer,
by tracing the small to know the great,
by using myself to understand others,
by clarifying the near to illuminate the distant.

Thus, the sage governs as the heart governs the body,
as the body governs itself.
The heart resides within the body,
yet it does not impose external rules—
only by subtly initiating harmony
do all limbs align in accord.

Not knowing to act in accordance with the Dao,
not desiring to respond to heaven,
acting without action to guide the world,
remaining without doing to nourish the people—
mysterious and silent,
allowing transformation to unfold naturally,
above in harmony with the divine,
below in unity with all things—
moving, they oppose yet sustain;
still, they preserve yet endure.
Empty, tranquil, and secluded,
they let things return to their natural state.

The sage, secluded and without action,
allows all things to naturally conform to the Dao—
like a pearl in water, making the river beautiful,
this is the transmission of divine transformation.
Thus it is said:
the sage speaks not yet is believed,
acts not yet achieves.

Some say the sage, having attained the Dao,
its principle eternally present,
divine transformation ever ongoing—
why, then, do I not practice,
yet naturally align with perfection?
The world grows ever more distant from the Dao.

This fails to grasp the sage’s transformation.
If rain and dew nourish grass and trees,
all flourish with fragrance—
yet withered and dried things remain unchanged.
Can the nature of withered things
absorb the grace of clouds and rain?
Is it not like the blind who do not believe in the light of sun and moon?

---
*(End of Daoist Canon: *Zhuangzi*’s *Gu Shen Zi* Commentary, Vol. 8–9)*

The pursuit of learning daily increases—
yet learning only increases the people’s knowledge.
The practice of the Dao daily diminishes—
yet diminishing only diminishes the people’s knowledge.

Diminish again, and again—
until they know not at all.
Reach the state of *wuwei*—
until there is no doing,
and thus no undone.
To seek to take the world,
one must first harmonize it—
ever abiding in *wuwei*,
ever without function.

When affairs arise, knowledge and ability are strained—
yet even then, they are insufficient to take the world,
and thus it is never attained.

**Commentary:**
The transformation of virtue and Dao—
shifting, void, and mysterious,
vast and silent,
boundless and formless,
turbulent yet indistinct,
chaotic yet without origin.
It cannot be seen, cannot be heard,
yet opens and guides all things—
nothing is absent from its embrace.
When deeds are accomplished, affairs fulfilled,
nothing is left undone.
*Wuwei* is the root of all things.

From this, we see:
The knowing of the unknown is the origin of knowing;
The teaching of the uninstructed is the source of teaching.
*Wuwei* as action is the beginning of action;
The doing of non-doing is the origin of affairs.
The teaching of the uninstructed,
*wuwei* as action—
all are the supreme movements of the ultimate Dao,
formless yet spiritually complete,
ineffable and nameless,
thus called the Great Origin, the Ancestral Source.

All these things:
The workings of the divine,
The return of heaven and earth,
The teachings of the Mysterious Sage,
The transmission of the recluse.

Yet when benevolence and righteousness grow shallow,
life and nature become false,
the Great Dao is unseen,
actions follow mere desires,
they sink into knowledge’s delusions,
are steeped in sorrow and favor,
their emotions and intentions multiply,
their spirit binds to things,
their schemes are deep yet unheard,
their grand theories clash with truth,
they exalt knowledge over the Dao,
value deeds over virtue.

Thus they devise arts and calculations,
compile words and writings,
record them in texts,
to instruct the people.
They weave the threads of heaven and earth,
measure the patterns of yin and yang,
divide and judge human affairs,
scatter the Ancestral Source,
corrupt simplicity with artifice,
fabricate deceits in all directions,
shift customs, topple norms,
alter rites and clothing—
all things become manifest.

Bells and drums, zithers and se,
flutes and sheng pipes,
ascending and descending,
advancing and retreating,
ornate symbols and soaring rites—
three hundred ceremonies, three thousand decorums.
Disputes arise, conflicts multiply,
affairs flourish, words dance,
they argue to subdue, outwit to triumph—
every hair raised, endlessly so.
This is the daily increase of learning.

Thus the world abandons its root, forsakes its origin,
turns to superficiality, clings to words.
Scholarship deepens, questions multiply—
every household knows, every door holds a sage.
The extreme: they emulate the Sage,
to establish lord and subject.

Those in accord, though powerless, are honored;
those who differ, though great in deed, are destroyed.
The Confucian way embraces love yet breeds factions—
those who align with them,
though wicked, are praised as good;
those who do not,
though virtuous, are condemned as evil.

Thus the world is restless,
unable to tend to their kin,
chasing trivial pursuits,
serving their lords.
They blend the five flavors to nourish their mouths—
rich, fragrant, sweet, and crisp—
yet ignore the suffering of all living things.
They alter the five colors to please their eyes—
deep blacks, bright yellows, delicate hues—
yet do not consider the people’s poverty.
They harmonize the five tones to delight their ears—
perfecting the intricacies of bells and chimes—
yet do not fear the world’s corruption.
They build high towers and vast halls to satisfy their desires—
yet do not dread the people’s exhaustion.
They hunt and ride to sharpen their resolve—
seeking personal gain,
yet defying heaven’s will.
They exploit others’ lives to sustain themselves,
diminish others’ wealth for their own profit—
they do not mourn the world’s plight,
only take what they can.
None of this stems from benevolence and love—
all defy the harmony of heaven and earth.

All these things:
Not done for virtue’s sake,
but to please their lords.

Thus the world abandons sincerity,
feigns virtue, masks deceit,
erodes harmony,
nurtures violence’s roots,
until it becomes custom—
cleverness is prized as wisdom,
the people’s vital essence is drained,
their labor increased,
their natural goodness harmed,
their burdens multiplied.

At such times,
valleys rebel against their rulers,
the seas each crown their own kings.
Titles and power are revered,
strength dictates right,
wrath and contention escalate,
might justifies force—
the strong enslave the weak,
the many dominate the few.
They nurse chaos as governance,
distort truth as policy—
subjects slay their lords,
sons slay their fathers.
The greater the strife,
the fewer who can endure.
Many seek, few attain—
the roads fill with sorrow,
all speak of war.
The wails and groans rise—
until men are boiled alive.

Why does this happen?
Because they adorn words and multiply affairs,
competing to outdo each other.

For learning, the error lies in daily increase.
Thus the Sage abandons virtue and discards righteousness,
returns to the Great Dao,
severs wisdom and rejects teachings,
seeking within oneself.
His words grow ever subtler,
his actions ever fewer.
For the Way is daily diminished.

Fade and vanish it must,
night and day without cease,
enveloped in boundless obscurity,
so the people know no shame.
Destroy all texts, abandon all affairs—
the world will settle of its own accord.
Diminish, diminish again,
until all striving ceases.
Diminish yet again.

Eschew renown, abandon the self,
preserve the vital essence and spirit.
Grasp the essence of virtue and power,
secure the mechanism of life and death.
Neither rule as sovereign,
nor teach as master.
Silent as nonexistence,
arriving at non-action.
To reach the utmost non-being.

Heaven and Earth act spontaneously,
virtue and beauty follow naturally,
all things manifest themselves,
the myriad tribes harmonize,
the common folk wander in bewilderment,
unaware of their path.
Illumination emerges from within,
trusting the four seasons.
The spirit drifts freely,
unbound by the mind’s designs.
The heart is empty within,
like wood floating,
like earth at rest.
They know not virtue nor righteousness,
nor grasp ritual and propriety.
The heart desires nothing,
the will acts without purpose.
Their steps are steady and true,
their gaze lofty and far.
*Shuǎnshuǎn*—honest and direct.
*Diāndiān*—elevated and boundless.
Their speech is silent,
their essence profound.
Externally, they seem like beasts,
yet inwardly, they differ.

Silent yet acting,
as if no rulers exist,
governing without action,
thick with loyalty and sincerity,
until great peace prevails.
The spirit rests, the essence breathes—
life and death preserved intact.
All things follow in succession,
aligned with virtue and power.
To act without acting,
yet nothing remains undone.

Why so?
Because the ruler issues no commands,
and the people hear none.
Thus, to take the world,
one must act through non-action.
Speak not of techniques,
teach through non-teaching.
Desire nothing as treasure,
ignorance as the key.
To act in accordance with the Dao,
nothing remains unopened.

To take the world is to act through non-action.
Release the void, return to reality,
take extremes as substance.
Know the height of Heaven above,
the depth of Earth below.
Discern the division of yin and yang,
grasp the patterns of all things.
By day, see stars in the sky,
by night, fish in the depths.
The ears harmonize with the eight winds,
the eyes perceive the fur of all beasts.
This is the utmost of thought—
yet it profits nothing for survival.
Strength tenfold that of Wu Ge,
might a hundredfold that of Meng Xin,
courage a thousandfold that of Xia Yu,
terror commanding three armies,
advancing like radiant light,
retreating like drifting clouds,
striking like thunder,
unmoving as yin.
This is the peak of power—
yet it profits nothing for victory.

If all beneath Heaven were to wield *The Rites* and *The Changes*,
master *The Odes* and *The Documents*,
understand laws and decrees,
know proclamations and orders,
each household a clerk,
each neighborhood an officer,
each village a granary,
each watchtower a treasury,
sharp in judgment, strict in punishment,
strong in suppressing bandits—
the people would stand with heavy feet,
glance with sidelong eyes,
fathers and sons would betray one another,
brothers would harbor no trust.
This is the extreme of governance—
yet it profits nothing for order.

Thus, to know what is known is to separate from Heaven,
to act is to oppose Heaven’s intent,
to act in affairs is to lose Heaven’s purpose.
Daily increase in governance
brings a hundred flaws to fruition.
Acting yet failing to achieve,
seeking yet never attaining—
the world descends into chaos,
ending in disorder.
This is called: when affairs arise,
they are insufficient to take the world—
thus, disorder follows.

**The Sage has no fixed heart.**
The Sage’s heart is formless,
for the Sage takes the people’s heart as their own.
To the virtuous, I am virtuous—
extending their clarity.
To the unvirtuous, I too am virtuous—
transforming their nature.
Thus virtue is attained,
and harmony is restored.
To the trustworthy, I am trustworthy—
extending their sincerity.
To the untrustworthy, I too am trustworthy—
transforming their emotions.
Thus trust is attained,
and peace is restored.

The Sage in the world—
the Emperor—
*Wǎnwǎn*—his heart is empty.
For the world, his heart is vast,
embracing all directions.
The people gaze with their ears and eyes,
but the Sage follows only the Dao.
**Pointers:**
Virtue and power are formless yet rule all beneath Heaven—
the heart without heart exists.
Heaven and Earth act without action yet all things comply—
the thought without thought operates.

From this, it is seen:
The heart without heart is the master of the heart.
Non-use is the mother of use.

How to clarify this?
Zhuangzi said:
*"What I use to be myself—
am I truly myself?
Even my body is not myself.
I am like my body,
yet my body is not myself.
What my body uses to be itself—
it is because I exist.
Because I distinguish,
I am called ‘body,’
yet I do not call myself so.
What I use to be myself—
it is because of the spirit.
What the spirit uses to retain me—
the Dao makes it so.
The Dao generates the spirit,
the spirit generates the body.
Body and spirit unite,
and I am called ‘I.’
I am not myself through the body,
so my body does not belong to itself through me.
I am not myself through the spirit,
so the body and spirit are one.
The Dao, though not having, has—
this is the heart without heart.
Relying on the Dao’s method,
preserving the spirit’s way,
stillness and purity as foundation,
emptiness and nothingness as constant—
this cannot be achieved by heart or intent,
nor realized by thought or deliberation.

Thus, the wise dwell thus:
ears and eyes see and hear,
mind and thought deliberate,
meals and rest follow their time,
fulfilling desires to their utmost.
Cleverness and insight surge without end,
day and night without pause,
experiencing myriad paths,
planning ten thousand affairs,
determining the beginnings of safety and peril,
clarifying the roads of retreat and advance,
aiming to preserve the body and prolong life.

Yet thus,
the spirit is diminished,
the vital essence decayed,
the soul and vital breath scattered—
life and death are cut short.
They strive for their bodies,
yet do not know that thought harms the body.
When they sleep,
mind and intent are idle,
hearing and sight sealed,
thought and deliberation cease,
neither eating nor drinking,
the spirit harmonized,
the vital essence at ease,
the heart finds rest,
the body free of ailments.

When calamity and harm befall,
great sores erupt as rashes,
broken bones are set and bound,
every joint and orifice
fulfills its natural desire.

Yet even in slumber,
one still finds fleeting peace—
how much more so when
one embodies the Dao and forgets the self,
ever at ease.

For with a single body,
to abandon thought is to turn peril into safety,
to employ thought is to risk losing what is secure—
how much more so for those
who uphold virtue and Dao,
align with the numinous and bright,
follow Heaven’s intent,
and nurture all living beings?

Nurturing all living beings
requires above all a tranquil mind.

Thus, the Sage establishes
a body without a body,
a heart without a heart,
a presence within absence,
a trust in what is not stored—
above, encompassing the transformation of virtue and Dao,
below, embracing the hearts of all people.

The Sage has no heart,
yet takes the hearts of the people as their own.

Neither hating nor loving,
neither favoring nor rejecting,
not feuding with the wicked,
not befriending the fortunate,
not consorting with the sincere,
not resenting the deceitful.

Bearing them as the earth bears all,
covering them as Heaven does,
illuminating them as the sun,
transforming them as the numinous.

For humanity’s delusion
has endured for ages.
To suddenly make the unvirtuous virtuous—
how could it be so swift?

One must first comfort and soften them,
let them seek it themselves,
immerse and moisten them,
let them find it themselves—
only then may their clarity grow,
their sincerity take root,
their desires align,
their hearts transform.

Thus it is said:
bear them as the earth bears all,
cover them as Heaven does,
illuminate them as the sun,
transform them as the numinous.

Whether great or small,
all things are viewed as the self.
Act before action begins,
govern before disorder arises,
cutting off misfortune at its source,
awakening fortune from its origin.

Block gradual corruption,
prevent evil’s sprouting,
suppress vice and promote virtue.

Abandon my desires,
take what brings the people ease;
abandon my scheming,
return to what is natural.

Let nature allow all things to find ease,
so the people live unaware in their daily lives.

Move them with harmony,
guide them with spontaneity,
above containing the intent of virtue and Dao,
below attaining the heart of the numinous and bright,
illuminating Heaven and Earth,
connecting virtue to all people.

The people bear no burdens,
the ruler holds no grievances,
all find their true nature,
all retain their vital essence.
Seeing nothing, hearing nothing,
forgetting their refined thoughts,
taking the ruler as their heart.

When the ruler embodies the Dao,
covering people with the Way,
the people receive the ruler’s grace
as if it were their own.

Their hearts follow the ruler,
like children returning to their mother.
Bowing, rising, resting, waking—
all move as if in a marketplace.

With them in bowing and rising,
with them in floating and sinking,
following their external stirrings,
releasing their flexing and bending—
without speaking, the world responds;
without acting, all things endure.
Within the four seas,
no commands are given,
yet all transform their hearts.

The virtuous reach great virtue,
their clarity deepening daily.
The wicked’s nature shifts,
gradually becoming serene.

So-called unvirtuous—
I also treat them with virtue,
thus they attain virtue.

The trustworthy become utterly trustworthy,
reaching beyond self-interest.
The deceitful’s nature transforms,
daily approaching sincerity.

The untrustworthy—
I also treat them with trust,
thus they attain trust.

The cruel and destructive return to virtue,
the deceitful return to truth.
Virtue and vice, trust and doubt—
all return to their natural state.

The reason the Way repeatedly returns to nature
is that the ultimate Dao stands independent and profound,
existing since antiquity.
Its power acts upon all things,
yet all things cannot act upon it—
thus it is called *natural*.

Not that insects and birds
are the ultimate measure.

Those who embody this natural Dao
can harmonize with the dust of the world,
stand without sharp edges,
let things transform of their own accord,
all returning to virtue.
Advancing their singular will,
as if by nature’s own impulse.

As the Sage says:
*"Without speaking, I nourish people with harmony."*

At such times,
the world is submerged in boundless unity,
drenched in supreme harmony.
The people forget their thoughts,
lost in a daze of floating ease,
losing what they hated,
gaining what they sought,
moving with Heaven,
flowing with the Dao—
not driven by coercion to abandon vice,
not bound by teaching to change.

Through *wuwei*, transformation occurs unknowingly.

Why is this so?
The ruler’s transformation
is empty, still, and silent,
like withered wood,
the heart like a hollowed gourd,
the will like the sea,
actions like valleys—
not distinguishing east and west,
not separating south and north,
not judging sweet and bitter,
not favoring white and black,
not enforcing square or round,
not fixing straight or crooked,
delving into the mysterious,
striving to remain hidden.

As the Sage says:
*"Awakened, awakened—
for all under Heaven, I muddle their hearts."*

Without governing things,
floating without end,
abandoning what I would do,
embracing what Heaven would gain,
all things in tumult—
all pour into their ears and eyes.

As the Sage says:
*"The people all pour into their ears and eyes."*

The ruler’s *wuwei*
is serene, composed—
Heaven and Earth as the furnace,
Great Harmony as the bellows,
the numinous as the wind,
all things as the iron,
virtue as the master craftsman,
the Dao as the work—
the world verdant and lush,
nothing left unmoistened.

The Sage contains such transformative power,
thus able to benefit all things endlessly.

Thus can they mold the people’s hearts,
transform the customs of the age,
above encompassing all,
below conquering all,
perfecting all things,
nothing left unmeasured,
stirring all living beings,
shaking the eight extremes.

The world is vast and indistinct,
unaware of good and evil,
darkly effective, obscure in form,
self-forming in law.

The Sage stirs all things,
returning them to the Dao,
following what is fitting to establish law.

---
**出生入死章**
**Birth and Death**

Birth and death,
abandoning *wuwei*.

Those who cling to life—thirteen types—
are heavy with false vitality.
Those who cling to death—thirteen types—
are burdened with excess.
Yet the people live their lives,
driven to death’s edge for profit and name—
thirteen types cling to strength.

Why is this so?
Because their obsession with life
destroys their very life.

**Chapter on Birth and Death**

Birth and death,
abandon *wuwei* [non-action].

Those who cultivate life—thirteen types—
are **empty** [虚], **without** [无], **pure** [清], **serene** [静],
**subtle** [微], **sparse** [寡], **soft** [柔],
**weak** [弱], **lowly** [卑], **self-effacing** [损],
**timely** [时], **harmonious** [和], **restrained** [啬]—
these thirteen are the **Birth** [生] types.

These thirteen,
are the **Dao/Way’s** [道] beginnings,
the **abode of the spirit** [神明].
Hence, they are called the **Birth** [生] types.

Those who cling to death—thirteen types—
are **solid** [实], **excessive** [有], **impure** [浊],
**turbulent** [扰], **manifest** [显], **abundant** [众],
**hard** [刚], **forceful** [强], **elevated** [高],
**full** [满], **extreme** [过], **profligate** [泰],
**exhaustive** [费]—
these thirteen are the **Death** [死] types.

These thirteen,
contradict the **Dao/Way** [道],
oppose the **spirit** [神].
Hence, they are called the **Death** [死] types.

Why is this so?
The **Sage’s Dao/Way** [圣人之道],
in motion has its **root** [因],
in stillness has its **response** [应].
The four limbs and nine orifices—
these thirteen are the **external** [外] **apparatus** [具] of life and death.

The matters of **emptiness** [虚] and **solidity** [实],
the changes of **hardness** [刚] and **softness** [柔],
are the **internal** [内] **counts** [数] of life and death.
Thus, thirteen are spoken of in total.

Because within are thirteen **Birth** [生] types,
and without are the four limbs and nine orifices,
thus they are spoken of as **internal** [内] and **external** [外].

---

The adept at preserving life
nurtures the **spirit** [神明].
On land, he avoids neither **rhinoceros** [兕] nor **tiger** [虎],
yet the tiger does not harm him.
Entering battle, he wears no armor nor wields weapons,
yet weapons do not strike him.

The **rhinoceros** [兕] has no place to lodge its horn—
his **body** [体] is **soft** [柔弱].
The **tiger** [虎] has no place to strike its claws—
his **form** [形] is **harmonious** [和平].
Weapons have no place to lodge their blades—
his **essence** [精] is **unharmed** [害亡中].

Why is this so?
Because **forms** [形] resonate with their kind.
He has no **place of death** [死地], no **form of loss** [亡形].
Thus, **returning to the Dao/Way** [指归]:
**Virtue/Power** [德] and **Dao/Way** [道],
**spirit** [神明], **purity** [清] and **impurity** [浊],
**Great Harmony** [太和] all **mixed** [浑同],
sinking to become **substance** [体].
All things take **form** [形] from it.

Where **form** [形] takes root,
it thrives with **luster** [英英] and **honor** [荣荣],
yet no **mark** [字] is seen.
It is called **Birth** [生].

**Birth** [生] as a **phenomenon** [物],
is neither **yin** [阴] nor **yang** [阳],
cannot be **measured** [揆度] nor **gauged** [测量],
too **profound** [深微] to be named,
too **mysterious** [玄妙] to be described.
Its **radiance** [光] is **dazzling** [耀] yet **flickering** [恍惚],
without **form** [形] or **sound** [声],
without **appearance** [状] or **image** [象].
Its **movement** [动] and **stillness** [静] have no **fixed principle** [方].
It wanders in the **wild of emptiness** [虚寂],
dwells in the **land of nonexistence** [无有].
Those who attain it **survive** [存],
those who lose it **perish** [亡].

Where the **Dao/Way’s qi** [道气] is transmitted,
**yin** [阴] and **yang** [阳] harmonize,
congealing to form **awareness** [识],
called **Birth** [生].
Yet it is neither **form** [形] nor **image** [象],
neither **yin** [阴] nor **yang** [阳].
Hence, it is said: neither **yin** [阴] nor **yang** [阳],
dwelling in the **land of nonexistence** [无有].

**Birth** [生] in relation to **form** [形],
the **spirit** [神] is its **bud** [蒂],
**essence** [精] is its **root** [根],
**vitality** [营] and **refinement** [爽] are its **palace** [宫室],
the **nine orifices** [九窍] are its **gates** [户门],
**clarity** [聪] and **intelligence** [明] are its **ministers** [侯使],
**desires** [情] and **intentions** [意] are its **carriage** [乘舆],
**soul** [魂] and **spirit** [魄] are its **attendants** [左右],
**blood** [血] and **qi** [气] are its **soldiers** [卒徒].

Advancing, he aligns with the **Dao/Way** [道],
retreating, he conforms to **virtue/power** [德].
He neither departs from nor opposes **virtue/power** [德] and **Dao/Way** [道].

Soaring and gliding in **softness** [柔弱],
resting in **emptiness** [虚无],
bending and stretching, bowing and rising,
harmonizing with the **times** [时] as they unfold.

To **lightly regard death** [轻死] is to **contradict** [反] it,
to **desire life** [欲生] is to **be its enemy** [仇].
If there is no **use** [利], it cannot be **pursued** [去],
if there is **use** [用], it cannot be **retained** [留].

To **abandon non-action** [无为] is to let **Birth** [生] arise naturally,
thus he does not **pursue non-action** [去无为].
To **desire life** [欲生] is to **invite death** [死],
thus he does not **retain it** [留].
Hence, **non-action** [无为] is the **home of Birth** [生],
while **action** [有为] is the **house of Death** [死].

To stand is to **forget one’s body** [遗其身],
to sit is to **forget one’s mind** [忘其心],
**plain as an infant** [澹如赤子],
**tranquil as formless** [泊如无形],
neither seeing nor hearing,
neither doing nor speaking.
**Transformation** [变化] and **subtle shifts** [消息]
are without **constancy** [常].
With the **Dao/Way** he bows and rises,
with **virtue/power** [德] he floats and sinks,
with the **spirit** [神] he merges in **substance** [体],
with **Harmony** [和] he bends and stretches.

He does not **debase himself for things** [贱为物],
nor **exalt himself as a man** [贵为人].
His **interests** [利] differ from those of **kings and nobles** [王侯],
his **sufferings** [患] are unlike those of the **common folk** [万姓].
**Death** [死] and **Birth** [生] are one,
thus he does not **distinguish survival and perishing** [别存亡].
This is the **non-action** [无为] of **self-cultivation** [治身].

Spring **gives rise** [生], summer **grows long** [长],
autumn **harvests** [收], winter **conceals** [藏].
He **serves the sovereign’s law** [奉主之法],
**follows Heaven’s command** [顺天之命],
**cherishes his parents within** [内慈父母],
**rejects fame and profit without** [外绝名利].
He neither **plans** [思] nor **ponder** [虑],
neither **competes** [与] nor **demands** [求].
Coming and going alone,
his **body** [体] is **harmonious** [和],
his **conduct** [袭] is **natural** [顺].
He **submits to others in speech** [辞让於入],
does not **contend with the times** [与时争].
This is the **non-action** [无为] of **household governance** [治家].

He **honors Heaven** [尊天] and **respects Earth** [敬地],
does not **dare to abandon the ancestors** [亡先].
He **cultivates himself** [修身] and **rectifies the law** [正法],
**discards self** [去己] and **trusts others** [任人].
He **verifies reality** [审实] and **establishes names** [定名],
**follows things** [顺物] and **harmonizes the spirit** [和神].
He **consults his ministers** [参伍左右],
**connects front and rear** [前后相连].
He **adapts to the times** [随时] and **follows principle** [循理],
**bends to what is fitting** [曲因其当].
All things **act in concert** [并作],
returning to **nature** [自然].
This is the **non-action** [无为] of **state governance** [治国].

**Crownless** [冠无有], **cloaked in formlessness** [被无形],
**embracing emptiness** [抱空虚], **treading Heaven and Earth** [履天地],
**galloping yin and yang** [驰阴阳], **ranging the Five Phases** [骋五行],
**following all things** [从群物], **wandering in the Mysterious** [涉玄冥],
**playing in the realm of no effort** [游乎无功],
**returning to the land of no name** [归乎无名].
This is the **non-action** [无为] of **governing all under Heaven** [治天下].

All who practice **non-action** [无为] are **Birth** [生] types.

Greedy for life and **longevity** [利寿],
fearing they may not attain it,
they **forcefully suppress** [强藏] their **heart** [心] and **intentions** [意],
**close off** [闭塞] their **ears** [耳] and **eyes** [目].
They **guide and lead** [导引] their **steps** [步],
**agitate** [动摇] their **hundred joints** [百节].
They **expel the old** [吐故] and **intake the new** [纳新],
**blow warmly** [吹煦] and **breathe deeply** [呼吸].
They **adorn themselves with the Five Stars** [被服五星],
**nourish with the Sun and Moon** [饮食日月].
Their **form** [形] and **spirit** [神] both **act** [作],
yet they **never rest** [休息].
This is the **action** [有为] of **self-cultivation** [治身].

They **neglect Heaven’s timing** [废释天时],
**solely rely on human affairs** [独任人事].
They **debase themselves** [贱强] to **pursue nobility** [求贵],
**poverty** [贫] to **pursue wealth** [求富].
They **name hunger** [饥名] and **call thirst power** [渴势],
their **heart** [心] is always **laden with seeking** [载求].
Their **clothing** [衣] and **food** [食] are **luxurious and extravagant** [奢泰],
their **undertakings** [事] exceed their **capacity** [务].
This is the **action** [有为] of **household governance** [治家].

They **amass lands** [兼壤] for their **wealthy state** [富国],
**lightly wage war** [轻战] and **take pleasure in arms** [乐兵].
They **establish threats** [底威] and **raise banners** [起节],
their **name** [名] is **displayed** [显], their **power** [势] is **exalted** [隆].
Their **punishments** [刑] are **severe** [严], their **penalties** [罚] are **harsh** [峻],
**rigid** [峭直] and **deeply engraved** [刻深].
Their **laws** [法] are **fine-meshed** [网周], their **governance** [察] is **poisonous** [操毒],
**sparse in kindness** [少恩].
The **feudal lords** [诸侯] **fear and revile** [畏忌] them,
they are **often hailed as heroes** [俊雄].
They **pursue the title of Marquis** [公强求伯],
**Marquis** [伯] to **King** [王].
This is the **action** [有为] of **state governance** [治国].

They **cherish ancestral and filial piety** [祖孝悌],
**uphold benevolence and righteousness** [宗仁义],
**refine rituals and propriety** [修礼节],
**teach the people to adorn themselves** [教民知饰].
They **cultivate** [修治] **colors** [色] and **flavors** [味]
to **please the people’s hearts** [以顺民心].
They **employ bells and drums** [钟鼓], **lutes and zithers** [琴瑟]
to **harmonize the people’s wills** [以和民志].
The **sovereign speaks** [主言], the **ministers listen** [臣听],
the **sovereign moves** [主动], the **ministers follow** [臣随].
They **display achievements** [表功] and **exert force** [厉行],
**opening with kindness** [开以恩厚],
**proclaiming orders with splendor** [号令声华],
**making the people cling** [使民亲附].
They **undertake all affairs themselves** [诸事任己],
**rely on the people in all matters** [百方仰朝].
This is the **action** [有为] of **governing all under Heaven** [治天下].

All who practice **action** [有为] are **Death** [死] types.

Hence, the thirteen **Birth** [生] types—
**emptiness** [虚], **without** [无], **purity** [清], **serenity** [静],
**subtlety** [微], **sparseness** [寡], **softness** [柔], **weakness** [弱],
**lowliness** [卑], **self-effacement** [损], **timeliness** [时],
**harmony** [和], **restraint** [啬]—
are the **Dao/Way’s** [道] beginnings,
the **abode of the spirit** [神].
Thus they are called the **Birth** [生] types.

The thirteen **Death** [死] types—
**solidity** [实], **excess** [有], **impurity** [浊],
**turbulence** [扰], **manifestness** [显], **abundance** [众],
**hardness** [刚], **strength** [强], **elevation** [高],
**fullness** [满], **excess** [过], **profligacy** [泰],
**exhaustion** [费]—
contradict the **Dao/Way** [道],
oppose the **spirit** [神].
Thus they are called the **Death** [死] types.

Why is this so?
The **Sage’s Dao/Way** [圣人之道],
in motion has its **root** [因],
in stillness has its **response** [应].
The four limbs and nine orifices—
these thirteen are the **external** [外] **apparatus** [具] of life and death.

The matters of **emptiness** [虚] and **solidity** [实],
the changes of **hardness** [刚] and **softness** [柔],
are the **internal** [内] **

The **void** [虚] gives rise to **fullness** [充] and **solidity** [实],
**emptiness** [无] sustains **constancy** [常存];
**clarity** [清] brings **acuity** [聪] and **penetration** [达],
**stillness** [静] yields **inner luminosity** [内明].

**Subtlety** [微] generates **magnificence** [章] and **manifestness** [显],
**sparseness** [寡] produces **abundance** [众];
**softness** [柔] begets **hardness** [刚] and **robustness** [健],
**weakness** [弱] fosters **firmness** [坚] and **strength** [强].

**Lowliness** [卑] engenders **elevation** [高],
**depletion** [损] spawns **advantage** [益];
**timeliness** [时] ensures **permeation** [通] and **reach** [达],
**harmony** [和] achieves **moderation** [中].

**Frugality** [啬] results in **excess** [余]—
this is called **augmenting life** [益生].

Those who practice this **Dao/Way** [道],
align with **Heaven and Earth** [天地],
endure long in **the body** [为身],
prosper far in **the realm** [为国].
Though they wish otherwise,
**Creation** [造化] does not comply.

For **emptiness** [虚] and **voidness** [无] are **clarity** [清] and **stillness** [静],
and if one seeks to **unify with the Dao/Way** [合道],
they can give rise to **all things** [诸有].
Thus, though they wish otherwise,
**Creation** [造化] does not permit it.

**Solidity** [实] produces **emptiness** [空] and **voidness** [虚],
**excess** [有] leads to **consumption** [消] and **extinction** [亡];
**impurity** [浊] causes **obstruction** [塞] and **deafness** [听],
**turbulence** [扰] brings **loss of luminosity** [失明].

**Manifestness** [显] reverts to **subtlety** [微],
**abundance** [众] returns to **sparseness** [寡],
**hardness** [刚] yields **softness** [柔] and **flexibility** [韧],
**strength** [强] generates **weakness** [弱] and **calamity** [殃].

**Elevation** [高] descends to **lowliness** [卑] and **abasement** [贱],
**fullness** [满] leads to **depletion** [损] and **emptiness** [空];
**profligacy** [泰] invites **constraint** [困] and **poverty** [穷],
**exhaustion** [费] beckons **misfortune** [祸].

These thirteen—
they are the **burdens** [累] of **form** [形],
the **roots** [元] of **disaster** [祸].
Thus, when one acts in accordance with them,
they drive one to **extremity** [穷].

In **the body** [为身], they bring **short-lived endurance** [不久],
in **the realm** [为国], they cause **instability** [不平].
Though one wishes otherwise,
**Heaven and Earth** [天地] do not obey.

**Action** [有为] must meet **defeat** [败],
**natural law** [理数] is immutable—
thus **Heaven and Earth** [天地] do not comply.

Yet the people all cherish their **life** [生] and **augment it** [益] without ceasing,
all love their **bodies** [身] and **favor them** [爱] without end.
Their **movements** [动] lead to **action** [有为],
their **scheming** [智虑] constantly arises.

**Human existence** [人之生],
is the **path to Death** [动之死地].

Thus they **forsake emptiness** [虚] for **solidity** [实],
**abandon voidness** [无] for **dependence** [依有],
**leave clarity** [清] for **impurity** [浊],
**turn from stillness** [静] to **turbulence** [扰].

They **change subtlety** [微] into **manifestness** [显],
**transform sparseness** [寡] into **abundance** [众],
**reject softness** [柔] for **hardness** [刚],
**discard weakness** [弱] to **exalt strength** [强].

They **abandon lowliness** [卑] for **elevation** [高],
**forsake depletion** [损] for **fullness** [满],
**indulge excess** [过] and **create profligacy** [泰],
**release moderation** [和] to **pursue extravagance** [泰].

They **act with intent** [有为],
**discard frugality** [啬] to **spend wastefully** [施费].

Why is this so?
They **possess their bodies** [有其身] yet **forget the Dao/Way of life** [忘生之道].

「They are called the disciples of death.

Thus, the practitioners of **life mastery** [摄生], with their lofty and boundless Dao/Way, stand apart in grandness and transcend the mundane, soaring far beyond the world’s constraints. They do not cling to the **customs of the masses** [俗], nor are they bound by the **affairs of the world** [世]. They diminish their **form** [形] in the **boundless** [无境], and let their **spirit** [神] drift in the **void** [无内]. They do not regard life as gain, nor death as harm. Their **comprehensive cultivation** [兼施] knows no limits—all things, great or small, are seen as the self, with neither aversion nor attachment. Their **spirit and virtue/power** [精神隆盛] are vast and harmonious, their blessings and **virtue/power** [福德] converge naturally. The Dao/Way is their central sovereign, its radiance visible without. In accordance with **natural transformations** [自然之变], they respond effortlessly—nothing in heaven, earth, or all things can defeat them.

When they walk on land, **rhino-beasts and tigers** [兕虎] cannot harm them; when they enter battle, the **five weapons** [五兵] cannot wound them. No added strength can conquer them, nor can any thrown force subdue them—**their spirit and qi** [神气] are in perfect accord, and the intent to harm is already nullified within.

For those skilled in **life mastery** [摄生], their actions are such that, with no love or hate for all things, they view each thing as if it were their own body. Thus, all things respond in kind, returning affection without malice, as **natural law** [理数] must.

Like shadows following form, it is not by **skill or technique** [法术] that they manipulate form, but by its inherent nature.

Why is this so?
Because **sounds echo in response** [声响相应], and **things follow their kind** [物从其类]. **Rhino-beasts and tigers** [兕虎] cannot harm the **formless** [无形], and the **five weapons** [五兵] cannot strike the **void of substance** [无质]. The practitioners of **life mastery** [摄生] have already extinguished the **thief’s or harmer’s intent** [贼害之心] within, and the **forms of death and injury** [死伤之形] vanish without.

Thus, **tigers have no place to set their claws** [虎无所措其爪], and **weapons find no opening for their blades** [兵无所容其刃], for they possess **no ground of death** [无死地]—this truth is not hollow.

**Dao/Way generates brilliance** [道生章]
The **inherent nature** [禀] of things born from the Dao/Way,
The **virtue/power** [德] bestowed that grants life to all things.
The **forms** [物形] of all things vary in every direction,
The **fulfillment of effort** [势成] that completes their shapes.

Thus, all things attain life through this,
And those who **honor the Dao/Way and value virtue/power** [尊道贵德] are like **sages and worthies** [视宗正].
The Dao/Way is honored, virtue/power is valued—**grand and flourishing** [高大盛].
None can confer titles upon it, for its name is **constant naturalness** [常自然].
The Dao/Way’s **generation of life** [道生] leaves nothing unborn,
Its **virtue/power’s nurturing** [德畜] leaves nothing incomplete.
It **lengthens** [长] without fail,
It **nourishes** [育] without rest,
It **completes** [成] without end,
It **ripens** [熟] without error,
It **sustains** [养] without harm,
It **covers** [覆] without concealment.

To **give birth without possession** [生而不有] is to do so without **hoarding** [赀],
To **act without reliance** [为而不恃] is to do so without **intent** [所为].
To **lengthen without slaughter** [长而不宰] is to do so without **purpose** [以为].
This is called the **mysterious virtue/power** [玄德], which **virtue/power does not know** [德不知].

**Pointing to the return** [指归]:
The **sage’s wisdom** [圣知] unfolds—
Not from the **heavens and earth** [天下],
Nor by **earthly means** [地出],
But **inherent within the body** [内在於身],
And **manifest in all things** [外在於物].
Guided by **natural law** [自然], it permeates without limit.
Following **patterns and effects** [因循效象], it is inexhaustible.

Thus, the Dao/Way is **formless** [虚], virtue/power is **voidless** [无],
Yet they do not lose their **heart** [心].
Heaven is **exalted** [尊], earth is **lowly** [卑],
Yet they do not violate their **principles** [节].

Why?
Because **knowing arises from the void** [有知无],
And **human discernment follows things** [由人识物].
Things of the same **kind** [类], when **voidless** [无], give rise to **possession** [有];
The **formless** [虚] generates the **solid** [实].
To **perceive subtlety and know its manifestation** [见微知着],
To **observe beginnings and foresee endings** [观始睹卒],
Is not a matter of **clever skill** [巧能],
But the **natural workings of things** [自然之物], which the **sage follows** [圣人因之],
In **harmony with heaven** [与天周密].

Thus, **knowing the Dao/Way through its ultimate formlessness** [太虚之虚],
They **draw from nothingness** [无所不禀].
This is the **inherent nature of things** [物性].

**Understanding virtue/power through its supreme voidlessness** [至无之无],
They **bestow without limit** [无所不授].
This is the **granting of life** [授物命].

The Dao/Way **acts without possession** [无为之为],
Its **manifestation** [品] in all directions has no **beginning** [首].
To **act without possession** [为而不有].

Virtue/power **sets without attachment** [无设之设],
It **fulfills the forms of all things** [遂万物之形] without **doing** [事].
To **complete without claiming** [成功不居].

Thus, they can **refine life and destiny** [陶性命],
**Regulate feelings and thoughts** [治情意],
**Shape resolve and cravings** [造志欲],
And **transform all affairs** [化万事].

What are **life, nature, feelings, thoughts, resolve, and cravings** [性命情意志欲]?
Ask of the **differences among these six** [六者之差].

That which is **inherited from the Dao/Way** [所禀於道] and forms **body and shape** [成形体],
Varies in every direction—**all things and beings** [人物],
**Male and female** [男女], **sage’s contemplation and bold daring** [圣虑、勇怯],
**Small and great, long and short** [小大、修短],
**Kindness and meanness, greed and cruelty** [仁廉、贪酷],
**Strength and weakness, lightness and heaviness** [强弱、轻重],
**Sounds and colors, appearance and substance** [声色、状貌],
**Refinement and coarseness, high and low** [精粗、高下]—
This is called **nature** [性].
All this is **inherited from the Dao/Way** [禀於道],
Arises from within, and **never changes** [终焉不变].

That which is **bestowed by virtue/power** [所授於德],
Riches and poverty, **early death and longevity, suffering and joy** [夭寿苦乐],
Some encounters are **fitting**, others **unfitting** [有宜不宜]—
This is called **heavenly destiny** [天命].
All this is **received from virtue/power** [受於德],
Comes from without, and **progress or retreat is in my hands** [进退由我].

To **meet with rulers and parents** [遭遇君父],
The **movements of heaven and earth** [天地之动],
To **encounter fortune or misfortune** [逆顺昌衰],
To **face life or death** [存亡及我]—
This is called **encountered destiny** [遭命].
It is **fortuitous** [偶然], not **fixed** [非常定].

When **all things are arranged** [万物陈列],
And I **undertake affairs** [将有事],
To **deploy or abandon** [举错废置],
To **take or leave, approach or withdraw** [取舍去就],
When **auspicious or inauspicious events come** [吉凶来],
When **calamity or fortune arrives** [祸福至]—
This is called **following destiny** [随命].
It is **obtained by my actions** [随我所为].

To **move from nature and destiny** [因性而动],
To **interact with things and awaken** [接物感寤],
To **love or hate, like or dislike** [爱恶、好憎],
To **startle or fear, rejoice or anger** [惊恐、喜怒],
