To **grieve or delight, worry or rage** [悲乐、忧恚],
To **advance or retreat, take or give** [进退、取与]—
This is called **feelings** [情].
They arise from **nature** [性], and come **unconsciously** [不觉而至].

To **act from destiny** [因命而动],
To **generate thought and deliberation** [生思虑],
To **establish plans and strategies** [定计谋],
To **judge safety and peril** [决安危],
To **understand all affairs** [通万事],
To **discern right and wrong** [明是非],
To **differentiate the same and the different** [别同异]—
This is called **thought** [意].
It moves **along with destiny** [缘命], and is **by my doing** [由我所为].

To **stem from feelings and thoughts** [因於情意],
To **move outward and connect with things** [动而之外],
To **always find delight** [与物相连，常有所悦],
To **summon fortune or misfortune** [招麾祸福],
To **accomplish fame and achievement** [功名所遂]—
This is called **resolve** [志].
The **movement of nature and destiny** [性命之动] leads to **feelings and thoughts** [情意],
And from these, **resolve is strengthened** [因而自强].

To **align with nature and destiny** [顺性命],
To **fit with feelings and thoughts** [适情意],
To **be drawn by diverse kinds** [牵於殊类],
To **be bound by all affairs** [系於万事],
To **form attachments that are hard to untie** [结而难解]—
This is called **craving** [欲].
Though **craving arises from feelings and thoughts** [出乎情意],
It **exceeds nature and destiny** [侈於性命],
And **must not be indulged** [不可纵].

All these six—**nature, destiny, feelings, thoughts, resolve, and craving** [性命情意志欲]—
Are **rooted in virtue/power and the Dao/Way** [原道德],
And **thousandfold transformations** [千变万化] know no end.
Only those who **hear of virtue/power and the Dao/Way** [闻道德者] can follow their **principles** [则].

The **Dao/Way is the principle** [则], and **those who attain the principle** [得本者]
Move freely in **advance and retreat**, unshackled by **feelings and cravings** [情欲].

**Nature is refined, destiny is high** [性精命高],
It can be **transformed or altered** [可变可易].
**Nature is coarse, destiny is low** [性粗命下],
It can be **diminished or enhanced** [可损可益].
If one **grasps the root and principle** [得根本],
They are not **stuck in possession or void** [滞有无].

Thus, **heaven, earth, and all beings** [天地人物] contain **heart and core** [含心包核],
Belonging to their **kind** [有类].
They **obtain the Dao/Way to be born** [得道以生],
Yet the Dao/Way **does not possess their virtue/power** [而道不有其德].
The Dao/Way **generates life** [道生], yet **does not claim it** [未有].」

The **One** attained brings completion,
Yet the **One** does not seek its own fortune.
All things honor and revere it,
Cherish and worry over it,
Yet it never repays their virtue/power.
Attaining the completion of the **One**,
The **One** requires no thanks—
This is called *"when principle reaches its utmost, opposites vanish."*

Why is this so?
The **Dao/Way** is lofty and its virtue/power vast,
Deep beyond words—
Things cannot enrich it,
Titles cannot exalt it.
It acts without doing,
Yet all things act through it.
It is not forced by anything,
Yet nature remains ever spontaneous.

It acts without acting toward things,
Yet things act through it without contrivance—
Principle and law move as they must,
Not compelled by things to do so.

Thus, the **Dao/Way** as a thing:
Looked upon, it has no door,
Examined, it has no gate,
Probed, it has no form,
Mapped, it has no shape.
Mind cannot exhaust it,
Speech cannot convey it.
All things are born through it,
Yet it is not diminished by them.
All things return to it,
Yet it is not filled by them.

Above and below, it knows no end,
Broad and vast without boundary.
Ebbing and flowing, curving and bending—
Its measure cannot be fathomed.
It plays in the autumn hair’s breadth,
Yet is not deemed small;
It encompasses all heavens,
Yet is not deemed great.
Its radiance shines like emerald and purple,
Yet it does not alter its resolve.
In darkness and decay,
It does not change its nature—
This is called **constancy**.

It moves without exertion,
Holds no favorites.
It bestows nature and destiny,
Yet does nothing in particular.

Its virtue/power flows through all things,
Yet cannot be reclaimed;
Its grace binds and its blessings endure,
Yet cannot be returned.
**Dao/Way** and virtue/power lend and give birth,
Like the sound of a *tuóluò* flute—
Qi issues forth endlessly,
Never to be recovered.

It gazes upon all under heaven without depletion,
Achieves and completes without exhaustion.
Toward all things, does it merely give life?
It shapes them, establishes them, arranges them into ranks,
Stops them to perfect them,
Ends them to begin anew,
Leads them to follow or precede.

Like water to fish—
Life, form, beginning, and end,
Never parting for an instant.
It both follows and precedes,
With spirit dwelling within,
Great Harmony preserved.
The clear ascends to accumulate,
The turbid descends to congeal.
Heaven is round through it,
Earth is square through it.
Yin finds its yin,
Yang finds its yang.
Sun and moon shine through it,
Stars move through it.
The four seasons transform through it,
The Five Phases overcome one another through it.

Fire burns through it,
Water chills through it.
Grasses and trees bend through it,
Metals and stones harden through it.
Flavors are sweet or bitter through it,
Colors are dark or bright through it.
Sounds rise or fall through it,
Changes stretch or contract through it.
Mountains and hills stagnate through it,
Winds and rains move through it.
Scaled creatures swim through it,
Feathered creatures fly through it.
Beasts run through it,
Humans gain wisdom through it.
Diverse kinds and races all exist through it,
Yet perish when they oppose its transformations.

All heavens differ in form,
Waters and lands vary in shape,
Customs clash, benefits and harms diverge,
Appearance and desire are deceptive,
Intentions and cravings are incomprehensible.
Even yin and yang cannot reach them,
Sun and moon cannot illuminate them—
All begin and end through it.

Opening the mouth, stretching the eyes,
Bending, tilting, bowing, or rising—
In the space of a breath,
In the space of inhaling and exhaling,
Where spirit traverses,
Where mind and intention dwell,
Where love and attraction take hold,
Where male and female transform—
It guides all things,
Does all things,
Gives life without claiming reward,
Acts without demanding return,
Nurtures without possession.

All under heaven is bewildered,
None can know it.
Dark and silent, formless and empty,
Yet it gives birth and completes—
Not like the boundless void,
For long has humanity been deluded,
Thus they do not recognize it.

Some say:
**"Dao/Way** is the divine mystery of heaven and earth;
Heaven and earth are the manifestation of **Dao/Way**."

Others claim:
**"Dao/Way** is the function of heaven and earth,
Heaven and earth are the substance of **Dao/Way**."
This is the shortsightedness of a gnat in a jar,
The limited wisdom of lice in clothing—
Unfit to speak of the **Dao/Way**.

How may this be made clear?
**Dao/Way** encompasses all heavens.
Zhuangzi said:
*"Heaven and earth have their kinds,
Yet **Dao/Way** has no form.
Things with kinds all have limits,
Things without form know no end.*
To entrust the limited to the boundless
Is like grasses and trees torn from the earth,
Or stars torn from the sky—
Insufficient to illustrate it.

Yet to say otherwise
Is to fail to grasp
How having and not-having embrace,
How emptiness and reality contain each other—
Like the rind of a gourd,
Unaware of the tendrils’ neighboring growth,
Or lice hiding in fur,
Unaware of the multitude in the city.

Thus, beyond the cosmos yet within its domain,
Unconstrained by any prohibition,
Bound by no regulation—
Safety and peril, ebb and flow,
Know no inside or outside.
All follow the same wind,
Point in the same direction,
Harmonious and obedient to its decree,
Perfect and unblemished,
Without flaw or ruin.
Ten thousand blessings abound—
**Dao/Way** covers them all.
Its deeds are mysterious, its work hidden,
Unrevealed to the world.
All under heaven sees it not,
Yet it never ceases to act.

It responds without being seen—
If seen, it is not true.
Its constant speech never reaches,
Its extraordinary nature cannot be recognized.
This is called **mysterious virtue/power**,
Virtue/power that aids without end.

---
**The Beginning of All Under Heaven**
All under heaven has a **beginning**—
A **non-doing body** that is the mother of all things,
The root of ten thousand beings.
Having obtained its mother,
It holds to spontaneity—
Thus it knows its offspring:
All things arise without intervention.
Having known its offspring,
It never strays—
Thus it returns to its mother,
Reverting to its origin.
Death does not bring peril,
Life ends in tranquility.

Seal its senses—
Eyes and ears are darkened,
Its doors and openings are closed—
No speech all its life,
No toil or labor—
This is ease.

Open its senses—
Ears and eyes are sharp,
Its affairs are accomplished,
Its fame and deeds are manifest—
Yet its life is unsalvageable.

Seeing the small is called **clarity**—
Perceiving what has not yet sprouted.
Holding to softness is called **strength**—
Harmony as constancy.

Using its light—
Spirit moves outward,
Returning to its clarity—
Spirit moves inward.
No harm befalls the body—
This is not greatness,
But donning the **Dao/Way’s** ordinary garb,
Following its decrees.

---
**Pointing to the Return:**
The **Dao/Way** as a thing—
Formless, shapeless,
Without mind or intention,
Yet never forgets or ponders,
Without knowledge or awareness,
Without head or direction,
Without action or deed,
Empty, insubstantial, serene and still,
Vague, hazy, pure and tranquil.

「Its transformations unfold—
Change within the unchanging,
Motion within the still,
Returning to give birth to cover,
Covering to return to give birth,
Having to birth nothingness,
Nothingness to birth having,
Return and cover interwoven,
Naturally holding fast—
Acting without action, all things flourish,
Not acting yet all things succeed.

Thus, the **Dao/Way’s** embodiment of *wuwei* (無為),
Is the origin of heaven and earth.
So it is said, "Heaven and earth have a beginning."

*Wuwei* is subtle and profound,
Encompassing all in secrecy;
Smooth and tranquil, yet nothing escapes its sway.
Life and growth are keen and bright,
Skillful and discerning—
Reaching all corners, yet none remain untouched.
Therefore, it is said: "The origin of all things,
Is the mother of ten thousand affairs."
This is the mother of all under heaven.

The sage attains it,
And reverses with all things.
Having obtained its child,
Thus able to grasp the **Dao/Way’s** essence,
To penetrate heaven’s principles,
To birth as its origin,
To open the gate of affairs,
To harness all knowledge of ten thousand realms,
To exhaust the tongues of the multitude,
To exhaust the cunning of divergent schools,
To drain the arts of a hundred families.

All knowledge of ten thousand realms,
The arts of a hundred families,
All spring from the **Dao/Way**, hence called its child.
Attaining the **Dao/Way’s** perfect harmony,
Not only does one cultivate virtue alone,
But responds to every situation with effortless skill—
Wondrous uses without measure.
Without measure in its use,
It guides all things back to the **Dao/Way**,
Hence it is said: "Having known its child,
One again guards its mother."

Moreover, the **Dao/Way** adapts to human affairs,
Turning with the times’ transformations,
Nurturing and refining it,
Ending to begin anew,
Sudden in its changes,
Penetrating spirits, commanding ghosts,
Manifest in the formless,
No matter unaddressed,
Exhausting the inexhaustible,
Reaching the unreachable—
Yet through it all, one carves and refines,
Returning to guard its mother.

Return and guard its mother,
The root of all under heaven,
Roaming in the mysterious depths,
A lifetime without peril.
Perishing yet without peril.

Thus the sage can:
Plug his ears to preserve clarity,
Close his eyes to preserve insight,
Silence speech to preserve virtue,
Abandon deeds to preserve efficacy—
Hearing without listening aligns with heaven’s acuity,
Seeing without gazing aligns with heaven’s brilliance,
Transforming without words aligns with heaven’s **virtue/power** (德),
Acting without striving aligns with heaven’s function.

What is guarded is essential,
What is cultivated is thorough.
The **Dao/Way’s** luminous virtue is never obscured,
And heaven and earth’s concerns are fully realized.

Thus one can echo and shadow,
Illumine without end,
As the origin of blessings,
As the ancestor of transformations—
Flowing through all, permeating the great middle,
Things follow in accord, the world without toil.
The **Dao/Way’s** use is never exhausted,
Like echoes and shadows to form and sound—
Thus a lifetime without toil.

Therefore, straining eyes harms clarity,
Forcing ears harms acuity,
Hasty speech undermines virtue,
Cunning deceit ruins efficacy.
Thus, with mouth wide open,
Eyes and ears stretched taut,
Knowledge and perception arise,
All things multiply and thrive,
Stirring the heart, raising thoughts—
Fame and deeds are accomplished.
Fame and deeds accomplished,
Calamity arrives, blessings end,
Motion triggers the **Heavenly Net** (羅天網),
Stillness invites the **Earthly Retribution** (地殃),
Spirits and **Dao/Way** cannot aid,
Creation cannot sustain—
Common folk lose their lives,
States perish in ruin.

Opening its senses,
Accomplishing its affairs,
Not embodying the **Dao/Way** yet acting—
Thus its life is unsalvageable.

Hence the sage withdraws from deeds,
Abandons affairs,
Embodies the **Dao/Way’s** heart,
Follows **virtue/power** (德) with intention,
Unites the boundless mechanisms,
Holds the essentials of nature—
Soaring before the origin,
Gathering in the profound,
Clarity acts as if unheard,
Insight as if unseen,
Sprouts and seeds undisturbed,
The subtle threads uncut—
Brightly perceiving alone,
The changes of the formless,
Penetrating the unexpressed,
Reaching the limitless—
Not even the slightest evil can arise,
Not even the greatest calamity can approach.
Seeing the small is called **clarity**—
Thus evil ceases, good prevails.

Acting and refining,
Cutting off speech, extinguishing thought,
Accumulating softness, embodying weakness,
Returning to the state of no awareness—
Punishing violence, aiding the few,
Aligning with the divine transformations,
The unconquerable is conquered,
The unattainable is achieved,
Strength cannot be added,
All under heaven cannot scheme.
Holding to softness is called **strength**.

Governing people, managing things,
In harmony with yin and yang,
Internally using its light,
Yet externally causing no offense—
Clothing, food, tilling, and harvest,
Silk weaving with abundance,
Blessings accumulate, misfortunes dissolve,
People are provided, households are supported,
The heart does not bear the weight of seeking,
The humble do not aspire to the noble,
The poor do not envy the rich,
The refined honor simplicity,
Within and without, nothing is excessive—
Serving above, nourishing below,
Human ways fully realized.

Using its external light,
Returning to its internal **clarity**,
Returning to its internal **clarity**—
Spirit and insight are never depleted,
Stored like a coiled serpent, firmly held,
Daring not to call it wisdom.

---」

「Like the great rivers and seas sharing the same purpose as Heaven,
To extinguish the **Three Five**—
To harm them with affairs,
To fill and block them,
So they cannot be discerned.

As **malaria** and **deafness**,
In harmony with Heaven and Earth,
As **mysterious** and **silent**,
Exhausting the Dao,
Departing leaves no blame,
Defying calamities and ruining bandits,
Floating **virtue** laden with peace—
Nothing it cannot overcome.

Because it does not leave the body to suffer.

Thus, when a person enters the Dao,
The Dao also enters the person,
Our Dao merging within—
Submerged and unified as one.

Preserving stillness to attain **emptiness**,
I become the Dao’s dwelling,
With all things in their natural state,
Chaotic yet complete in every detail,
Returning to the origin, to the beginning—
The Dao covers me like a robe.

A robe—
Layer upon layer.

Merging with the **constant Dao** in **virtue/power**,
Like piling garments upon the body,
Hence it is said the Dao covers me,
This is the **constant Dao** that envelops me.

In the chapter *Conducting the Great Dao*:

It is I who, with knowledge and clarity,
Conduct myself in the Great Dao—
Refining the **constant Dao**,
Only fearing **Shi** lest I stumble and fall.

The Great Dao is vast and smooth,
Easy and level—
Yet people prefer narrow paths,
Delight in reckless action.

Morning is pristine, yet palaces are adorned with excess,
Fields are overgrown with weeds and pests,
Granaries are empty, agriculture neglected,
Garments flash with five colors,
Swords are worn for slaughter,
Feasts are indulged in gluttony and drunkenness,
Wealth is hoarded like mountains,
All treasures compared to a sovereign’s.

This is called **plundering, boasting, and hoarding**—
A perversion of the Dao,
A rebellion against Heaven.

**Pointing to return**:
The Dao’s **virtue/power** is not a matter of cleverness,
Thus it can mold Heaven and Earth,
Shape yin and yang,
And Heaven and Earth cannot deceive it.

Heaven and Earth do not rely on cleverness,
Thus they contain and release transformations,
Kill and give life to all beings,
And all things cannot escape them.

If the Dao **releases** and **returns** to cleverness,
Then the body cannot preserve itself,
And how could Heaven and Earth be shaped,
Or yin and yang be realized?

If Heaven and Earth **release** and **return** to cleverness,
Then the body cannot sustain itself,
And how could transformations be embraced,
Or all things be fully nurtured?

This so-called **naturalness**,
Like water naturally moistening below,
Fire naturally blazing upward—
Within their inherent nature,
It is not a matter of contrivance.

Thus, **emptiness** and **non-action**,
**non-knowledge** and **non-desire**—
The heart of **virtue/power** and the intent of Heaven and Earth.

**Clarity** and **stillness** mirroring the **form**,
**Non-action** responding to circumstances—
The movement of **virtue/power** and the transformation of Heaven and Earth.

**Virtue/power** responds to circumstances,
Heaven and Earth move and transform—
Like images within a mirror,
Echoes in empty space—
This is no difficult matter.

How does one know this?
Zhuangzi said:
*"What the Dao produces, Heaven nurtures,
Beginning without beginning,
Giving life without giving life,
Preserving without preserving,
Destroying without destroying.
That which has no beginning, no giving life,
No preserving, no destroying—
This is the origin of **virtue/power**.*

All these things,
Are the **verifications** of naturalness,
The **constants** of transformation.

Thus, when a person’s actions do not align with the Dao,
The Dao does not favor them;
When they do not align with **virtue/power**,
**Virtue/power** does not aid them;
When they do not align with Heaven,
Heaven does not shelter them;
When they do not align with Earth,
Earth does not bear them.

What the Dao does not favor,
What **virtue/power** does not aid,
What Heaven does not shelter,
What Earth does not bear—
This is where calamities linger,
And blessings never draw near.

People draw **qi** from **virtue/power**,
Take form from Heaven and Earth—
If their actions do not align with the Dao,
They naturally find no peace,
Thus blessings recede daily,
And misfortunes approach.

Therefore, the **mysterious sages** and **recluses**,
Bearing the Dao and embracing its **completeness**,
Lifting **insight** and grasping **clarity**,
Aligning with the Dao and honoring **virtue/power**,
Discarding cleverness and abandoning the body,
Grasping their resolve with dread,
Only fearing to stumble and fall.

Thus they strive for **cleverness** that is not clever,
Pursue **clarity** that is not clear,
Trust in softness and weakness,
Tilling the land for their sustenance,
Ever content with moderation,
Returning to the **nameless**,
Trembling with fear,
Lest they lose **naturalness**,
And their misfortunes extend to Heaven and Earth,
Affecting all people.

Those who, with knowledge and clarity,
Conduct themselves in the Great Dao—
Only fear **Shi**.

Thus auspicious responses and blessings arrive,
Like shadows following form,
Echoes answering sound,
Without expectation or prearrangement,
Arising as if born together—
Hence the Great Dao is vast and smooth,
Its transformation formless,
Like something distant yet near,
Like something dim yet bright.

Simple and vast without blemish,
Concise yet easy to follow,
Achieving success without contrivance,
Attaining blessings without effort—
Heaven and Earth follow it,
And all things come to life from it.

The Great Dao is vast and smooth.

Yet people turn away from it,
Using their cleverness,
Embracing deceit and neglecting the Dao,
Reversing Earth and defying Heaven,
Exalting knowledge and valuing cleverness,
Cheating spirits and mocking gods,
Adorning false governance with perversion,
Pursuing deceit while abandoning truth,
Inventing customs and altering institutions,
Creating affairs and accomplishing deeds.

People delight in narrow paths.

Palaces are grand, gates towering high,
Adorned with bizarre embellishments,
Layered with colorful patterns—
Cleverness as their foundation,
Cunning as their measure.

Morning is pristine, yet deception is their axe,
Falsehood is their adze—
Wielding schemes and manipulating numbers,
Weaving fine cloth while exploiting labor,
Neglecting fields, letting weeds and pests flourish,
Harvests failing, granaries empty.

Fields are overgrown, granaries are empty.

Garments flash with five colors,
Silks and brocades in dark yellows,
Fine linen and delicate embroidery,
Smooth as deer, radiant as phoenixes.

Wearing garments of five colors.

Sharp blades and sturdy armor,
Mighty crossbows and powerful bows,
Light chariots and swift steeds,
Many reckless and fierce warriors.

Wealth is heavy, status honored,
Power and influence prevail—
Slaughtering without restraint,
Subjugating the common folk,
Jealous of the upright, resentful of the generous,
Hating loyalty, poisoning trust,
Binding with evil, joining with falsehood,
Harming the good, nurturing enmity,
Valuing contention and martial prowess—
None they do not oppress,
Forcing borders to expand,
Ever plotting to assassinate rulers.

Wearing swords of slaughter.

Feasts overflow with five flavors,
Pests swarm in abundance,
Cutting into wombs, killing unborn—
A defiance of Heaven’s intent,
Ever drunk and gluttonous,
Taking without restraint.

Indulging in food and drink.

Hoarding gold and jade,
Piling wealth like mountains—
All treasures compared to a sovereign’s.»

Excess in wealth and goods.
Strange and wondrous comings and goings,
Honor and splendor radiant and bright,
Detached from the masses, severed from custom,
Standing alone in tumultuous times,
Praised as a great sage—
This is called **theft of glory**.

Exceeding the crowd in vice, great in evil,
Crimes heavy, calamities deep,
The virtuous father does not rear them,
The enlightened ruler does not employ them,
The Dao does not favor them,
The spirits do not dwell with them,
Heaven does not shelter them,
All things hold them in hatred.

If one is thus,
To lose them is to invite calamity,
To keep them is to invite ruin,
Their bodies unprotected,
Their misfortunes extending to descendants—
All through un-Dao ways.

**On Establishing Virtue Properly**
Those who establish well do not falter—
They stand firm through the Dao.
Those who embrace well do not slip—
They hold fast through virtue.
Their descendants’ sacrifices never cease—
The world knows no end.

Cultivated in the self, its virtue becomes true—
**Nurturing life and breath.**
Cultivated in the family, it governs kindness and abundance—
Its virtue overflows, benefiting kin.
Cultivated in the village, it orders roles and duties—
Its virtue endures, conquering all.
Cultivated in the state, it establishes laws and norms—
Its virtue flourishes, free from slander and treachery.
Cultivated in the world, it sets standards and models—
Its virtue is universal, all under heaven in service.

Thus, by observing the self, one knows other selves,
By observing the family, one knows other families,
By observing the village, one knows other villages,
By observing the state, one knows other states,
By observing the world, one knows the world—
Near and far revealed.

How do I know this to be true?
By seeking it within oneself.

**The Principle of Return:**
Between Heaven and Earth, vast and boundless,
Diverse winds and customs, myriad creatures great and small,
Endless transformations, benefits and harms deceitfully entwined—
Thus, the able cannot control the unable,
And the unable cannot act where the able cannot.

I act for the world, yet the world also acts for me.
When I and it meet, if I am few and it many,
To meet many with few—
The many grow secure, the few grow perilous.

Thus, if one establishes by strength, others will seize it;
If one establishes by cunning, others will counter it;
If one establishes by force, others will threaten it.
Only by doing nothing can one not be defeated.

How does this manifest?
Silent, yet seeking echoes—
Echoes do not answer me.
Trusting shadow to follow shade—
Shadow does not follow me.
Yet fearing echoes, I strike the bell—
Echoes answer louder than before.
Hating shadows, I stand in the sun—
Shadows cling to me more fiercely.

From this, it is clear:
Non-action cannot evade blessing,
Action cannot escape misfortune.

Thus, the sage abandons strength,
Abandons cunning,
Abandons knowledge,
Abandons virtue—
Establishes the Dao, embraces virtue,
Harbors essence, nurtures spirit,
Harmonizes the body, follows weakness,
Steps upon the Earth, bears Heaven.
**This is the unshaken foundation.**

Empty, still, and quiet,
As if absent yet present,
Inner and outer both silent,
Transforming in the Mysterious,
Doing nothing, yet nothing undone,
Returning to simplicity, embracing truth,
Without laws or measures,
Yet aligned with transformation.

**This is the unbroken embrace.**

Nurturing the small to sustain the great,
Tending the myriad people,
Ordering square and round, precedence and sequence,
Ever abiding with the body,
Upright in form, serene in spirit,
Transmitting lineage to descendants.
Descendants’ sacrifices never cease.

Virtue accumulates, transforming and flowing,
Endless, ebbing and swelling with Heaven.
Cultivated in the self, its virtue is true—
**Life’s vitality thrives, the body light and strong,**
Beauty enduring yet untamed.

Cultivated in the family,
Husbands trustworthy, wives chaste,
Fathers merciful, children filial,
Brothers obedient, younger siblings respectful,
Nine clans harmonious and affectionate,
Farming and silk-reeling timely,
Storehouses abundant,
Livestock thriving,
Affairs prosperous, wealth ever sufficient,
Neighbors envy their fortune.

Cultivated in the family, its virtue overflows.

Cultivated in the village,
Clear distinctions in governance,
Actions aligned with harmony,
Names and realities correct,
Black and white distinct,
Curved and straight in their nature,
Right and wrong self-evident,
No deceit arises,
Authority revered and displayed,
Orders enforced without obstruction,
Above transforming, below responding,
Public and private as father and child,
Respect and love sincere,
Superior and inferior in joy,
People united, officials without grievance,
Duties fulfilled, reputation honored,
Called *junzi*, virtue ever abundant,
Death not a peril.

Cultivated in the village, its virtue endures.

Cultivated in the state,
The ruler enlightened, ministers loyal,
No blocking of the worthy in court,
No jealousy of merit among scholars,
No obstruction of the upright by the crooked,
No slander harming the public,
Harmony and compliance above and below,
No grievances, officials delighted in their duties,
All affairs in natural order,
Distant peoples drawn in longing,
The world follows its wind,
The state rich, the people flourishing,
Borders secure without conquest,
Ancestral temples honored,
Altars and fields eternally at peace,
Yin and Yang eternally united,
No calamities arise,
All things bountiful and ripe,
The realm at great ease,
Neighbors entrust their lives,
Posterity thrives,
Virtue and Dao abundant,
Ever as Heaven’s constant.

Cultivated in the state, its virtue is exalted.

Cultivated in the world,
The ruler yin, ministers yang,
The ruler still, ministers active,
The ruler round, ministers square,
The ruler follows, ministers respond,
The ruler silent, ministers speak.
Upright and fair, harmonious and unified,
Easy and effortless, quiet and soundless,
Virtue spreads like whispers,
Spirit transmits like currents,
Movement without origin,
Transformation like Heaven,
Acting without action,
Achieving without doing,
Merit aligned with the Dao,
The world returns to truth,
No affairs, no worries,
Great Peace spontaneously arises.

Cultivated in the world, its virtue is universal.

Thus, my self is the measure of other selves,
My family the balance of other families,
My village the compass of other villages,
My state the standard of other states—
This is the meaning of:
Observing the self to know other selves,
Observing the family to know other families,
Observing the village to know other villages,
Observing the state to know other states,
Observing the world to know the world—
Near and far revealed.

The ruler is the vital core of the land;
The land is the form of the ruler.

Thus, the land and the ruler share prosperity and suffering,
Share corruption and rectitude.
When the people thrive, the land flourishes;
When the ruler is whole, the land is whole.
Families and states preserve each other,
Rulers sustain one another.
If one attains self-mastery, the land naturally follows.

Therefore, those who can know me know all;
Those who can govern me govern all;
What benefits me benefits all;
What suits me suits all.
What harms me yet benefits others—
The world knows none such.

This is the meaning of:
*"A single word sufficient for a lifetime’s practice—*
*Is it not perhaps the virtue of *rú*?"*

How do I know the world is thus?
It is by this.
It is by this.

---
**Volume Ten: *The Dao and Virtue Classic—Guidance on the True Path* (Attributed to Shùjùn Yán Zhūn, style name Jūn Píng, with annotations by *Gǔshénzǐ*)**

**Falsehood and Emotional Flux:**
*"False"* was originally *"do"* (作), corrected according to the *Mì Cè* text.
*"Lightly risking death"* was originally *"Lightly risking death as a friend"* (轻死与之友), per the *Mì Cè* text.
*"Harsh punishments"* was originally *"Harsh forms"* (刑原作"形"), corrected according to the *Yílán* text.
*"Cruelty"* was originally *"Brutal cruelty"* (惨毒), per the *Mì Cè* text.
*"Disturbing the cosmic order"* was originally *"Falling into the cosmic order"* (罹罗天纲), with *"罹"* (罹) corrected from the *Mì Cè* text.
*"Sustaining the people, providing for the family"* was originally *"Providing for the family, giving to others"* (人给家赠), with *"赡"* (赡) corrected according to the *Yílán* text.
*"The Dao and Virtue"* was originally *"Heaven"* (夫原作"天"), corrected according to the *Yílán* text.
*"Its virtue is true"*—these four characters were originally omitted, supplemented from the *Yílán* text.
*"Is it not perhaps the virtue of *rú*?"*—*"始"* (始) was originally *"doubt"* (殆), corrected according to the *Mì Cè* text.

**Chapter on the Profound Depth of Contained Virtue**

The profound depth of contained virtue—
Its body aligns with the Dao’s origin,
Like a babe in its tender, weak, and void state.

Venomous creatures do not sting,
Raptors do not clutch,
Fierce beasts do not seize,
Nor do they add harm—
Its bones are frail, its sinews soft,
Yet its grasp is firm, its hold unyielding.
It knows not the union of male and female,
Yet the Dao’s effortless transformation is complete—
Its essence is the most divine and luminous.

All day it wails, yet its throat never grows hoarse,
Its voice remains in perfect harmony—
The harmony of the Dao is its way.

To know harmony is to know the eternal Dao,
To know the eternal Dao is to be enlightened and discerning—
Life flourishes as a blessed, boundless day,
The heart directs the *qi* to become robust and unshakable—
When things grow strong, they turn decrepit and rigid,
This is called *not* aligning with the Dao—
A fate of calamity and ruin.
To stray from the Dao means an early end to one’s great destiny.

**Explanation of the Way:**
Virtue is void and boundless,
Divine luminosity is tranquil and profound—
Pure, still, and subtly vast,
The Great Harmony flows like water.
Listen to it, and it is silent and empty,
Observe it, and it is formless and easy.
Its limits are without end, its bounds without measure—
Heaven cannot enfold it,
Earth cannot contain it,
The compass cannot make it round,
The square cannot make it square,
Measure cannot measure it,
Yet scales cannot weigh it—
Gold and jade cannot shield it,
Water and fire cannot obstruct or destroy it,
All things fail to grasp it,
Misfortune cannot befall it.

How much more so for those who float and soar,
Who are pure and vast like the primordial chaos—
Their hearts have no dwelling,
Their forms no fixed abode.
Through natural refinement and reception,
They take form from the Ten Thousand Heavens,
All beings receive it—
Nourished and content,
Yet thought cannot grasp it,
Action cannot seize it—
The farther one seeks, the thinner it becomes,
The more one clutches, the more it eludes.
To grasp it is to be caught by it,
To let go is to be released by it.

Only those without desire
Make their bodies its dwelling,
Store it within their hearts—
Thus it is called *containing virtue*.

To align with virtue is to receive virtue—
The depth of contained virtue is profound.
Virtue in a person
Is like a parent’s love for their child—
For all beings, it is like pearls and jade compared to clay and lead.
Parents give birth to me, and this cannot be changed,
Pearls and jade nourish me, and this cannot be discarded.

Thus, the virtuous person
Values their body above all else,
Yet regards the world with lightness—
Like a benevolent father and filial child,
Who would not trade their love for wealth.
The one who cherishes their body
And holds all else in slight regard
Is like a wise merchant,
Who would not exchange pearls and jade for clay and lead.

Their lack of desire is not from hating wealth or loving ease—
The world’s treasures cannot please their heart.
Their embrace of emptiness is not from loving stillness or hating disturbance—
The world’s affairs are not worth their effort.

Why is this so?
Because they hold their own nature as weighty,
And the world as light.

They understand the distinction between weight and light,
They grasp the shifts between profit and harm—
Thus all things cannot enslave them,
Nor can the world deceive them.

Therefore, they do not seek stillness, yet stillness arises,
They do not seek harmony, yet harmony is born,
They do not rest their spirit, yet the spirit finds peace,
They do not cultivate harmony, yet the *qi* becomes balanced.

Thus, they do not listen, yet hear the soundless sound,
They do not look, yet see the formless form,
They do not think, yet discern right and wrong,
They do not ponder, yet reach the realm of unity.

Their spirit permeates Heaven and Earth,
Their virtue follows Yin and Yang—
They do not pray for blessings, yet Heaven and Earth protect them,
They do not shun misfortune, yet calamities and harm depart,
They do not execute, yet all under Heaven fears them,
They do not bestow, yet all under Heaven loves them.

They find joy in a full belly,
Delight in bowing and rising,
Eat coarse grasses yet find it savory,
Drink plain water yet find it sweet.

Beneath towering trees,
Their spirit remains whole,
Within rocky caves,
Their heart ever rejoices—
The poor find joy in their work,
The lowly forget their humility,
In destitution, they meet death with serenity,
In hardship, they forget all danger.
Their deeds match the Earth’s,
Their virtue aligns with Heaven’s—
They return to simplicity, embrace naturalness,
And are like infants once more.

The profound depth of contained virtue
Is likened to the babe in its cradle.

Thus, to establish the body as the foundation of the state,
And to take the babe as the model of governance,
Then the world will honor the Dao and revere virtue,
Each will cherish their own body,
Renown and power will become stains,
All things mere dust—
The greedy will flee titles,
The cruel will turn to benevolence,
Gathering softness and weakness,
Only virtue will be cultivated.

Yet those who create blessings and sow chaos—
How could this ever arise?

It is from aligning with virtue by nature,
No cause for its generation.

Alas, the Dao of Heaven and Earth—
Deep and distant, subtle and refined—
Few can recognize it,
Fewer still can follow it.
Wisdom and insight cannot grasp it,
Only the babe embodies it.

The babe’s nature mirrors virtue—
The babe knows yet does not speak,
Understands yet does not reveal,
Has power yet does not act,
Is skilled yet remains hidden—
Alive yet like death,
Fresh yet like decay—
Acting without action,
Matching the Dao in every detail.

Life that is not life,
A body that is not a body,
Use that is not use,
Hearing that is not hearing—
Without action or affairs,
Without intention or heart,
Not seeking virtue or spirit,
Not accumulating wisdom—
Neither thinking nor pondering,
Nor obstructed by barriers—
Their spirit does not stir,
Their clarity knows no bounds,
Soft yet void, still yet tranquil,
Their souls are at peace.

Joy without seeking joy,
Ease without desiring ease—
They live without wasting their spirit,
They die without lingering regrets.

Thus they can be enveloped by the Dao and contain virtue,
Align with Heaven and Earth—
Then bees and wasps, venomous creatures and snakes,
Will have no will to inflict their stings.
Raptors and fierce beasts
Will have no intent to seize or attack.

Venomous creatures do not sting,
Raptors do not clutch—
Because there is no place for death.
Bones frail, sinews soft,
Yet their grasp is firm and unyielding.
They see not male and female,
Yet Yin and Yang transform them.

Their spirit is full and complete,
All beings unite with them—
Their cries do not grow hoarse,
Their harmony can be called perfect.
Their actions and deeds
Align with the eternal Dao.

To know harmony is to know the eternal.
To hold fast and guard it
Is to be wise and enlightened—
To know the eternal is to be clear.

By nature, they flourish and grow—
When they move, all blessings gather.
Their hearts act in profound mystery,
Their *qi* flows, robust and unyielding—
The heart directs the *qi*, and this is called *strength*—
Without striving, they overcome all.

Without desire, their movements lose nothing.
Naturally open and free, all virtues sprout anew—
Heaven and Earth shower their favor,
While calamity and chaos fade away.

Yet why is this so?
Because they embrace virtue and harmony of spirit,
And preserve the innocence of youth.

When knowledge dawns, they abandon unity for duality,
Discard obscurity for clarity—
Their bodies adorned, their virtue erodes,
The more they know, the deeper their confusion grows.

Thus, they prize the world yet neglect their spirit,
Value fame and power yet scorn their own bodies,
Overthink and overplan, scattering their spirit’s essence,
Rejecting softness, abandoning weakness,
Forcing progress toward rigidity,
Falling into greed, drowning in the pursuit of life,
Opening themselves to peril while blocking all safety.

When strength peaks, decay begins.
Thus, blessings as vast as Heaven and Earth—
You see them yet cannot grasp them;
Disaster strikes like thunder—
You hear it yet cannot avoid it.

They give without receiving,
Daily inviting ruin.
This is called *not aligning with the Dao*.

Act and you reach exhaustion,
Strive and you court destruction—
Cultivating the self, loving the nation,
Yet such devotion brings misfortune.

Offer sacrifices, and Heaven and Earth turn against you;
Pray to spirits, and the gods abandon you.
No fault of fate—
The consequences of actions unfold as they must.

The wise do not speak of their virtue—
The wise do not speak lest they lose focus,
Those who speak do not know—
And lose their lives.

---

To block the senses, dull the ears and eyes,
To close the mouth and door, speak not at all.
To blunt the sharpness of purpose and its direction,
To dissolve the anger of the heart and its thoughts,
To smooth the brightness of appearance without strangeness,
To blend with common garb, unmarked by eccentricity—
This is called *playing with the Dao*, aligning with the mundane.

They cannot be drawn close by love nor pushed away by neglect,
They cannot be gained by benefit nor lost by harm,
They cannot be honored by rank nor humbled by disgrace,
Yet they stand as the most noble and revered under Heaven and Earth.

**Key Principle:**
The Dao has no fixed manifestation,
Virtue no fixed direction,
The spirit no fixed form,
Harmony no fixed appearance—
You gaze upon it yet cannot see,
You listen to it yet cannot hear,
It cannot be foreseen nor touched.

Thus, those who attain the Dao
Perceive it alone, hear it alone,
Act upon it alone, and abide by it alone.

A father cannot pass it to his son,
A subject cannot bestow it upon his lord,
Yet as a mother recognizes her child,
Or a younger brother his elder—
So too, the child recognizes the mother.

This recognition is natural,
Yet its reason cannot be articulated.

The five flavors are in the mouth,
The five tones in the ear—
Yet what is sweet is not sweet,
What is bitter is not bitter,
What is *shang* is not *shang*,
What is *yu* is not *yu*—
Yet the cook Yi and the musician Jiang could distinguish them.

Yet their means of distinction—
The mouth could not speak of it.

Thus, the saying: *"Those who speak do not know, those who know do not speak."*

Hence, the form without form,
Can be seen yet not seen;
The image without image,
Can be imitated yet not declared;
The action without action,
Can be followed yet not described;
The use without use,
Can be practiced yet not transmitted.

Therefore, those who attain the Dao
See it as a child recognizes its parent,
Tread it like the earth,
Wear it like the sky,
Encase it as clothing,
Embody it like the self,
Act with it in rise and fall,
React to external stimuli as if in water,
Bend with the flexing of fortune,
Yet remain steadfast in their own spirit.

Their spirit wanders with transformation,
Their resolve moves with virtue,
Their wisdom acts inwardly,
Yet outwardly they seem deaf and blind.
Their thoughts arise in mystery,
Their demeanor seems mad.

Thus, their mouth cannot speak,
Nor can their intent be made clear—
Like dreaming of being a king,
Standing on the brink of peril,
Joy and sorrow reversed,
The heart alone knows—
Yet upon waking, they cannot convey it to another.

Those who stray from the Dao are not so.
They see only the exterior, not the interior,
Follow the current, yet grasp not the source,
Hold the end, yet exhaust not the root.
They affirm what is not affirmed,
Deny what is not denied.
The superficiality of things,
Is what they affirm as true.

The fundamental truth of the Dao,
Cannot be comprehended by such superficiality.

Thus, the Dao lies in externals,
Not in the self—
The central ruler is undecided,
His defenses are not steadfast,
The heart harbors doubts, the will wavers,
Emotions cling to things,
Wisdom is flashy,
Falsity is mistaken for truth,
He oscillates between affirmation and negation,
Between existence and non-existence,
Harmonious *qi* is easily disturbed—
Like illness in a man,
Vitality leaks, spirit escapes,
He loves speech yet hates silence.
When he speaks, his heart is troubled,
His resolve is distracted,
His wisdom is all outward,
His spirit departs.

His inner voice is spent,
Yet his outer words overflow,
His virtue and power scatter daily,
His self grows ever more distant.
The more he speaks, the less he understands his own perfection,
The more he acts, the less he knows his own virtue.

Thus, those who speak
Are the essentials of opposing the Dao,
The means of straying from virtue,
The craftsmen of defying Heaven,
The instruments of overturning Earth.

Therefore, those who attain the Dao
Diminish their hearing, discard their brightness,
Do not see, do not listen,
As if without sight or sound,
Close their mouths, seal their tongues,
As if they know not speech.

Block their senses,
Close their doors.
Blunt their sharpness,
Release their attachments,
Their will guards nothing,
Their form seems void.

Dissolve their thoughts,
Scatter their worries,
Seem to know nothing,
Yet hide as if alone in existence.
Blunt their sharpness,
Dissolve their anger.

Extinguish disaster at its root,
Return to the *Tai Su* (Great Primordial),
Their appearance is unchanged,
Their dress is unmarked,
They follow Heaven and Earth,
Blend with the common in transformation,
Plunge deep into the Great Dao,
Wander with virtue.

Without words to speak of speech,
Without action to speak of action,
They govern themselves with clarity and stillness,
Respond to the times with harmony and balance,
Merge with the world in undifferentiated chaos,
Align with the common in *playing with the Dao*.

They smooth their brightness,
Blend with the dust.
Seizing the root of all things,
Grasping the foundation of all affairs,
They alone differ from the crowd—
Yet the world knows them not.

They drift through the thresholds of closeness and distance,
Soar through the gates of gain and harm,
Float in the wilds of honor and disgrace,
Steadfastly guard their own spirit,
Vanish into the realm of the formless,
Roam in the land of abandon.

Poverty and lowliness do not shame them,
Wealth and nobility do not flatter them—
They hide when they wish to hide,
They reveal when they wish to reveal.
Even *yin* and *yang* cannot harm or benefit them,
Nor can rulers obscure their clarity.

This is called *playing with the Dao*.
Thus, they cannot be drawn close nor distanced.

They stand unmatched, alone,
Distinct without peer—
Sounds and colors cannot please them,
The five flavors cannot sweeten them,
Ten thousand things cannot contend with them,
Wisdom and strength cannot dispute them.

Without taking nor giving,
Without gaining nor losing,
They close their doors, shut their gates,
Sever the ends, extinguish the threads,
Their spirit and clarity are self-made,
The Dao is their central ruler—
Their movement aligns with transformation,
Their stillness harmonizes with the natural.
When they follow the natural order, they endure.

Abandoned and unrestrained,
They have no fixed form,
No one can precede or follow them—
Thus, those who love them cannot approach,
Those who hate them cannot distance,
Rewards cannot be added,
Taxes cannot be taken,
Rank and honor cannot be elevated,
Poverty and lowliness cannot be imposed.

They have no need of all things,
Thus all things cannot enslave them.
They take no possession of the world,
Thus the world cannot possess them.

This is how they become noble under Heaven.

**The Methods:**
To govern the nation with uprightness and loyalty,
To employ the Dao in warfare with cunning and strategy,
To take the world without action, relying on natural order.

How do I know this is so?
I know it from my own self.

The world abounds with prohibitions, taboos, shame, and contempt for what is ugly and coarse,
Yet the people grow ever poorer, their wealth ever fewer.

When the people are skilled in sharp tools and clever stratagems,
The state becomes increasingly chaotic and deceitful.

Men rely on artifice and elaborate deception,
And strange things proliferate without end.

When laws and decrees are made ever more explicit and traps set ever tighter,
Thieves and bandits multiply, their violence and rebellion increasing.

The Sage’s words declare the **true method of governance**:
If I do not rule with **non-action** (*wuwei*), the people will not transform themselves,
Yet they will gather in harmony and unity.
If I do not govern with **non-interference** (*wushi*), the people will not enrich themselves,
Yet they will have no cravings.
If I favor **stillness** and rule with emptiness and tranquility,
The people will naturally align with proper principle and order.
If I suppress desire and govern by contentment,
The people will return to simplicity and abandon ornamentation.

When governance is **obscured** and **obscured** (*mènmèn*), lacking virtue and power (*fude*),
The people are **docile** and **docile** (*pièpiè*), loyal and steadfast.
When governance is **scrutinizing** and **scrutinizing** (*cháchá*), virtue and power clear,
The people are **cunning** and **cunning** (*quēquē*), knowing how to scheme and grow.

Calamity arises from fortune’s reliance—fortune leans upon calamity to complete it,
Fortune hides within calamity’s guise—calamity lurks to fulfill it.
Who knows where their extremes begin, with no discernible threads?

If there is no **uprightness** (*zhèng*), no **loyalty** (*xìn*) will endure.
**Uprightness** (*zhèng*) inverted becomes **cunning** (*qí*), **cleverness** (*zhì*), and **deceit** (*zhà*) in action.
**Goodness** (*shàn*) inverted becomes **evil** (*yāo*), and **evil omens** (*yāo xiáng*) follow.

Men have long strayed from what is proper and constant—
The source of their prolonged confusion.

**Key Principle**:
The **emotion of virtue** (*dàoqíng*) is constant—**uprightness** (*zhèng*) and **loyalty** (*xìn*) are the norm.
Change and movement, stillness and action—
One arises, the other vanishes.

The **covering** (*fù*) of Heaven and Earth,
The **threads** (*jī*) and **patterns** (*gāng*) of yin and yang,
The **records** (*jì*) and **guidelines** (*lǐ*) of sun and moon,
Nurturing all living beings—
Those who oppose it perish, those who follow it thrive.

Thus, the **Dao/Way** of Heaven and Earth,
Is one yin and one yang,
**Yang-qi** (*yángqì*) governs **virtue/power** (*dé*),
**Yin-qi** (*yīnqì*) governs **punishment** (*xíng*),
Punishment and virtue are contrary,
Yet harmony lies at the center.

Spring brings forth, summer grows,
Autumn harvests, winter conceals—
Ending to begin anew,
Decaying yet rising again,
Yang reaches its end and turns to yin,
Yin reaches its end and turns to yang,
Yin and yang in opposition,
Extending to infinity.

Thus, the **Dao/Way** of kings and the conduct of men,
Is one soft and one hard,
One civil and one martial,
With **central uprightness** (*zhōngzhèng*) as the guiding thread—
Hardness and softness in contrast,
War and virtue intertwined,
War turns to virtue,
Virtue turns to war,
War and virtue safeguarding each other,
Law at the center,
**Numbers** (*shù*) and **principles** (*fǎ*) in harmony,
Thus all can flow freely.

Therefore, the **enlightened kings** and **sage rulers**,
Reduce their desires to empty their minds,
Empty their minds to calm their spirits,
Calm their spirits to grasp the **Dao/Way**,
Gain the **Dao/Way** to rectify their hearts,
Rectify their hearts to cultivate their bodies,
Cultivate their bodies to order their households,
Order their households to establish laws,
Establish laws to clarify names,
Clarify names to govern the state.

This is how they govern the state with **uprightness**.

When the state is **upright** (*zhèngguó*), its **records** (*jì*) are firm,
Its principles clear and discerned,
From the **roots** (*yuán*) to the **origins** (*běn*),
Drawing connections left and right,
Aligning ranks front and back,
Things return to their proper places—
Clarifying names to **cover** reality,
Verifying reality to **supervise** names.

One name, one reality,
Balanced and thorough,
Square and round, straight and curved,
None can stray—
Rewards and punishments applied,
Neither **excessive** (*yáng*) nor **stunted** (*suō*).
Names and reality,
Like moon and sun,
One name **upright** brings prosperity to the state,
One name **deceitful** brings enslavement to the state.

The **secrets** (*mì*) of nurturing the state,
Lie in having no fixed course—
Bending and extending, giving and taking,
All in accordance with the times.
Following disorder, relying on law,
Encountering rebellion, using war,
Guarding peace with the **Dao/Way**,
Embodying **virtue/power** as the norm,
Great and small states meet—
With **uprightness** as their mutual expectation.

If they stray from **uprightness**, transform them,
If they do not comply, restrain them,
If they do not cease, regulate them,
If they do not submit, strike them.

**Understanding** the great state’s **coordination** (*xié*) with the small,
They dare not lightly use war,
Thus they first employ **transformation** and **restraint**,
Only when compliance fails do they resort to regulation and punishment.

If a small state is **pressed** between great states,
Facing a ruler without the **Dao/Way**,
And **uprightness** cannot prevail,
Then leave it—
If leaving is impossible, cede land to it—
If ceding land is impossible, lead the people to flee—
If fleeing is impossible, take up the staff and depart—
If departing is impossible, calamity will reach all the people,
And disaster will fall upon me—
Thus, I must **devise plans** and **scheme**,
For this is where **contention** arises,
And war is born.

I wish to **select generals** and **train soldiers**,
Sharpen arms and fortify defenses,
Stockpile grain and raise ramparts,
Camp and defend myself—
Yet the people suffer exhaustion,
The state becomes hollowed out—
This is how **war** is **initiated**,
And **uprightness** is **invoked**.

If I enter with **uprightness**,
Yet I am few while they are many,
I am weak while they are strong—
Like an egg thrown upon a stone,
I will be the enemy’s victim,
Suffering calamity—
The armies must surely fail,
Soldiers die in wounds,
The **Heavenly intent** (*tiānxīn*) will not be fulfilled,
The ancestral temples will perish—
Below, I lament the people’s fate,
Above, I fear the **heart of Heaven and Earth** (*tiāndìxīn*)—
This is how **strategy** (*quán*) is **activated**,
And **deceit** (*qí*) is **deployed**.

Thus, I **establish** the **plan of opposition** (*fǎnwéng*) and **attraction** (*fùlái*),
Open the **hearts of the people**,
Stimulate the **schemes of the feudal lords**,
Reveal my **virtue/power’s** (*dàodé*) **blessings**,
Illustrate the **assistance of Heaven and Earth**—
To **unify** the hearts of the four seas,
To **harmonize** the intentions of all states.

The people respond to me like echoes,
Neighboring states follow me like shadows,
Birds and beasts take flight with me—
This is how **plans** are **utilized**,
And **deceit** is **executed**.

**Deceit** is **strategy**—
When a small state is **pressed** between great states,
And matters of fleeing or retreat arise,
War cannot be avoided—
Thus **strategy** and **deceit** are **employed**.

**Understanding** that war is an **omen of misfortune**,
Used only when there is no alternative—
I **activate** schemes and **plans**,
To **align** with the people’s expectations—
Heaven and Earth, birds and beasts,
Assist me as my **fortified city** (*chéng*—*cf.* 以浑四海之心，同万国之意，天地鸟兽助我为城),
Thus it is said: *"Employing **deceit** in war."*

Above, **aligning** with the **intention of virtue**,
Below, **harmonizing** with the **heart of Heaven and Earth**,
In **danger**, ensuring **safety**,
In **harm**, safeguarding **benefit**—
Treating the people as one’s own body,
Embodying the **formless form** (*wúxíng zhī xíng*),
Dwelling in the **Great Yin** (*Tài Yīn*),
**Issuing** the **action of non-action** (*wúwéi zhī wéi*),
**Displaying** the **soundless sound** (*wúshēng zhī shēng*),
Distinguishing the **crimes of extinguishing transformation** (*mièhuà zhī zuì*),
Revealing the **labors of defying Heaven** (*nìtiān zhī gōng*),
Manifesting what **Heaven** bestows,
Showing what **Earth** produces.

There are names without reality,
There are realities without names,
Names and reality **contradict**—
Sometimes **upright**, sometimes **tilted**,
Sometimes **flexible**, sometimes **rigid**,
Sometimes **contrary**—
Yet all **converge** in the **mysterious** (*míng*).

**Understanding** the **virtue/power’s** (*dàodé*) **effects**,
Revealing the **transgressions of rebellion** (*bó nì*),
Sometimes **contradicting** names and reality
To **flexibly align** with the **Dao/Way**.

The calamities of Heaven arise spontaneously,
The portents and misfortunes emerge naturally—
Severing father and son,
Cutting off brothers,
Slaying their valiant generals,
Beheading their loyal ministers,
So that all under Heaven harbor resentment,
None sharing a single heart.
Standing alone and unyielding,
Receiving Heaven’s decree of war,
Victory brings great joy,
And the Four Seas find peace—
This is the **highest** use of the **unconventional** (*qí*).

First employing the **Dao/Way**,
Only when it is not followed do the calamities arise—
Thus it is the **highest**.

Soothing the anger of the world,
Gathering those skilled in the **unconventional**,
Ears attuned to distant whispers,
Eyes scanning the horizon,
Scholars roaming freely,
Forming alliances and bonds of kinship,
Life and death transform strangely,
Following the **Dao/Way** to respond to deceit.

Adorning authority and nurturing influence,
To deceive the people with substance;
Spreading rumors and fabricating schemes,
To confuse the enemy;
Using humble words to subdue the lowly,
To close the mind of their lord;
Offering light tasks with heavy rewards,
To open the hearts of their ministers.

When rifts form between lord and subject,
Manipulating their spirits,
Actions concealed in darkness,
Power shifting in subtlety,
Suspending their fate,
Exploiting their vulnerabilities,
Driving the enemy to madness and confusion,
So they cannot act—
Advancing or retreating with the times,
No fixed rituals,
Not striking yet the enemy surrenders,
Not fighting yet the enemy falters,
Overthrowing their lord without harming their ministers,
Slaying their generals without touching their troops,
Victory brings the people’s joy,
The feudal lords fear them—
This is the **second** use of the **unconventional**.

First devising strategies,
Later securing their fate—
Thus it is the **second**.

Controlling the terrain,
Mastering their lords and ministers,
Offering low status with heavy rewards,
To pacify their outward appearance,
Spreading covert schemes,
To sow discord among their kin,
Deceit comes from them,
The **Dao/Way** arises from this—
Granting cities to seal generals,
Joining states to reward deceit.

Deceit arrives like a specter,
Plots unfold like divine foresight,
Strategies unmeasured,
Unconventional shifts endless,
Dividing their strength,
Sowing doubt in their hearts,
As if rising from the earth,
As if born of Heaven,
Severing their inner circle,
Scattering their alliances,
Raising influence and generating change,
To determine their fate,
Blocking their schemes,
So they cannot trust.

Breaking their strong supporters,
To isolate their resolve,
Exploiting their form to ensure victory,
Like an endless ring,
Striking at the opportune moment,
Harmony as its constant,
Attacking their vulnerabilities,
In stillness, cutting their supplies.

Stripping them of resources,
Starving and parching them,
Burdening them with weight,
Drowning them in fire,
Exhausting them with labor,
Freezing and scorching them,
Luring them with profit,
Maddening them with confusion,
Driving them to desperation,
Pressing them to the brink.

Striking from high to low,
Using many to overcome few,
Strengthening ranks and divisions,
Officers and troops aligned,
The high protecting the low,
The low aiding the high,
The three armies united,
Bound as father and son.

**Unconventional** formations merge and split,
Hidden and concealed in layers.
Camps before, supplies behind,
Overwhelming the left, routing the right,
Dazzling with banners and drums,
Confounding with music and war cries,
Advancing like surging waves,
Retreating like wind and rain,
Striking like a collapse,
Clashing like a tiger—
Defenses unbreakable,
Offensives unyielding,
Victory brings awe,
All under Heaven trembles—
This is the **lowest** use of the **unconventional**.

Employing force first,
Only then determining their fate—
Thus it is the **lowest**.

When chaos and disorder cease,
All things flourish in peace,
Heaven’s will is fulfilled,
The world rejoices—
Concealing the **unconventional**, diminishing cleverness,
Prioritizing loyalty and sincerity,
Cultivating stillness and simplicity,
Withdrawing from affairs, halting speech.

Though skilled in unconventional victory,
Unclear in **Dao/Way** and **virtue/power**,
Fearful that affairs will shift and change,
Corrupting purity, scattering simplicity—
Thus halting speech.

Why is this so?
**Dao/Way** and **virtue/power** transform endlessly,
All things have high and low,
Directions diverge,
Paths intertwine—
Some turn west, some east,
Each follows its nature,
To sustain its life.

The virtuous thrive through goodness,
The wicked spread through evil,
The sincere shine through truth,
The deceitful mask with falsity—
Each displays their wisdom,
To avoid calamity and ruin.

Seeking without fulfillment,
The wise feign cunning;
Laboring without rest,
The loyal turn deceitful;
Oppressed and tormented,
The faithful spread lies;
Driven to ruin without end,
The worthy do not transform.

Thus when the ruler favors knowledge, the people deceive;
When the ruler favors profit, the people suffer;
When the ruler favors rewards, the people grow weary;
When the ruler favors punishment, the people resent.

Why?
Affairs originate with the ruler,
Actions rest with the ministers;
Rewards come from the ruler,
Wealth comes from the people;
Laws come from the ruler,
Obedience rests with the ministers.
When the ruler desires,
All under Heaven follows the wind.

All affairs stem from the ruler,
The ruler is the source of transformation.
If the ruler does not conceal their schemes,
They revert to the **Dao/Way**.

Though clever and wise in strategy,
It is not as effective as acting without thought.
Thus governing with public-mindedness
Is not as harmonious as the great unity of non-action;
Seeking to curb excess through prohibition
Is not as effective as loyalty born of no desire;
Guiding through measured anger
Is not as fruitful as the merit of non-action;
Balancing thought with **virtue/power**
Is not as vast as the boundless flow of inaction;
Mastering the arts of divination and omens
Is not as beneficial as nurturing a world without ailment;
Wielding the strategies of the Yellow Emperor and Duke Zhou,
Or grasping the essentials of Sunzi and Wu Qi,
Is not as profound as letting all under Heaven
Refrain from exerting cleverness or strength.

Thus what **Dao/Way** and **virtue/power** produce,
Love cannot profit from;
What Heaven and Earth complete,
Action cannot achieve.

Small acts of love and gain
Ultimately defy the great **Dao/Way** of Heaven.
Only those without love can bring profit,
Only those without action can fulfill.
Thus the enlightened kings and sage rulers
Have no desires, no seeking,
No creation, no contrivance,
No burdens, no formalities—
Returning to origins, embracing simplicity,
All under Heaven finds peace.

Taking the realm through inaction—
How is this made clear?
Zhuangzi said:
*"To bring fortune and benefit,
To achieve success and complete affairs,
To prepare all things and fulfill their use,
To enrich people greatly—
Then all under Heaven indulges in extravagance,
Wealth and goods are insufficient,
The people grow ever more depraved.
Fortune fills the mountains and marshes,
Gold and jade pile up,
Yet the state grows ever less secure,
The people gain less benefit.
Adorning cleverness while appearing foolish,
Using deceit to manipulate,
Guarding against licentiousness and lust,
The paths of deceit and falsity grow dense,
Distinguishing same from different,
The shifts of right and wrong multiply—
Then the state grows dim,
And governance decays."*

The world fears taboos,
Yet the people grow ever poorer.
The more sharp tools they possess,
The more the state descends into chaos.

Crafting schemes and perfecting arts,
Carving and embellishing with ornament,
Strange transformations and monstrous novelty—
To exalt those of virtue,
To distinguish high and low.

Artifice multiplies,
Talents flourish ever more bizarre,
Rewards are swift and deep,
Punishments harsh and laws severe,
Piercing flesh and severing limbs,
Distant kin grow estranged, near kin grow discordant,
Guilt leads to utter annihilation,
Reward leads to knighthood and lordship,
Earth and Heaven tremble—
Yet thieves and bandits multiply.

The people grow skilled in strange cleverness,
Strange things multiply,
Laws and decrees grow ever more elaborate—
Thieves and bandits grow ever more numerous.

Thus the Sage’s words declare:
*"I act with non-action, yet the people transform themselves.
Why so?*
The ruler is the heart of all under Heaven.
Qi responds to sensation, the body follows its impulse,
The heart moves, the body obeys,
Sounds echo in resonance, forms shadow in pursuit—
Not enough to illustrate the point.

Therefore, if the ruler truly practices non-action,
Then the hearts of all under Heaven have no direction,
Enveloped by the Dao, containing virtue,
Without thought nor desire,
Without orders nor laws,
The people transform themselves of their own accord.
I act with non-action, yet the people transform themselves.

If the ruler truly practices the affairs of non-affairs,
Then all under Heaven lacks effect nor form,
Lacks knowledge nor perception,
No rewards nor gifts given,
The people grow rich of their own accord.
I act with non-affairs, yet the people grow rich.

If the ruler truly practices the stillness of non-stillness,
And the joy of non-clearance,
Then all under Heaven does not study nor inquire,
Hears nothing nor sees nothing,
Has no punishments nor laws,
The people align themselves naturally.
I love stillness, yet the people align themselves.

If the ruler truly practices the desires of non-desire,
Then the hearts of all under Heaven grow empty and their wills level,
Great bodies and small things,
Action yet returning to cessation,
Stillness yet returning to sufficiency—
Without constraint nor regulation,
The people return to simplicity.
I act with non-desire, yet the people return to simplicity.*

Thus, when the ruler’s governance is correct,
There is no filial piety nor benevolence,
No giving nor bestowing,
Yet the people are drawn and swayed,
Mute and docile,
Their likes and dislikes indistinguishable,
Their right and wrong undiscerned—
Thus they obtain what they desire,
And their lives are preserved whole.
His governance is stifling,
And his people are docile.

When the ruler’s governance is probing,
Bestowing virtue and spreading benefit,
Making distinctions clear and keen,
The people are bright and discerning,
All know of calamity and fortune.
Filial piety and brotherly respect,
Benevolence and righteousness,
All affairs are differentiated—
Yet the wise are obscured and the foolish prevail.
His governance is probing,
And his people are obscured.

Thus, he loses what he relies upon,
And his life is cut short by Heaven.
Fortune arises from calamity,
Calamity arises from fortune—
Fortune and calamity,
Share the same source yet different realms,
Both perish together, both endure together,
Different in nature yet the same in appearance,
Following each other in and out,
Same in origin yet different in end.
Without the Sage,
None can grasp them alone.
Fortune and calamity,
Depend upon each other,
Lie in wait for one another.

Thus, to abandon fortune is to abandon calamity,
To abandon calamity is to abandon fortune—
Fortune without fortune,
The most subtle and profound,
Yet all under Heaven loves to know,
None can exhaust its depths.
Who knows its ultimate extent?

Only the non-acting can follow its natural course,
Standing correct between calamity and fortune,
Overcoming all without effort.
This is the true correctness.
To lose correctness is to give rise to strangeness,
Strangeness arises and the people are bewildered,
Good men become malevolent,
Right and wrong invert.

Correctness becomes strangeness,
Goodness becomes malevolence.
All under Heaven is deeply confused and cannot return.

The Dao is very easy to follow,
Yet people’s confusion endures long—
Thus it cannot be recovered.

Rectangular yet not cutting,
Sharp yet not harming,
Straight yet not overbearing,
Bright yet not dazzling.

To govern people and harmonize Heaven for living—
Nothing surpasses frugality and non-action.

Only frugality,
Thus early service without prohibitions.
Accumulating virtue in subtle profundity,
Then there is nothing it cannot overcome,
Nothing it cannot conquer.
None know its ultimate transformation—
Tangtang, it can make a state,
It can make a sovereign king.
The mother of states is frugality,
It can endure long and move with difficulty.

Deep roots and firm stems,
Spirit concealed,
Long life and enduring vision,
The body preserved whole.

Pointing back:
The Dao has nothing it does not possess,
Yet does not give or withhold—
Thus all things exist.
It lacks no power,
Yet does not act or kill—
Thus all things flourish.
How can this be made clear?

The Dao is formless yet all things have form,
It lacks state nor appearance yet all things are square or round,
Silent yet all things have sound.
From this perspective,
The Dao does not give nor withhold,
Yet all things exist;
It does not act nor slaughter,
Yet all things flourish.
Flourishing arises from non-flourishing,
Existence arises from non-existence—
This is clear.
The Dao can preserve in non-preservation,
Flourish in non-flourishing.

Some say:
*"The Dao is formless and soundless,
Yet does not give nor withhold—
How can it flourish in non-flourishing,
Preserve in non-preservation?"*

The Sage discerns each thing in its natural state,
Each thing preserves its own Dao—
This is called recognizing form and sound,
Yet not recognizing their influence.

The sun, though not making form to cast shadow,
Yet shadow must follow sunlight,
The void, though not making sound to produce echo,
Yet echo must follow hollow valleys.
If the sun and void had hearts to create shadows and echoes,
Then there would be times when they fail—
How could they ever be seen nor heard,
Nor ensure that flourishing and preservation must exist?

The Dao can flourish and preserve in things,
Yet the Dao has never had a heart.
Thus, when the king raises troops and uses sharp tools,
The people grow desirous—
Desire grows, and with desire comes cutting.
Cutting as the standard,
Then the licentious advance while the upright retreat,
Loyal ministers suffer its poison,
And all the people bear its harm.

The desirous use desire as the standard,
Yet desire is licentious—
Thus the upright are cut down,
And all the people suffer harm.

To value wealth,
Then the people seek—
Seeking grows, and with seeking comes piercing.
Piercing as the standard,
Then the greedy prevail while the frugal suffer,
Loyal ministers bear the blame,
And all the people suffer defeat.

The seekers use seeking as the standard,
Yet seeking is greedy—
Thus the frugal are pierced,
And piercing brings injury.

When strife is opened, the people bend crookedly—
Bending crookedly, yet the standard is uprightness,
Uprightness then becomes unrestrained.
If unrestraint is taken as uprightness,
Then the perverse soar while the upright lie low,
Loyal ministers bear its calamity,
And all the people suffer its ruin.

When the ruler prizes fame, the people feign—
Feigning, yet the standard is brightness,
Brightness then becomes dazzling.
If dazzling is taken as brightness,
Then great virtue is concealed while petty favors are displayed,
Loyal ministers face death,
And all the people suffer misfortune.
The feigners use feigning as brightness,
Yet brightness is then darkness—
Thus, those who claim brightness are struck by misfortune.

The ruler who rules alone,
While ministers serve with divided loyalty,
Nurtures the ruler’s will,
Flatteringly indulges the ruler’s heart,
Blocks the ruler’s ears,
And veils the ruler’s wisdom—
This is how the state becomes perilous
And the ancestral temples fall into ruin.

Thus, the enlightened kings and sage rulers
Hold alone what they do not share,
Know alone what they do not teach,
Possess alone what they do not employ,
Measure themselves by uprightness yet do not impose it,
Are frugal in all things yet do not hoard,
Cling to natural rectitude yet do not rely on it,
Let their virtue shine universally yet do not haggle over it.

Why so?
Remove desire yet uphold uprightness,
So that the people act justly by themselves;
Pierce not where piercing is not due,
So that the people have no quarrels.
Matters are naturally resolved,
All things flow freely—
None call it fortune, none call it misfortune,
The world drifts in harmony, without fixed norm.
Treasure the Dao in one’s heart,
Be open and magnanimous,
Let things find their own place,
No one knows their limits.

Though not piercing, all things attain their proper form—
This is the piercing that transcends mere cutting,
Not the work of any blade.
Not that there is no cutting—
Pruning the proud, restraining the violent,
Yet leaving no scars or wounds.
Adapting to the times, conforming to nature,
Ruler and people are as one—
Though cutting, it is not injury.

Remove wealth yet uphold frugality,
So that the world naturally balances;
Pierce not where piercing is not due,
So that people have no disputes.
The greedy and grasping cease,
Purity and honesty arise—
None call it turbid, none call it clear,
Reputation is not falsely conferred,
Truth is not misrepresented.
Not that there is no piercing—
Practicing virtue, beauty, and humility,
Exposing flaws and manifesting vice,
Yet debate is without deception.
Remove wealth, embrace sincerity,
Humility and yielding follow reason—
Good and evil self-separate,
Thus nothing is concealed.

Remove strife yet uphold rectitude,
So that the people restrain themselves;
Unrestrain not where restraint is not due,
So that the people submit themselves.
Right the perverse, correct the chaotic,
Transform licentiousness, rectify customs—
None call it blessing,
Yet the world thrives in wildness,
All things find their natural place.
Not that there is no unrestraint—
Promote the upright, exalt the just,
Expose errors, highlight crimes,
Diminish the perverse, curb the crooked,
Reveal people’s faults—
The world is thoroughly rectified,
Yet action brings no sound.
Follow reason to mediate disputes,
Align with the Dao to suit the occasion—
Though just, there is no excess,
Though not unrestrained, it is not so.

Remove vanity yet uphold brightness,
So that the people act appropriately;
Dazzle not where dazzling is not due,
So that the people are naturally enlightened.
None call it illumination, none call it obscurity,
The world is vast and harmonious,
All things flourish and grow—
Virtue compares with Heaven,
Transformation aligns with the Dao.
Not that there is no dazzling—
Virtue shines universally,
Illuminates all things,
Yet its transformation is formless.

The Dao is its own brightness,
Permeating all without measure—
Each thing finds its own place,
No one knows its name.
Above and below mirror each other,
Inner and outer correspond,
Entry and exit leave no trace,
Movement and stillness know no bounds—
Like shadow to form, echo to sound.

Thus, the Way to govern a state,
The foundation of nurturing the people,
Is rooted in frugality.
No method surpasses frugality in governing people and harmonizing with Heaven.
Frugality means moderation and restraint.

Therefore, the enlightened kings and sage rulers
Diminish their outward displays,
Lower their official palaces,
Abandon the five flavors,
Extinguish music and color,
Use wisdom to dwell in simplicity,
Speak with clarity yet hold silence.
Establish a form without ostentation,
Set a pattern without imitation—
Fearful that others know them,
They conceal themselves in the unfathomable.

Thus, before they act, the world responds;
Before they command, the people gather;
Before they wage war, victory is assured;
Before they attack, the world submits.
Hence, they do not labor yet the people prosper,
They do not divide yet their duties are fulfilled,
They do not punish yet all fear them,
They do not scheme yet they receive Heaven’s blessings—
Disaster and chaos do not arise,
All auspicious signs converge,
Without action yet nothing fails to succeed,
Without strife yet nothing fails to conquer.
This is called "accumulating virtue"—
Thus, nothing fails to conquer.

All things return to their mysterious unity,
The world is in perfect accord—
Floating and sinking, ebbing and flowing,
Align with the Dao’s natural course.
Like end and beginning,
Like chaos and order,
Like emptiness and fullness,
Like absence and presence,
Like sparseness and density,
Like slowness and speed—
No form, no shadow,
No root, no trace—
Vague and indistinct,
Dark and silent,
Mysterious and boundless,
Like the vastness of Heaven and Earth,
Beyond measure or limit.

No one knows its limits.
Self-cultivation leaves abundance,
Thus one can establish a state;
Governing people and ordering things,
One’s descendants will never perish.
This is the way to establish a state.

Why so?

With its frugality thus established,
The Dao of sound is neither given nor bestowed—
Sparing and subtle, its virtue refined,
Full yet appearing as if nonexistent.
When sincerity flows through its intent,
Then endurance becomes its nature.

Form small, spirit vast—
A thousandfold its might,
One bearing ten thousand—
Thus it moves with effortless grace.

One principle governs all things,
In harmony with Heaven’s Dao.
Roots deep, foundations firm,
Dwelling with the divine—
The True Person embodies it,
The Sage preserves it.

This is the "mother of states,"
Deep-rooted, enduring, long-lived, and ever-visionary.

---

**On Governing Great States**

To govern a great state is to speak of its ruler—
Like poaching a small fish, gentle and unhurried.

With Dao as the cauldron, the world simmers beneath,
True authority reigns above—
Its spirits neither frighten nor harm.

What is not its spirit does not frighten,
Its spirit, when present, aids nature’s flow.
What is not its spirit does not harm life,
Its spirit, when balanced, nurtures all things pure.

Two forces unharming, Dao preserved,
Virtue returns—
A thousandfold the people’s blessing.

**Illustrating the Principle:**
When the sun declines, shadows rise;
Dryness peaks, winds stir;
Valleys tremble, seas surge high—
High and low stand in contrast,
Differing by hundreds of fathoms—
Because of their vast form.

Cliffs a thousand *ren* high,
Precipitous a hundred *zhang* deep—
Beasts ascend, yet crumble to ruin,
While gnats and ants glide unscathed,
And rhinos, elephants, tigers, and leopards—
Because of their weight—
Perish in the fall.

Gales howl, roofs lift, trees snap,
Rocks fly, iron scatters,
Mountains crumble—
Yet human blood flows undisturbed—
Because of their sudden might.

A breeze through cracks and holes
Stirs not a hair—
Yet when it enters the body,
It breeds a hundred ailments, bringing death—
Because of its subtlety.

Great states are like the ocean, like rhinos—
Yet their virtue is like the wind through cracks,
Like the breeze through holes.

Thus their blessings cannot be recklessly bestowed,
Their gains cannot be violently seized,
Their goodness cannot be grandly displayed,
Their evils cannot be recklessly abandoned.

To recklessly bestow is to recklessly lose,
To violently seize is to violently collapse,
To grandly display is to grandly depart,
To recklessly abandon is to recklessly invite.

To hold high office, wielding the world’s levers,
Power and authority already vast—
To agitate further would multiply losses.
Thus, governing a great state is like poaching a small fish.

Issuing decrees like the wind through cracks,
Still fearing overreach—
A thread’s tension, a hair’s breadth.

How much more so when indulging desires,
Lightly ruling the seas,
Acting with grand schemes,
