though harsh, are seen as deep virtue;
harmonious customs and familiar ways,
adapted to the land’s climate and terrain.

They delight in their customs,
rest in their homes.
When the Dao/Way flourishes and virtue abounds,
harmony extends to widows and orphans,
boundaries are respected, each guarding their own.

Neighboring states lie in sight,
yet spirits are unexhausted,
souls unbroken,
lives complete and desires fulfilled.

The sounds of roosters and dogs reach one another,
people gather firewood and vegetables,
climb hills to catch sight of kin,
share streams and rivers for bathing—
though distant, they do not conspire with ruler or subject,
nor gather in forbidden assemblies.
Each content with their own,
from birth to old age,
from old age to death,
without passing on authority or engaging in fraternization.

That the people do not fraternize until death
is because of the utmost *non-action* (無為),
and thus human desires are nonexistent.

*Sincere words are not ornate*—
sincere words are not ornate because they are direct,
ornate words are not sincere because they are flattering.
The wise do not indulge in broad knowledge—
*returning to the root* is their principle.
The broad-minded do not attain wisdom—
their pursuits are too manifold.
The virtuous do not argue—
*silent integrity* is their nature.
The eloquent do not possess virtue—
they adorn speech to deceive.

Thus, the Sage does not hoard the Dao/Way—
its clarity is self-evident.
When it is applied to the people, the Dao/Way is put into practice,
and the Sage’s own benefit deepens.
When it is fully given to the people, the Dao/Way is transmitted,
and the Sage’s own benefit overflows.

The Dao/Way of Heaven is both *yin* and *yang*,
beneficial yet not harmful—
its purpose is to nurture life.

The Sage’s Dao/Way avoids display and honor,
acts yet does not contend for merit or fame.

*Returning to the source*:
The interplay of emptiness and reality,
presence and absence,
cold and heat,
clarity and obscurity.
When *yin* wanes, *yang* flourishes;
when *yang* flourishes, *yin* wanes.
If the root is strong, the branches endure;
if the branches perish, the root decays.
The Dao/Way of Heaven and Earth is the mechanism of transformation.

All these principles—
the gateways to wisdom,
the origins of sincerity,
the measure of doubt and suspicion,
the scales of dazzling display—
are grasped by observing their roots,
cultivating their essence,
aligning with Heaven’s intent,
supervising by Nature’s law,
refining to their core,
simplifying to their truth.
To discern the near and know the far,
to observe what is hidden and reveal what is inverted,
to hear of names and recognize their substance,
to see beginnings and foresee endings,
to listen to sounds and perceive forms—
thus to illustrate gain and loss.

Then this is the *resonance of ten thousand years*,
a shared method for all ages,
the visible heart of Heaven and Earth,
and the complete intent of spirits and deities—
what of human affairs?

This is the natural order of the world,
the common essence of all people.

When one harbors the Dao/Way of Nature,
understands the logic of human sentiment,
holds fast to the primal *造化* (creative transformation),
and grasps the distinctions of *紀* (order/principle),
then harsh words strike the mark,
plainness harmonizes with virtue—
this is called *sincerity*.

The inferior look up to the superior,
and the superior depend on this.
The source of strength and authority,
the origin of commands and threats,
the aid of the people,
the foundation of success,
the basis of power and influence,
the rise of titles and renown—
all stem from here.

The Dao/Way is plain and unadorned,
without embellishment or taste.
Thus, sincere words are not ornate,
yet deeds are accomplished and truth is revealed.

So one voice sings and a thousand voices respond,
one moves and ten thousand follow.
Crushing mighty foes,
trapping great armies,
rushing into peril like water and fire—
dying without hesitation,
yet the people hold no resentment—
this is *sincerity*.

Though *sincerity* is not ornate,
its benefit is profound.
Sweet-talking and persuasive,
endless flattery and grand promises—
this is called *lack of sincerity*.

What is *lack of sincerity*?
Words that do not align with truth—
this is *lack of sincerity*.

When a person lacks sincerity,
virtue and grace cannot be established,
commands and threats cannot prevail,
power and influence cannot shine,
titles and renown are unclear.
Bestowing rewards does not inspire obedience,
inflicting punishments does not deter crime.
Thus, superiors and inferiors do not unite,
undertakings fail,
though one may be noble yet without position,
high yet without followers,
lonely and isolated,
the ancestral altars and states unsettled,
the world expecting salvation,
only to meet with ruin and punishment—
this is the harm of *sweet words*.

Sweet words without substance,
ornate yet untrue.

*Reverting to the root and returning to the origin*,
abandoning superficiality and discarding artifice,
primordial and fundamental,
few in means yet vast in effect,
one in response yet encompassing all,
refining to control the elaborate,
simplifying to uphold the singular—
this is called *limited knowledge*.

*Limited knowledge* thus enables wisdom.
The wise do not indulge in broad knowledge.

What is *wisdom*?
To grasp human sentiment and penetrate divine insight—
this is *wisdom*.
The wise are the safeguards of the body,
the instruments for unifying the realm.
The superior’s reliance,
the inferior’s attachment,
the path to Heaven’s guidance,
the road to the Dao/Way’s truth.

Thus, they encompass the grand scope of safety and peril,
hold the utmost keys to order and chaos,
so that all within the seas are loyal and exert their utmost,
dividing duties and fulfilling their roles,
to bring peace to their superiors.
Power and influence flow freely,
authority and virtue flourish greatly—
this is *wisdom*.

Though the wise do not indulge in broad knowledge,
their achievements are profound—
as it is said: *Know one thing, and all ten thousand things are known*.

The mind perceives myriad details,
the eyes survey human affairs,
yet without exhaustive limits—
when ministers scatter in confusion,
this is called *broad knowledge*.

*Broad knowledge* thus leads to ignorance.
The broad-minded do not attain wisdom.

What is *ignorance*?
To doubt Heaven’s Dao/Way,
to suspect human affairs—
this is *ignorance*.
The ignorant,
content in ease and pleasure,
internally consumed by endless thoughts,
externally driven by endless desires,
both loathe and hate,
easily lured to life,
easily coerced to death.»

The one who perceives the strange and is moved,
who fears danger and recoils,
who dazzles with superficial displays,
who deceives with shifting words and times,
who opposes what is open and rejects what is clear—
such a one falls into ruin and constraint,
whose actions neighbor calamity,
whose stillness borders disaster,
whose ancestral temples tremble in peril,
whose people scatter and depart—
this is *broad knowledge*.

This is the fate of the broad-minded who do not know.

When one is widely informed and open-minded,
yet speaks haltingly and is slow of tongue,
this is called *not eloquent*.

When one is drawn and drawn again, yet succeeds,
when one remains silent yet is trusted—
thus one achieves *virtue*.

The virtuous, though not eloquent, achieve virtue.

What is *virtue*?
When actions align with Heaven’s will,
when stillness attunes to Earth’s intent,
when words flow without obstruction,
when silence brings no harm—
this is *virtue*.

*Virtue* is the foundation of the noble,
the pinnacle of all conduct,
the convergence of auspiciousness,
the path of boundless blessings,
endless yet unexhausted,
used yet never depleted—
unaltered by ten thousand kings,
unchanged by diverse customs,
granted by Heaven and Earth,
enhanced by the numinous.

Thus, above it harmonizes with Heaven,
below it harmonizes with humanity—
the origin of governance,
the eternal principle of affairs,
the fulfillment of all things,
the sheltering of all life.
When the world reveres and follows it without end,
this is *virtue*.

Though the virtuous may not be eloquent,
they possess such achievements.

Not recognizing the fundamental source,
not perceiving the root origin,
defaming Heaven and Earth,
defaming humanity and spirits,
twisting words and altering intent—
this is called *eloquence*.

Clinging to suspicion, treading in doubt,
following desire while acting recklessly,
prizing fine words and empty rhetoric—
thus *vice* is born.

The eloquent are not virtuous.

What is *vice*?
When actions defy Heaven’s will,
when stillness contradicts Earth’s intent,
when words harm humanity and spirits—
this is *vice*.

Those of vice
divide the Dao and separate virtue,
dilute purity and corrupt sincerity,
alter and embellish speech,
lean on pretense while claiming benevolence,
fabricate omens and signs,
linking Earth and Heaven,
invoking masters and beasts—
though revered by the world,
they invert meaning and conceal truth,
fleeing substance for mere names,
dazzling others while remaining empty,
bewildering all without foundation,
abandoning truth for deceit,
striving to deceive the sovereign.

Adorning speech to please superiors,
forming factions to sway the ruler’s heart,
exposing the traces of favoritism,
sealing the path of loyalty and rectitude,
employing flattery to tilt the state’s authority—
thus they nurture violence and foster great deceit.
The world speaks ill, the age grows corrupt,
the ruler grows dim-witted,
obstruction and stagnation lead to peril and ruin—
this is *eloquence*.

Though eloquence is not virtuous,
its harm is thus manifest.

Therefore, the Sage guards against its beginnings,
cuts it off before it sprouts,
rejects eloquence and knowledge,
discards artifice and speech,
embracing emptiness, stillness, softness, and weakness,
mysterious silence, undyed truth,
concealing wisdom and virtue,
guiding all by naturalness.

Right and wrong, black and white,
are as clear as sun and moon;
same and different, true and false,
are as vast as Earth and Heaven.
Empty yet boundless, transforming with all things—
this is the Sage’s non-accumulation.

Acting without action,
harmonizing with all things,
nurturing yet never full,
dispersing yet never exhausted—
encompassing all directions.

The broad-minded ponder deeply,
yet see no thread;
the eloquent plan far ahead,
yet hear no beginning.
Extending without bending,
transforming without end,
returning to their start—
great clarity like darkness.
The more one gives to others, the more one possesses;
the more one exhausts for others, the brighter one becomes.
The more one nourishes others, the longer one lives;
the more one teaches others, the greater one’s gain.
The more one gives to others, the more one has;
the more one shares with others, the more one accumulates.

Both bright and dark,
dark yet again bright—
this is the Dao of Heaven.

Beneficial yet causing no harm,
aligned with Heaven and Earth,
giving life yet never killing,
communing with the numinous.

Establishing virtue and flowing blessings,
ever abiding in radiant honor,
yielding eloquence to let blessings return to namelessness,
acting yet not relying—
moving with the Dao.

Though Heaven’s Dao is beneficial yet causes no harm,
the Sage acts yet does not contend.

Though Heaven and humanity differ,
their benefits are the same.
Thus, aligning with Heaven’s Dao,
I have no separation.

---

**Dao/Way that can be spoken of is not the eternal Dao/Way;**
**Name that can be named is not the eternal Name.**
**The Nameless is the beginning of Heaven and Earth,**
**The Named is the mother of all things.**

Thus, **when one always lacks desire, one may perceive its subtlety;**
**when one always has desire, one may perceive its peril.**

These two—though issuing from the same source yet bearing different names—
are both called **Mysterious/Profound (Xuan)**.
**Mysterious/Profound beyond measure,**
the gateway to all wonders.

**The Supreme Sage’s manifestation:**
None is loftier than **Dao/Virtue**,
None is grander than **Divine Clarity (Shenming)**,
None is vast as **Great Harmony (Taihe)**,
None is exalted as **Heaven and Earth**,
None is more intimate than **Yin and Yang**,
None is more luminous than the **Great Sage (Dasheng)**.

**Dao/Virtue** is that which can be spoken of yet cannot be exhaustively explained;
**Divine Clarity (Shenming)** is that which can be preserved yet cannot be fully articulated;
**Great Harmony (Taihe)** is that which can be embodied yet cannot be transformed;
**Heaven and Earth** are that which can be followed yet cannot be proclaimed;
**Yin and Yang** are that which can be utilized yet cannot be transmitted;
The **Great Sage (Dasheng)** is that which can be observed yet cannot be described.

Hence, **what can be measured is known, yet few know its limits;**
**what can be understood is shallow, yet few act upon its depths.**

The **most multitudinous of the multitudinous cannot be counted,**
the **most vast of the vast cannot be measured;**
**subtle and profound, exhausting principles—**
this is beyond the reach of mere wisdom.
**The utmost fulfillment—**
this cannot be attained through striving.
Between **Heaven and Earth**, calamities and chaos
cannot be overcome by human schemes.

Thus, **Dao/Way that cannot be spoken of is the eternal Dao/Way,**
**Virtue/Power that cannot be named is the eternal Virtue/Power—**
the origin of governance.
**Name that cannot be named,**
**achieving merit without ostentation—**
the root of transformation.

Therefore, **when rulers act,**
the people crave desires,
**abandoning purity and forsaking sincerity,**
**refining yet becoming coarse,**
**opening their ears and eyes,**
**enticing them with sounds and colors,**
**indulging them with the five flavors,**
**pleasing them with merit and reward,**
**guiding them with rites and propriety,**
the people are like those awakening from sleep,
emerging from a dark chamber,
ascending hills to gaze upon the eight directions,
beholding the **Big Dipper (Shenchen)** and **constellations (Cen)** to see the sun and moon.

Thus, **transformation can be articulated,**
**virtue can be enumerated,**
**merit can be recounted,**
**and names can be distinguished.**

Hence, **knowing yet flowing unrestrained,**
**evil and falsehood arise;**
**Dao/Virtue is obstructed,**
**Divine Clarity is severed;**
**a hundred flaws sprout,**
**Great Harmony is exhausted.**

The people wander in confusion, lost in the realm of right and wrong,
**losing their natural rhythms.**
**Emotions shift with the utmost transformations,**
**entangled with all things;**
**their faces grow wan and dark,**
**their hearts filled with sorrow and woe;**
**they do not find peace in life,**
**nor joy in their customs;**
**they lose their Heaven-ordained years,**
**all harmed by violence and tyranny.**

Thus, **sovereign and subject regard each other with anxious scheming,**
**father and child cling to one another with yearning,**
**brothers fret over one another with melancholy,**
**the common folk tremble in fear and shrink their bodies.**

**Shrinking their bodies yet clinging together,**
death comes swiftly—
this is the source of calamity and woe.
**Clinging with yearning,**
**fretting with melancholy,**
**nighttime vigil and morning inquiry,**
**words of distress and faces of anguish—**
this is the cause of untimely injury.

**When subjects behold their rulers,**
**their complexions lack composure,**
**they hurry in haste and bow with exertion,**
**shoulders hunched, elbows pressed,**
**prostrating themselves in obeisance,**
**crawling forward in submission—**
this is **not the way of true kinship.**

Thus, **Dao/Way that can be spoken of is Dao/Virtue made manifest, yet not the natural Way;**
**Name that can be named is fame and merit displayed, yet not the innate Truth.**

**(II)**
Having a name is not the Dao;
Being without a name is not the Dao.
Having action is not the Dao;
Being without action is not the Dao.
Without a name yet encompassing all names,
Without action yet accomplishing all deeds.

**(III)**
Without name, without trace,
Merging with the Divine,
The world relies upon it,
Yet none know its source—
Transforming from the Void,
It is the origin of Heaven and Earth.

**(IV)**
Those with names who embody transformation
Follow the Dao and virtue,
Revere the numinous,
Emulate Great Harmony,
Conform to Heaven and Earth,
Thus becoming the Mother of all things.

**(V)**
The desireless one gazes beyond expectation;
Observing its subtlety,
They attain the **Pure and Bright** [太清].

**(VI)**
The heart like metal and stone,
The form like withered wood,
Silent in seclusion,
With resolve as steadfast as a colt—
Such is the desireless one.
Restoring the root of life and essence.

Yet those with desires
Chase after transient things,
Losing the path of ease,
Seeing only the narrow confines,
Lost and unable to return,
They squander their true essence.

When all know beauty as beauty,
Then ugliness arises;
All know goodness as goodness,
Then not-goodness arises.

Thus, being and non-being give rise to each other,
Difficulty and ease complete each other,
Long and short define each other,
High and low depend on each other,
Sounds harmonize with tones,
Before and after follow in sequence.

Therefore, the Sage acts without action,
Teaches without speech,
Yet all things arise without resistance—
Creates without possession,
Acts without reliance,
Accomplishes without claiming.
Because they do not claim,
Their power does not depart.

---

**(VII)**
Human cleverness can be restrained but not dispersed,
Human desires can be countered but not indulged.
Adorning one’s appearance harms one’s nature;
Indulging desires diminishes one’s vitality.
What the world calls "beautiful" and "good"
Is not the utmost beauty or goodness.
For the utmost beauty is not seen by the world,
The utmost goodness is not known by the world.

---

**(VIII)**
Without being, one cannot perceive having;
Without having, one cannot comprehend non-being.
Without difficulty, one cannot know ease;
Without ease, one cannot grasp difficulty.
Without long, one cannot know short;
Without short, one cannot know long.
Without mountains, one cannot know valleys;
Without valleys, one cannot know mountains.
Without tones, one cannot discern sounds;
Without sounds, one cannot recognize tones.
Without before, one cannot know after;
Without after, one cannot know before.

All these pairs—
Heaven and Earth’s proof,
Nature’s seal—
Are laid out in plain sight, yet some deny them,
Affirming or negating in sequence,
Reversing at their end.
The divine cannot evade them,
Yin and Yang cannot defy them.

From this, it is clear:
The affairs of the Sage-King cannot be forced by action.

---

**(IX)**
The radiant does not endure,
The obscure does not persist.
Honored splendor flourishes in mid-spring,
Yet wild greens and millet thrive at autumnal equinox.
On the winter solstice, all things grow lush;
On the summer solstice, all things sigh in sorrow.

---

**(X)**
Only those who dare not rest complacently
And continually cultivate their virtue
Forget their deeds while their virtue remains—
Thus they do not claim yet do not lose it.
Their transformation aligns with the Dao,
They do not expect reward,
Their virtue equals Heaven’s,
They do not seek repayment,
Hiding their deeds, evading fame,
Deep in the mysterious realm.
Though they do not claim,
Their virtue does not depart.

---

**Chapter: Not Valuing the Skilled**

Do not value the skilled,
So the people do not compete;
Do not treasure rare goods,
So the people do not steal;
Do not display what is desirable,
So the people’s hearts remain undisturbed.

Thus, the Sage’s governance:
Empties their minds, fills their bellies;
Weakens their ambitions, strengthens their bones.
Always keep the people without knowledge, without desire,
So even the wise dare not act.

Act with *wuwei*,
And nothing remains untended.

---

**(XI)**
When the world extols rites and morality,
People compete, yet fall short—
Then hypocrisy arises.

---

**(XII)**
Those with abundant virtue rule,
Those with meager virtue serve.
The worthy are rare—one in ten thousand,
The Sage appears not every age.

---

**(XIII)**
As when a slow horse and a swift steed race on level ground,
Or a wild goose and a partridge fly in the blue sky—
Then the worthy and unworthy become clear.

---

**(XIV)**
Hoarding jewels and jade makes people seek them,
Yet scarcity breeds theft.
Displaying music and dance delights people,
Yet excess leads to licentiousness.

---

**(XV)**
If the world does not value the skilled,
The people do not vie for them—
No vying, no strife, no chaos.
If the world does not treasure goods,
The people do not covet—
No coveting, no theft.
If the world abandons music and dance,
The people feel no joy—
No joy, no pleasure, no licentiousness.
This is the natural order.

---

**(XVI)**
Empty the mind, calm the breath,
Focus the essence, gather the spirit.
Silent and without action,
Serene and without governance.

---

**(XVII)**
Offer no titles or rewards,
Yet filial piety arises naturally;
Impose no punishments,
Yet deceit ceases on its own.
Return to the true, restore the simple,
Revert to the origin.
The ruler acts with *wuwei*,
Heaven and humanity interact effortlessly;
Soaring in natural harmony,
All things govern themselves.

---

**Chapter: The Dao’s Pervasiveness**

The Dao is boundless yet can be used without exhaustion—
Deep, like the origin of all things.
It dulls the sharp,
Unravels the tangled,
Blends its radiance,
Aligns with the dust.
It sinks like the unseen—
I do not know whose child it is,
Yet it precedes the Sovereign.

---

**(XVIII)**
The Dao is supremely void,
Thus its action is supremely unrestrained.
Virtue is supremely without,
Thus its action is supremely harmonious.
All things receive it—
None escape its unrestrained, harmonious flow.

The application of Dao and virtue is the constant of the numinous,
The path followed by Heaven and Earth, the principle revered by yin and yang.

**(XIX)**
That which is supremely void is not void,
That which is supremely harmonious is not harmonious.
Only by not striving for voidness and harmony
Does one attain true voidness and harmony.
Voidness takes emptiness as its dwelling;
Harmony takes *wuwei* as its home.
To be able to empty and to be without,
Is to have surplus voidness;
To be able to be without and to empty,
Is to always align with harmony.

**(XX)**
To have resolve yet no sharpness,
To have intent yet no scheming,
To devise what is not devised,
To plan what is not planned.

---
**Chapter: Heaven and Earth’s Impartiality**
Heaven and Earth are not benevolent,
Yet they treat all things as sacred offerings;
The Sage is not benevolent,
Yet he treats the people as sacred offerings.
Between Heaven and Earth—
Is it not like a bellows?
Empty yet unyielding,
Moving yet ever producing.

Much speech leads to exhaustion;
Better to guard the center.

---
**(XXI)**
Heaven is high and clear,
Earth is deep and tranquil;
Yin and yang intermingle,
Harmonious *qi* flows freely,
Serene and without contrivance—
All things arise spontaneously.

Heaven and Earth do not incline their hearts or shift their intentions,
Exhaust their spirits, or labor in affairs.
With sorrowful yearning, they bestow love and profit,
Spread kindness and abundance,
And yet complete all things without effort.

The enlightened ruler and sage,
Upholding Dao and harmony,
Remains clear and tranquil, unchanging,
Adapting with singular transformation,
Reaching subtly and silently,
Conforming to Dao’s manner—
The world responds,
All things transform naturally.

The Sage does not exhaust his wisdom or abilities,
Agitate his mind or unsettle his resolve,
Drain his essence or weary his spirit,
Cease from contemplation or fret in distraction,
Yet benevolence arises from action,
And he governs myriad lives without contrivance.

---
**(XXII)**
If Heaven and Earth abandon emptiness for love and profit,
Their transformations falter,
Things do not flourish fully.
If the Sage abandons emptiness for love and profit,
His virtue does not spread universally,
The realm does not unite,
His grace does not reach deeply,
His deeds do not complete fully.

Why?
The art of transforming through love has limits,
Yet the myriad things’ dependence on transformation is boundless.
To wield a limited measure against an endless demand
Is like trying to replenish a dried river with tears.

---
**(XXIII)**
When lice and fleas move upon the hair,
Sleep becomes restless;
When mosquitoes and gnats cling to the skin,
The spirit grows agitated, thought obstructed;
When stung by wasps or hornets,
The heart is pierced with pain;
Even without harm to ears and eyes,
All limbs grow useless.

---
**(XXIV)**
Heaven and Earth speak not,
Yet through their boundless emptiness,
They attain the harmony of all things,
And bring forth without end.
The Sage speaks not,
But his laws are void yet all things conform to them.

The prison of Heaven is vast yet holds no restraint,
The spirits and gods are tranquil yet act not.
The world drifts in ease,
Ignorant yet unknowing, yet great harmony prevails.

---
**(XXV)**
Words spoken invite calamity,
Words lost bring death to the self.

---
**Chapter: "The Valley Spirit Never Dies"**
The Valley Spirit never dies,
This is called the Mysterious Feminine.
The gate of the Mysterious Feminine,
This is called the root of Heaven and Earth.
Endless yet as if it exists,
Used without depletion.

---
**(XXVI)**
The Dao of Great Harmony—subtle *qi*,
Things born from it are divine.
Emptiness and voidness are its home,
Stillness and solitude its constant.
Coming and going have no opening,
Forward and backward have no obstruction.
In motion, nothing is not accomplished,
In stillness, nothing is not formed.
Transforming yet not transforming,
Giving birth yet not giving birth.

---
**(XXVII)**
The Feminine, though yielding and soft,
Can give birth.
The Mysterious, though deep and distant,
Is unseen.
Though it bears all things like a mother,
None can obscure its form.

---
**(XXVIII)**
The Dao of Great Harmony gives birth yet does not die,
Begins yet does not end.
It opens and guides the divine and enlightened,
As the root and origin of Heaven and Earth.

---
**(XXIX)**
Motion and stillness are profound and wondrous,
As if nonexistent, as if existing.
It accomplishes things and fulfills affairs,
In nothing does it fail.
Shining yet not extinguished,
Used without depletion—
For its birth is not born,
Its form is without shape.

---
**Chapter: "Heaven and Earth Endure Long"**
Heaven and Earth endure long.
Heaven and Earth endure long because they do not generate themselves,
Thus they endure long in generating.
Therefore the Sage places his self last, yet his self is first,
Sets his self aside, yet his self is preserved.
Is this not because he has no private desires?
Thus he can fulfill his private desires.

---
**(XXX)**
The Sage’s awe shakes the eight directions,
His wisdom penetrates the four quarters.
He entrusts his deliberations to desirelessness,
Returns his plans to non-action.
He humbles himself to honor Heaven,
Sets himself aside to benefit the people—
Thus he accomplishes without acting,
Commands without speaking,
And the people willingly serve him.

Therefore, he places others first and reverses his own self to conform to the Dao,
Sets himself aside to benefit the people—
His deeds are vast yet unseen,
His virtue is high yet unheard.
His transformation flows with the divine and enlightened,
His longevity aligns with the mountains and rivers—
Thus he endures.

---
**Chapter: "The Supreme Good is Like Water"**
The supreme good is like water.
Water benefits all things yet does not contend,
Dwells where people revile it—
Thus it approaches the Dao.
Residing, it is good as Earth,
In heart, it is good as the depths,
In giving, it is good in kindness,
In speech, it is good in trust,
In governance, it is good in rectitude,
In action, it is good in capability,
In timing, it is good in motion.

Only because it does not contend,
It has no grievances.

---
**(XXXI)**
Man, in body soft yet spirit weak,
Descends from heights to lows,
Endures humiliation like Earth,
Holds filth like the sea,
His words conform to the hearts of others,
His self is last among people.
Where people revile, he alone abides,
Serene as if heartless,
Drifting as if selfless,
Ever-changing yet constant—
Flowing with the Dao.
To relinquish the self and follow nature,
None surpasses water.
Emperors embody it, using it to govern.
Its virtue is subtle and profound—
What grievances could there be?

---
**Chapter: "Hold and It Will Be Full"**
Hold and it will be full,
Yet not as good as letting it go.
Grasp and it will slip away,
Yet cannot be long preserved.
Gold and jade fill the hall,
Yet none can guard them.
Riches and honor bring arrogance,
Yet invite one’s own doom.
When deeds are accomplished, withdraw the self—
This is the Dao of Heaven.

---
**(XXXII)**
Pursuing wealth and honor in times of abundance,
One accumulates fortune and goods—
The heavier the goods, the more the divine and enlightened are drained.
Wealth and goods piled up bring calamity and doom—
Better than having fullness and stopping.

---
**(XXXIII)**
To sharpen the heart and focus the will,
To strategize and plot—
Wisdom and ability bring rank and honor,
Fame and influence advance the self.
The divine departs,
How can peace be long preserved?

---
**(XXXIV)**
Riches and honor to me,
Are like ascending a mountain to gaze afar.
Fame and power to me,
Are like a fleeting bolt of lightning.

---
**(XXXV)**
Gold and jade compared to the self,
Fame and power compared to the divine—
Like ice and charcoal,
Their essences cannot coexist.
Thus fame is the defilement of the divine,
Profit is the harm to the self.
Nurturing the divine’s defilement,
Accumulating the self’s harm—
It diminishes what I have accomplished,
And increases what I have failed.
Gaining it is deemed as profit,
Losing it is deemed as harm—
Then one’s thoughts grow muddled,
And inclinations perverse.

---
**(XXXVI)**
Wealth that benefits me harms my divine,
Fame that gives me birth destroys my self.
Calamity arises from within me,
Not from others.
Fortune arises from within me,
Not from Heaven.

---
**(XXXVII)**
Riches and honor without arrogance,
Easy to say, yet hard to practice.
The higher the self’s station,
The more distant the will must be.

But when one is wealthy and noble yet remains arrogant,
It is like a torch seeking fire—
The brighter the torch, the more swiftly it burns away;
Can one not be cautious?

---
**(Chapter XXXVIII: *Nurturing the Vital Essence and Embracing Oneness*)**
To bear the vital essence and embrace oneness,
How could one remain detached?
To focus one’s *qi* and attain supreme softness,
How could one not be like an infant?
To purify and remove all obscurity,
How could one not be flawless?
To love the people and govern the state,
How could one not be without knowledge?
To open and close the celestial gates,
How could one not be without partiality?
To be clear and unobstructed in all directions,
How could one not act without contrivance?
To give birth to them, to nourish them,
To give birth yet not possess them,
To act yet not claim credit,
To grow yet not dominate—
This is called the **Mysterious Virtue**.

---
**(Chapter XXXVIII: *The Mysterious Virtue*)**
Not possessing, not claiming,
Not giving birth yet not slaughtering—
Transformation unfathomable,
Heaven and Earth govern themselves.
Abandoning ornamentation and discarding excess,
Returning to the origin, reverting to the beginning—
Disaster ceases from within me,
Chaos vanishes from others.
Fortune springs from Heaven,
Virtue arises from Earth.
Yet in quietude, ever turning,
All things are harmonized and balanced.
Its virtue is profound and dark,
No one can see or hear it.

---
**(Chapter XXXVIII: *Thirty Spokes and the Central Axis*)**

**(Chapter XXXIX: *The Shepherding of the People in the Primordial Age*)**
In the Age of Great Antiquity, the sage shepherded the people,
Following what Heaven and Earth naturally did,
Not resorting to clever schemes.
They drank from gourds,
They ate with their hands—
All things were equal and balanced,
No distinction between high and low.

When rulers began to act with purpose,
They imposed heavy taxes and laborious duties,
The people grew exhausted beyond measure,
While the sovereign’s demands never ceased.
Their tributes came from distant lands,
Men and women carried burdens they could not bear,
And thus the clever devised the wheel hub,
To harness horses and oxen,
To bear heavy loads and travel far,
To ease the people’s toil.

Later generations followed this path,
And artificial refinements multiplied.
The wheels were painted with stripes and red,
Adorned with gold and silver,
And embellished with jade ornaments.
The cost of a single chariot
Was enough to impoverish a family.

Thus, Laozi lamented the harm of contrivance to **Dao/Way** and **virtue**,
Illustrating how well-intentioned action breeds disaster and chaos.
Hence, he cited the three cases—chariot, vessel, dwelling—
To explain how **having** and **non-having**,
**utility** and **use**,
Interdependently lead to both benefit and ruin.
This was his warning to all.

---

**(Chapter XL: *The Decay of Dao and Virtue*)**
When **Dao/Way** and **virtue** decline,
Worries assail from within,
While yin and yang ravage without.
The people grow frail and emaciated,
Plagued by disease.
Thus, water and fire rise together,
The five flavors take form,
Raw and cooked are not distinguished,
Dry and damp are not separated.
The clever then knead clay to make vessels,
To cook sour and salty foods.
This leads to hunting and indulgence,
To slaughtering all living things,
To piercing wombs and killing eggs,
To gratify the ruler’s desires.
They carve and polish pearls and jade,
To fashion bowls and plates,
And refine crude materials into tools—
All this to such an extent.

---

**(Chapter XLI: *The Corruption of Human Nature and Its Consequences*)**
Once human hearts are corrupted,
All things grow resentful and hateful.
Serpents and venomous creatures rise,
Birds and beasts harm mankind.
Thus, even caves and hollows
Are no longer sufficient to ward off calamity,
To preserve one’s life,
Or to complete one’s natural span.
The clever then devise dwellings:
Roofed with beams, walled with eaves,
Windows pierced for surveillance,
Gates fortified with locks,
Openings and closures made swift and sharp—
So that wasps and insects cannot enter,
And birds and beasts cannot approach.

Yet later generations consider this governance,
While earlier ones saw it as chaos.
For this is the flaw of **having** and **non-having**,
**utility** and **use**,
Interdependently leading to both order and disorder—
It lies in the hands of humanity alone.

---
**Five Colors**

**Five Colors**

The five colors blind the eyes,
The five tones deafen the ears,
The five flavors dull the palate,
Galloping and hunting drive the heart to madness,
Rare treasures lead to errant conduct.

Thus, the Sage nourishes the belly, not the eyes,
And discards the one to embrace the other.

*(Wang Bi’s commentary on Laozi, Chapter 12)*

(42) To indulge in the shifting allure of the five colors
Is to gaze without perceiving the forms of calamity and fortune—
A spear piercing the eyes.

To revel in the shifting tones of the five sounds
Is to listen without hearing the voices of auspice and omen—
A plug sealing the ears.

To delight in the shifting flavors of the five tastes
Is to taste without discerning the truth of right and wrong—
A blade to sever the tongue.

*(Qiang Sici’s Tang-era *Moral Teachings of the Dao De Jing*, Exalted Virtue Commentary)*

(43) To take pleasure in the shifting thrills of hunting and pursuit
Is to let the mind fall into frenzy and delusion.
Hunting and pursuit are the generals of frenzy and delusion.

*(Qiang Sici’s Tang-era *Moral Teachings of the Dao De Jing*, Exalted Virtue Commentary)*

(44) To covet the shifting allure of wealth and goods
Is to let the mind stray into perverse inclinations.
Wealth and goods are things that harm the root.

*(Qiang Sici’s Tang-era *Moral Teachings of the Dao De Jing*, Exalted Virtue Commentary)*

(45) The Sage wears the color of no-color,
Listens to the sound of no-sound,
Tastes the flavor of no-flavor,
Gallops through realms of no-boundaries,
Traverses paths of no-limits,
Casts nets of no-form—
And thus attains the heart of Dao and virtue!

*(Qiang Sici’s Tang-era *Moral Teachings of the Dao De Jing*, Exalted Virtue Commentary)*

**Chapter on Treating Favor and Insult as Startling**

---

**Chapter on Treating Favor and Insult as Startling**

Treating favor and insult as startling,
One esteems great calamities as if they were one’s own self.

What is meant by *treating favor and insult as startling*?
Favor is a lowly thing—
To receive it is startling,
To lose it is startling;
This is what is meant by *treating favor and insult as startling*.

What is meant by *esteeming great calamities as if they were one’s own self*?
The reason I have great calamities
Is that I have a self.
And when I have no self,
What great calamities do I have?
Thus, to value one’s self as the foundation of all under Heaven,
Is as if one could entrust all under Heaven;
To love one’s self as the foundation of all under Heaven,
Is as if one could be trusted by all under Heaven.

---

**Chapter on the Unseen Vision**

(46) Rest the mind in the Dao and virtue,
Preserve the will in divine clarity,
Harmony as the central sovereign,
Serene as if not born.

Plans without calculation,
Nurture the heavens and earth;
Concerns without deliberation,
Soar through the boundless void.
Presence and absence in transformation,
Not regarded as strange.
Honor and disgrace, exaltation and abasement,
No lack or excess in them.

Great virtue perishes in the self,
Thus great calamities cannot befall,
And the Heavenly Net cannot ensnare.

---

**Chapter on the Unseen Vision**

(46) What cannot be seen is called *Yi* (平易, simplicity),
What cannot be heard is called *Xi* (希, subtlety),
What cannot be grasped is called *Wei* (微, faintness).
These three cannot be defined in words,
Thus they merge into one.
Above, it does not dazzle,
Below, it does not obscure—
Its threads are indistinct, yet it cannot be named,
Returning to the formless.
This is called the *State of the Unseen* (无状之状),
The *Form of the Formless* (无物之象),
This is called *Hunhuang* (惚恍, indistinct yet discernible).

Pursue it, yet you cannot see its head,
Follow it, yet you cannot see its tail.
Hold to the ancient Dao,
To govern the present with its naturalness—
One who knows the ancient beginning,
This is called *Dao’s Pattern* (道纪).

---

(47) Before the great goose is formed,
If one cracks its egg and examines it,
It is not yet a goose.
Yet its shape and sound, head and tail,
Are already present in essence.
This is the goose that is not yet a goose.

How much more so when,
Before the egg of the great goose exists,
Creation and transformation already give it form!
Thus it is clear:
The origin of the *Tai Ji* (太极),
Before Heaven and Earth,
Already possesses indistinct shape and sound,
Though unseen and unheard.

To see without using sight,
To hear without using hearing,
To grasp without clinging,
To speak without words—
This is how one discerns.

Therefore,
The *Form without Form* (无形之形),
From which Heaven and Earth arise,
Is called *Yi*.
The *Sound without Sound* (无声之声),
From which the five tones begin,
Is called *Xi*.
The *Thread without Thread* (无绪之绪),
From which myriad things emerge,
Is called *Wei*.

---

(48) Profound and vast, it returns to emptiness,
Its curves shape all things, allowing them to exist.
Exhausting the subtle, reaching the mysterious,
All things find their fulfillment.
Flowing through all directions,
No trace of its absence can be seen.

---

(49) The *State of the Unseen* (无状之状),
Yet it shapes all states;
The *Form of the Formless* (无象之象),
Yet it mirrors all forms;
Its light shines in *Hunhuang* (惚恍),
Yet it reveals all things.
Great yet appearing small,
Present yet appearing lost.

---

(50) Holding to the ancient Dao’s naturalness,
To govern the present without altering its simplicity for barbarians,
Or changing its form for the Central States.
With one principle, know the beginning,
With one principle, know the end—
Reverence the Dao’s commands,
And all things hang suspended.

It governs all without exception,
It oversees all without fail—
Its duties are vast and great,
Nothing it does not fulfill.
As the *Empty Framework* (虚纲纪),
It is the progenitor of Heaven and Earth.

---

The Guest:
Adapting to circumstances yet not innovating,
Following the Dao and yielding to Heaven.
Always as a respectful guest,
Not altering the halls for the host,
Nor changing his wives and concubines.

Ice:
Ever yin yet never yang,
Quiet yet never clamorous,
Adapting to events and shifting with things.
Soft and yielding, smooth and supple,
It can adapt to all—
Like winter’s accumulation as ice,
Spring’s release as water—
Heaven’s timing in motion.

---

**Chapter on Attaining the Ultimate Void (致虚极章):**
Attain the ultimate void,
Hold fast to stillness with sincerity—
All things arise together,
And I observe their return.

Things teem and flourish,
Each returning to its root.
Returning to the root is stillness—
This is called restoring the vital breath.
Restoring the vital breath is constancy.
Knowing constancy is clarity;
Not knowing constancy, reckless action brings ruin.
Knowing constancy is tolerance.
Tolerance brings impartiality,
Impartiality brings kingship,
Kingship aligns with Heaven,
Heaven aligns with the Dao,
The Dao endures eternally.
Thus, one’s life remains unharmed.

---

**Moral Virtue and the Void:**
Dao and virtue are void and formless,
Thus they can bestow and receive.
Heaven and Earth are serene and tranquil,
Thus they can transform and change.
Yin and yang alternate,
Thus they can give life and bring death.
Sun and moon advance and retreat,
Thus they can radiate brilliance.
The four seasons begin and end,
Thus they can nurture and complete.

To discard the Void,
Dao and virtue cannot endure;
To abandon tranquility,
Heaven and Earth cannot exist;
To move without returning,
Yin and yang cannot harmonize;
To advance without retreat,
Sun and moon cannot shine;
To end without beginning,
All things cannot flourish.

Thus, being yet returning to non-being,
Substance yet yielding to emptiness—
The mind bears nothing,
The will is unobstructed.
Act without action, like a sealed vessel;
Unworried, like madness;
Embrace the True, tread the Pure;
Abandon cleverness,
Ignorance as the foremost virtue,
Emptiness as constancy—
Then the divine and luminous reach their peak,
And nature unfolds in its fullness!

Reflect upon actions inwardly,
Recollect thoughts to restore the spirit;
Hide myself in non-thought,
Carry my form in non-being;
Do not burden the will with what harms life,
Do not exhaust the spirit with what harms Heaven;
Act with ease, yet the spirit remains undisturbed,
Flow inwardly, yet the exterior remains unchanged;
Turn vision inward, reverse hearing,
Align with the spirit’s shifts—
Ascend with Heaven, descend with the world;
The spirit guards without disturbance,
Vital breath flows without strain,
Advance and retreat, bend and stretch—
All find the Middle Way.

---

**The Way’s Origin:**
Begin with non-action,
Move with the formless,
Manifest in timely harmony,
Thus success is naturally achieved.

---

**Returning to Transformation:**
Heaven and Earth alternate,
Thus they endure eternally;
Humans return to sleep,
Thus they attain clarity;
Flying birds return to gather,
Thus they soar high;
Running beasts return to rest,
Thus they leap far;
Dragons and serpents return to their coils,
Thus they shine resplendent;
Grasses and trees return to root,
Thus they remain verdant.

When transformation returns,
The divine attains its place,
Communing with the Void,
The soul rests, the vital breath settles,
Each finds its ease—
The will is tranquil, the breath flows smoothly,
Blood and vessels harmonize.

---

**Those Who Lose the Dao:**
Discarding constancy,
Pursuing cleverness,
Indulging desires,
Reckless action brings calamity.

Thus, wisdom invites disaster,
Clarity brings calamity,
Deep insight leads to death,
Erudition brings ruin.
Why is this so?
They do not return to the Original Beginning,
They do not restore the Root Source;
Their actions defy the Dao,
Their stillness estranges them from the Spirit.

Existing, yet they cannot preserve;
Doing, yet they cannot accomplish.

---

Cultivate the mind in emptiness and stillness,
Anchor the will in subtlety and wonder,
Abandon thought in desirelessness,
Return to action in non-action—
Thus one attains longevity,
And abides with the Dao eternally.

---

**Chapter on the Supreme Dao:**
The Supreme Dao acts without contrivance,
Yet the world knows its existence.
Next, it is cherished and praised.
Next, it is feared.
Next, it is reviled.
When trust is insufficient,
Doubt arises.
Mysterious! How precious its words!
When deeds are complete and affairs fulfilled,
The people say, *"It happened naturally."*

---

People delight in being rulers,
Calling them *"Emperors."*

---

**Chapter on Discarding Learning:**
Discarding learning brings no anxiety.
How far apart are *"only this"* and *"that"*?
How different are *"good"* and *"evil"*?
What people fear, one must not fail to fear.
Vast! Its end is boundless!

The masses rejoice and bustle,
Like feasting on the grandest sacrificial offerings,
Like ascending the Spring Terrace—
I alone remain tranquil, yet no signs appear,
Like an infant yet to be weaned,
Staggering and unsteady, as if lost.

The masses all have excess,
While I alone seem abandoned.
Am I the heart of a foolish man?
Dull and indistinct!

The common folk are bright and discerning,
I alone am dim and murky.
The common folk are keen and probing,
I alone am muddled and obscure.

Serene as the sea, yet boundless in its sweep—
How profound! How endless!

The masses all have something to grasp,
While I alone appear crude and coarse.
I alone differ from others,
Yet cherish the **Mother of All** (*Food of the Dao*).

---

**Chapter on the Perils of Worldly Learning:**
Worldly learning extols argument and values knowledge,
Fosters cliques and partisan debates.
The virtuous gain from it, the wicked suffer harm.
Within heaven and earth, the virtuous are few while the wicked are many,
Thus learning’s benefits are shallow, yet its harms are deep.

The wicked who pursue learning
Are like tigers gaining wings—
Soaring and prowling across the four seas,
Selecting flesh to devour.

The Sage discards it,
And the world rests in peace.
No teaching, yet all transform naturally;
No commands, yet all submit of their own accord.

---

**Chapter on the Dao’s Fullness Through Flexibility:**

**Chapter on the Dao’s Fullness Through Flexibility:**

What is bent remains whole,
What is warped becomes straight,
What is hollowed becomes filled,
What is worn becomes renewed,
What is few gains much,
What is much falls into confusion.
Thus the Sage embraces **Oneness**,
And serves as a model for all under heaven.

He does not flaunt himself, so he is bright;
He does not insist on being right, so his virtue shines;
He does not boast of his deeds, so his merit endures;
He does not pride himself, so he endures long.

Only by not contending does he surpass all contenders in heaven and earth.
Was it mere empty words when the ancients said,
*"What is bent remains whole"*?
Indeed, it is whole and returns to its source.

Even sages among kings and lords
Still regard it as *"bent"*—
By entrusting governance to officials,
Their virtue remains whole.

When constraints are few, gains are many—
Yet even then, things find their proper measure on their own.

To rely solely on one’s own thoughts and deliberations,
Without drawing from others,
Is to invite madness through excessive speech and knowledge.

The Sage does not pride himself in his clarity,
But lets all under heaven see with their own eyes—
Thus even **Lí Lóu** cannot surpass his vision.

*"Boasting"* means aggressive assault.
If one exploits the world’s anger to attack the world,
Even the Yellow Emperor could not rival his might.
If one harnesses the world’s strength to wage war upon it,
Even **Tang** and **Wu** could not match his achievements—
Thus all under heaven submit to him,
And the descendants of feudal lords serve him willingly.

Shadows follow form, echoes answer sound—
They do not contend with anything,
So who could contend with them?

---

**Chapter on the Virtue of Few Words:**

Few words align with the natural Way.
Hence, gusting winds do not last a morning,
Sudden rains do not last a day.
Who brings this about?
Heaven and Earth.
Even heaven and earth cannot endure long—
How much less can mortals?

Those who follow the Dao:
Those aligned with the Dao merge with the Dao,
Those aligned with virtue merge with virtue,
Those aligned with loss merge with loss.
Those who merge with the Dao find the Dao rejoices in them;
Those who merge with virtue find virtue rejoices in them;
Those who merge with loss find loss rejoices in them.
*"Trust"* is insufficient—there is *"no trust."*

---

**Chapter on the Perils of Arrogance:**

The overreaching cannot stand,
The striding cannot walk,
The self-admiring cannot see clearly,
The self-righteous cannot shine,
The self-praising achieve no merit,
The self-proud do not endure.
In the Way, they are called *"excessive food, superfluous limbs."*
Things abhor them—
Thus those who follow the Dao do not dwell among them.

---

**Chapter on the Primordial Oneness:**

There exists a **Primordial Unity**,
Born before heaven and earth,
Silent, vast—
Independent, unchanging,
Circulating without exhaustion,
Capable of being the **Mother of All under heaven**.
I do not know its name—
I call it the **Dao**.
Forced to name it, I call it **"Great."**
Great means *"passing"*—
Passing means *"distant"*—
Distant means *"returning."*
Thus the Dao is Great,
Heaven is Great,
Earth is Great,
And the Sovereign is Great.
Within the realm, there are four Greats—
And the Sovereign holds one of them.

Humans model Earth,
Earth models Heaven,
Heaven models the Dao,
The Dao models **Naturalness**.

---

**Chapter on Lightness as the Root of Substance:**

Substance is the root of lightness,
Stillness governs agitation—
Thus the Sage, though traveling all day,
Never strays from his **carriage and baggage**.
Though adorned with splendor,
He dwells aloof—
How could one who rules a thousand chariots
Lightly cast aside the weight of all under heaven?
Lightness leads to losing one’s foundation,
Agitation leads to losing one’s master.

---
**Chapter on Knowing the Masculine:**

**Chapter on Knowing the Masculine:**

Know its **masculine** (雄),
Hold its **feminine** (雌),
And the world will be **a valley** (溪).
If the world is a valley,
His **virtue/power** (德) remains unerring,
And he returns to the state of **innocence** (婴儿).

Know its **bright** (白),
Hold its **dark** (黑),
And the world will be **transformed** (式).
If the world is transformed,
His **virtue/power** (德) will not falter,
And he returns to the **boundless** (无极).

Know its **glory** (荣),
Hold its **humiliation** (辱),
And the world will be **a natural plain** (谷).
If the world is a natural plain,
His **virtue/power** (德) will be complete,
And he returns to **Naturalness** (朴).

**Naturalness** (朴) dispersed becomes **vessels** (器),
The Sage uses it and becomes **officials and leaders** (官长).
Thus the great **mechanisms** (制) are not severed.

---

**Chapter on Knowing the Masculine (Additional Commentary):**

(71) Return to **innocence** (婴儿) is to return to **essence** (志).
In **innocence**, he is **simple and unknowing** (蠢然无而无知也).

(72) Revert to **the unborn** (未生),
Return to **the beginningless** (未始),
Align with the **Dao/Way** (道) as constant,
And return to the **boundless** (无极).

(73) **Virtue/power** (德) and **Dao/Way** (道) are **auxiliaries** (佑),
**Divine clarity** (神明) is **assistance** (助).
When **Dao/Way** (道) is complete and **virtue/power** (德) is complete,
Then all things attain **great purity and Naturalness** (大淳朴).

**Chapter on Taking the World:**

**Chapter on Taking the World:**

If one would take the world and act upon it,
I see that it cannot be done.
The world is a divine vessel—
It cannot be forced.

Those who force it ruin it;
Those who grasp it lose it.
Thus things sometimes move, sometimes follow,
Sometimes sigh, sometimes blow,
Sometimes grow strong, sometimes weak,
Sometimes falter, sometimes collapse.

Therefore, the Sage avoids excess,
Avoids extravagance,
Avoids grandeur.

---
*(74)* The world is what divine clarity creates,
What **Great Harmony** (太和) fulfills.
Divine clarity perceives it,
While the Sage’s wisdom and might cannot reach or control it.

*(75)* Excess is overdoing;
Extravagance is unbalanced;
Grandeur is overbearing.
Thus, they are discarded.

---

**Chapter on Fine Arms:**

Fine arms are an inauspicious tool.
Men detest them,
So those who follow the Way do not dwell upon them.

The gentleman, at home, values the left;
In war, values the right.
Arms are an inauspicious tool,
Not the tool of the gentleman.
Used only when unavoidable,
He holds to serenity as supreme,
Victory without pride.
To take pride in victory is to delight in killing.
He who delights in killing
Cannot achieve his aims in the world.

Auspicious matters favor the left;
Inauspicious matters favor the right.
The **Left General** takes the left,
The **Right General** takes the right—
This is to treat war as a funeral rite.
For the multitude slain, let there be mourning and weeping.
When victorious, treat it as a funeral rite.

---
*(76)* The gentleman is the ruler of the land.
To value the left is to honor life and growth.

---

**Chapter on Knowing People:**

To know others is wisdom;
To know oneself is enlightenment.
To overcome others is strength;
To overcome oneself is power.
To know contentment is wealth;
To persevere is resolve;
To remain steadfast is endurance;
To die without perishing is longevity.

---
*(77)* Not knowing others, one cannot act in the world;
Not acting in the world, one cannot engage with society.
Not knowing oneself, one cannot comprehend **Dao/Way**;
Not comprehending **Dao/Way**, one cannot foresee what is unseen.
Not overcoming others, one cannot rule;
Not ruling, one cannot be sovereign.
Not overcoming oneself, one cannot attain self-mastery;
Not attaining self-mastery, one cannot win others.
Not knowing contentment, one cannot know wealth;
Not knowing wealth, one cannot curb desire.
Not persevering, one cannot align with the **Way**;
Not aligning with the **Way**, one cannot find fulfillment.
Actions not in accord with nature—
One cannot achieve harmony;
Without harmony, one cannot long endure.
Not enduring, one cannot nurture **spirit-qi** (神精);
**Spirit-qi** not accumulated, one cannot attain longevity.

Thus, to establish oneself in the world,
To promote benefit and remove harm,
To interact with others and adapt—
Nothing surpasses knowing people.

To gather wisdom and preserve clarity,
To establish the state and nurture the people,
To embody the **Way’s** intent,
To grasp **Heaven’s** will—
Nothing is greater than self-knowledge.

To govern with authority,
To set laws and rites,
To implement measures and commands,
To rectify the realm,
To subject the feudal lords—
Nothing is more noble than overcoming others.

To uphold **Dao/Way** and **virtue/power**,
To align with divine clarity,
To follow **Heaven** and **Earth**,
To harmonize **yin** and **yang**,
In action and stillness, advance and retreat—
To subtly win the hearts of men—
Nothing is more exalted than self-mastery.

To govern the family and state,
To make the people content and joyful,
To dwell in propriety, reverence, and caution,
To be filial, kind, and law-abiding—
Nothing is higher than contentment.

To wander in divine clarity’s luminous realm,
Serene and undisturbed,
To attain honor, splendor, and grace—
Nothing is better than fulfillment.

To serve in office, attend to superiors,
To complete others’ works,
To follow in their footsteps,
To benefit the myriad people—
Nothing surpasses endurance.

What **Heaven** and **Earth** cherish,
What the living rely upon,
To dwell in it without satiety,
To rejoice in it without end—
When all blessings converge,
And none can rival its splendor—
Nothing is more beautiful than longevity.

---

**Chapter on Grasping the Great Image:**

Grasp the **Great Image**,
And the world will come to it.
Come to it without harm,
And it will be peaceful and vast.
Offer delight and bait,
And passing guests will stop.

When the **Way** emerges in speech,
It is bland, without flavor.
To gaze upon it, insufficient to see;
To listen, insufficient to hear;
To use it, never exhausted.

---
*(78)* The **Way** has no form,
Yet **Heaven** and **Earth** rely on it to generate.
The **Way** has no being,
Yet **yin** and **yang** rely on it to begin.
The **Way** has no law,
Yet the four seasons rely on it for their work.
The **Way** has no image,
Yet the myriad beings rely on it to move.

Thus, the **Great Law** has no law,
The **Great Image** has no image,
The **Great** has no limits to what it lacks,
The **Great** has no limits to what it possesses.
To act where there is no acting,
To negate where there is no negation—
Thus the **Way** achieves its purpose without doing,
And **virtue/power** governs without exertion.

What then is there to do?
Not lacking what is lacking,
Not negating what is negated—
The **Way** finds itself here,
And all things find themselves there.

---

*(79)* When one is about to **withdraw** it, one must first **fully expand** it;
When one is about to **weaken** it, one must first **fully strengthen** it;
When one is about to **abolish** it, one must first **fully promote** it;
When one is about to **take away** it, one must first **fully grant** it—
This is called the **subtle luminosity**.

The **soft and weak** overcome the **hard and strong**.
A fish cannot be lifted from the depths,
And the **state’s sharp tools** cannot be kept from the people.

*(80)* The **Dao/Way** that passes through **virtue/power** and **mystic luminosity**,
That **Heaven** and **Earth** transform through,
That **yin** and **yang** regulate—
The **real** returns to the **void**,
The **luminous** returns to **obscurity**,
The **flourishing** returns to **decay**,
The **expanded** returns to **relaxation**,
The **possessed** returns to **loss**,
The **alive** returns to **death**—
This is the nature of things and the **natural Way**.

Thus, the **advantage of reversal** and the **benefit of yielding**—
The **Way** governs **Heaven**,
**Heaven** governs the **sovereign**,
The **sovereign** governs the **ministers**,
The **ministers** govern the **people**,
And all **qi-bearing** kinds **preserve themselves in life**.

When **tigers and leopards** seek to grasp,
They **conceal** their claws;
When **jackals and wolves** prepare to devour,
Their **fangs** are not seen;
The **sage** abandons **intent** to follow the **Way**,
The **wise** turn against the **world** to follow the **people**.

**Loyal words** that are **displeasing to the ear** contain their **rectitude**,
And **wicked ministers** about to rise **submit** to their **lord**.

If one knows this and **applies** it,
Then between **Heaven** and **Earth**, within the **six directions**,
All shall be **blessed**.
If one does not know this and **applies** it,
Then even within the **inner chambers**, among **bone and flesh**,
All shall be **thieves**.

Thus, **children** and **brothers** may at times be **jackals and wolves**,
And **enemies** and **foes** may at times be **father and elder brother**.
Yet within **affirmation** lies **negation**,
And within **negation** lies **affirmation**—
**One negation, one affirmation**,
And **some perish while others survive**.

Thus, unless it is **loyalty**,
Even **kin** cannot be trusted;
Unless it is **goodness**,
Even the **near** cannot be **loved**.
